Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
6 min
Testimony of a Naiha (Professional Mourner)
Ruling on testimony of professional female mourners

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a professional mourner, distinguish it from natural crying, and identify the proof from hadith.

Core Idea
Professional wailing nullifies 'adalah and rejects testimony; natural crying does not.

This lesson examines the distinction between natural crying over a deceased and professional wailing for hire. The Hanafi school considers professional wailing a major sin that destroys a person's 'adalah (moral integrity), thereby rendering their testimony unacceptable. We will explore the evidence from the hadith that supports this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the specific act being discussed (professional wailing vs natural crying) and the corresponding hukm (haram for professional wailing; permissible for natural crying).
The word 'naiha' refers only to a professional wailer, not any crying woman.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
Contrast the two cases: a woman who cries naturally due to genuine grief vs one who wails loudly for hire without genuine sorrow.
Natural crying does not affect 'adalah; professional wailing nullifies it.
3
Locate the proof
Identify the hadith cited: 'The Messenger of Allah cursed the wailing woman and the one who listens to her.' (Abu Dawud, Muslim).
The curse indicates the act is a major sin (kabirah).
4
Apply the Hanafi principle
Link the hadith to the ruling: persistent commission of a major sin without repentance makes a person fasiq, and a fasiq's testimony is rejected in Hanafi law.
Repentance restores 'adalah and the right to testify.
5
Note the practical consequence
Understand that the testimony of a professional mourner is rejected until she repents, while the testimony of a natural crier is accepted.
This ruling is based on Zahir al-Riwayah and is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نائكة : غم اور مصیبت کی وجہ سے فطری طور پر روئے تو اس سے عدالت ساقط نہیں ہوتی ، اس کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔ یہاں نائکہ سے مراد وہ عورتیں ہیں جو پیشہ ور رونے والی ہو کہ غم وغیرہ کچھ نہیں ہے۔ کرایہ پر نوحہ خوانی کرتی ہیں۔ ایسی نوحہ خوانی گناہ کبیرہ ہے۔ اس لئے ان کی عدالت ساقط ہو جائے گی ۔ اور گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی۔ نوحہ حرام ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے۔ عن ابي سعيد الخدري قال لعن رسول الله الله النائحة والمستمعة (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی النوح، ج ۲، ص۱۷۴ نمبر ۳۱۲۸ / مسلم شریف ، باب التشديد فى النياحة بص ۳۰۳، نمبر ۹۳۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نوحہ گناہ کبیرہ ہے اس لئے نوحہ کرنے والیوں کی گواہی مقبول نہیں جب تک کہ اس سے تو بہ نہ ہو۔
A naiha (female mourner): if she cries naturally due to grief and calamity, her 'adalah does not fall, and her testimony is accepted. Here, 'naiha' refers to women who are professional wailers, who have no actual grief but perform lamentation for hire. Such lamentation is a major sin. Therefore, their 'adalah will be nullified and their testimony will not be accepted. The evidence that wailing is prohibited is the hadith: Abu Sa'id al-Khudri reported: 'The Messenger of Allah cursed the wailing woman and the one who listens to her.' (Abu Dawud, Muslim). From this hadith, it is understood that wailing (al-niyahah) is a major sin. Hence, the testimony of wailing women is not accepted unless they repent.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between natural crying due to genuine grief and professional wailing (al-niyahah). Natural crying does not affect 'adalah, so the testimony of such a woman is accepted. However, a professional mourner who wails for hire commits a major sin because she pretends grief and engages in prohibited vocalization. The hadith of the Prophet cursing both the wailer and the listener establishes the prohibition. Therefore, such a woman is a fasiq, and her testimony is rejected until she repents. This ruling is based on the consensus that wailing is haram (major sin) and the Hanafi principle that persistence in major sins without repentance disqualifies a witness.

Key Terms
نائحة (naiha): A professional female mourner who wails loudly for hire, often without genuine grief.
نوحہ (niyahah): Lamentation or wailing that involves raising the voice and feigning grief.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the testimony of a professional mourner (naiha) rejected in the Hanafi school?
A) Because she is a woman.
B) Because wailing for hire is a major sin and makes her fasiq.
C) Because she is not a free person.
D) Because she lacks intelligence.

Key Takeaway
The testimony of a professional mourner is rejected because her wailing is a major sin that nullifies her 'adalah; natural crying due to genuine grief does not affect testimony.

Testimony of a Professional Singer (Mughanniya)
Ruling on testimony: occasional vs. professional female singer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between occasional and professional singing regarding 'adalah and state the Hanafi ruling with its evidence.

Core Idea
Professional singing is a major sin that disqualifies testimony; occasional singing does not.

In this lesson, we examine a classical Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a female singer (mughanniya). The key is the distinction between casual, occasional singing and making singing a profession. The Hanafi school, drawing on Quran and Hadith, holds that professional singing is a major sin (kabirah) that nullifies judicial credibility ('adalah), while occasional singing does not. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly assessing witness eligibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the testimony of a mughanniya. The ruling is that it is rejected if she is a professional, but accepted if she sings only occasionally.
The definition of mughanniya here is key: one who makes singing her trade and invites to singing and dancing.
2
Locate the distinction
The passage explicitly separates occasional singing from professional singing. Occasional singing does not affect 'adalah; professional singing does.
The distinction is based on the gravity of the sin: occasional is minor (saghirah) while professional is major (kabirah).
3
Examine the proofs
The author cites three proofs: Quran 31:6 interpreted by Ibn Mas'ud as referring to singing, a hadith that singing breeds hypocrisy, and another hadith forbidding two foolish sounds including 'rannat al-shaitan' (singing).
These proofs establish that professional singing is haram and a major sin.
4
Understand the legal consequence
A professional singer is a fasiq (sinner) whose 'adalah is vitiated, so her testimony is rejected. Occasional singing does not make one a fasiq.
The consequence is practical: testimony is accepted from occasional singers, rejected from professionals.
5
Recognize cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school may consider singing generally permissible under certain conditions, leading to acceptance of testimony from singers. This is a legitimate ikhtilaf.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is directly on the admissibility of testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مغنیہ : کبھی کبھار گیت گالی یا شعر کہ لیا اس سے عدالت ساقط نہیں ہوگی ۔ یہاں مغنیہ سے مراد ہے جو گانے کا پیشہ بنالیا ہو۔ اور ناچ گانے کی دعوت دیتی ہو۔ اس کی عدالت ساقط ہوگی کیونکہ ایسا گانا گناہ کبیرہ ہے۔ وجہ آیت میں ہے۔ ومن الناس من يشترى لهو الحديث ليضل عن سبيل الله بغير علم ويتخذها هزوا اولئك لهم عذاب مهين ( آیت ۶ ، سورۃ لقمان (۳۱) اس آیت کی تفسیر میں حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود کا قول ہے۔ ھو او الله الغناء (سنن للبیہقی ، باب الرجل یعنی فيتخذ الغناء صناعتہ ہوتی علیہ دیا تی له و یکون منسوباالیه مشهورا به معروفا اوالمرأة ، ج عاشر ص ۳۷۷ نمبر ۲۱۰۰۳) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ گانا حرام ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن مسعود قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الغناء ينبت النفاق في القلب كما ينبت الماء البقل (سن للبیہقی ، باب الرجل يغني فيتخذ الغناء ضاعتہ یو تی علیه ویا تی ال الخ، ج عاشر ص ۳۷۸ نمبر ۲۱۰۰۸ ر ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی کراہیتہ الغناء، ص نمبر ۴۹۲۷) (۳) ترمذی شریف میں ہے۔عن جابر بن عبد الله قال عبد الرحمن بن عوف ... ولكن عن صوتين احمقين فاجرين صوت عند مصيبة خمش وجوه وشق جيوب ورنة شيطان (ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرخصة في البكاء على الميت ص ۱۹۵ نمبر ۱۰۰۵) اس حدیث میں رستہ الشیطان سے مراد گانا گانا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ گناہ کبیرہ ہے۔ اس کا پیشہ بنانے سے گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔
A mughanniya (female singer): if she occasionally sings a song or recites a poem, her 'adalah does not fall. Here, 'mughanniya' refers to one who has made singing her profession and invites to singing and dancing. Her 'adalah will fall because such singing is a major sin. The evidence is in the verse: 'And of the people is he who buys the amusement of speech (lahw al-hadith) to mislead [others] from the way of Allah without knowledge and who takes it in ridicule. Those will have a humiliating punishment' (Quran 31:6). In its tafsir, Ibn Mas'ud said: 'By Allah, it is singing (al-ghina')' (Bayhaqi). From this verse, it is understood that singing is prohibited. (2) In a hadith: Ibn Mas'ud reported: 'The Prophet said: Singing causes hypocrisy to grow in the heart as water causes vegetation to grow' (Bayhaqi, Abu Dawud). (3) In Tirmidhi: Jabir reported from Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf: '...but I have been forbidden from two foolish, immoral sounds: a sound at the time of calamity (scratching faces, tearing collars), and a sound of Shaitan (rannat al-shaitan).' In this hadith, 'rannat al-shaitan' refers to singing. Therefore, this is a major sin. If one makes it a profession, his testimony will not be accepted.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage addresses the testimony of a female singer (mughanniya). The author distinguishes between occasional singing (e.g., reciting poetry or singing a song on rare occasions) and professional singing. Occasional singing does not affect 'adalah. However, making singing a profession, especially where one invites others to singing and dancing, constitutes a major sin (kabirah). The proofs include: (1) Quran 31:6, interpreted by Ibn Mas'ud as referring to singing; (2) the hadith that singing fosters hypocrisy; (3) the hadith listing two foolish sounds, where 'rannat al-shaitan' (the sound of Shaitan) is interpreted as singing. Based on these, the Hanafi school considers professional singing (al-ghina' as a craft) to be haram and a major sin. Therefore, a professional singer is a fasiq, and her testimony is rejected unless she repents and gives up the profession.

Key Terms
مغنیہ (mughanniya): A female professional singer who makes singing her trade and invites to singing and dancing.
لهو الحديث (lahw al-hadith): Amusing or distracting speech; interpreted as singing.
عدالت (adalah): Judicial credibility; the moral uprightness required of a witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the testimony of a woman who occasionally sings a song for entertainment (not as a profession)?
A) Her testimony is rejected because any singing is a major sin.
B) Her testimony is accepted because occasional singing does not nullify 'adalah.
C) Her testimony is accepted only if she is married.
D) Her testimony is rejected unless she repents immediately after singing.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects the testimony of a professional singer because singing as a profession is a major sin, but occasional singing does not impair 'adalah.

Testimony of a Habitual Drinker and Its Acceptance Upon Repentance
Ruling on testimony of habitual drinker and its acceptance upon repentance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a habitual drinker and explain why sincere repentance immediately restores its acceptability.

Core Idea
A habitual drinker's testimony is rejected because drinking is a major sin and removes 'adalah; sincere repentance immediately restores it.

In this lesson, we examine the case of the mudmin al-shurb — one who habitually drinks wine without intention to repent. The Hanafi school rules that his testimony is rejected due to his fisq. However, upon sincere repentance, his testimony becomes accepted immediately, as demonstrated by an athar of Umar ibn al-Khattab. This lesson will walk through the evidence from Quran, hadith, and the practice of the Sahaba.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is habitual drinking (mudmin al-shurb). The ruling is that drinking wine is haram and a major sin, which disqualifies the person from being a credible witness.
The ruling is derived from Quran and hadith.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Quran 5:90 explicitly prohibits intoxicants. The imperative 'fajtanibuhu' (avoid it) is a clear command, indicating that drinking is haram and a major sin.
The hadith from Bukhari further emphasizes that the drinker does not remain a believer at the time of drinking.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition implies that the drinker commits a major sin, which makes him a fasiq. A fasiq cannot be 'adl (upright), and thus his testimony is rejected.
This is based on the principle that 'adalah is a condition for testimony.
4
Note the exception upon repentance
If the drinker repents sincerely (tawbah), his 'adalah is restored. The athar of Umar ibn al-Khattab demonstrates immediate acceptance of testimony after repentance, with no waiting period.
Repentance requires abandoning the sin, feeling remorse, and resolving not to return.
5
Apply the ruling
For a mudmin al-shurb who has not repented, his testimony is rejected. For one who has sincerely repented, his testimony is accepted immediately.
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مد من الشرب : جو شراب پیتا ہو اور توبہ کرنے کی نیت نہ ہو اس کو مدمن الشرب شراب میں دھت کہتے ہیں۔ شراب پینا گناہ کبیرہ ہے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ انما الخمر والميسر والانصاب والازلام رجس من عمل الشيطان فاجتنبوا لعلكم تفلحون ( آیت ۹۰ ، سورة المائدة (۵) اس آیت میں شراب پینا حرام قرار دیا گیا ہے (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة أن رسول الله الله قال لايزني الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن ولا يشرب الخمر حين يشرب وهو مؤمن ( بخاری شریف، باب الزنا وشرب الخمر ص ۱۰۰۱ نمبر ۶۷۷۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شراب پینے سے مؤمن باقی نہیں رہتا۔ اس لئے اس کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ اگر شراب پینے سے توبہ کرلے تو اس کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال كنت مع عمر بن الخطاب في حج ... فامر الناس ان يجالسوه ويوا كلوه وان تاب فاقبلوا شهادته و حمله و اعطاه مأتی درهم فاخبر عمران شهادته تسقط بشرب الخمر وانه اذا تاب حينئذ تقبل شهادته (سن للبیہقی ، باب شهادة اہل الاشربہ، ج عاشر ص ۱۳۶۲، نمبر ۲۰۹۴۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ شراب پینے سے تو بہ کرے تو اس کی گواہی قبول کرو۔
A habitual drinker (mudmin al-shurb): he who drinks wine and has no intention to repent is called a mudmin al-shurb (addicted to drink). Drinking wine is a major sin. Its evidence is the verse: 'O you who have believed, indeed, intoxicants, gambling, [sacrificing on] stone alters [to other than Allah], and divining arrows are but defilement from the work of Satan, so avoid it that you may be successful' (Quran 5:90). This verse declares drinking wine to be prohibited. (1) In a hadith: Abu Hurairah reported: 'The Messenger of Allah said: The adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer, nor does the drinker drink wine while he is a believer.' (Bukhari). From this hadith, it is understood that the drinker does not remain a believer. Therefore, his testimony is not accepted. If he repents from drinking wine, then his testimony will be accepted. In an athar (tradition): Ibn Umar said: 'I was with Umar ibn al-Khattab during Hajj... He ordered the people to sit with him and eat with him, and if he repents, accept his testimony, and he gave him two hundred dirhams. Umar informed that his testimony is dropped due to drinking wine, and if he repents, then his testimony is accepted.' (Bayhaqi). In this athar, it says that if he repents from drinking, accept his testimony.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage concludes the section on disqualified witnesses by addressing the habitual wine drinker (mudmin al-shurb). It defines him as one who drinks wine without intending to repent. Drinking is a major sin, proven by Quran 5:90 (prohibition of khamr) and the hadith that the drinker does not remain a believer at the time of drinking. Therefore, such a person is a fasiq and his testimony is rejected. However, if he sincerely repents (tawbah), his 'adalah is restored and his testimony becomes acceptable. The athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab illustrates this: Umar ordered that a repentant drinker be associated with, eat with, and his testimony be accepted. This shows that repentance removes the disqualification. The Hanafi school holds that tawbah from a major sin, with the conditions of abandoning the sin, remorse, and resolve not to return, restores 'adalah. Note that the text does not specify a period of probation; immediate testimony is accepted after repentance, as indicated by the athar.

Key Terms
مدمن الشرب (mudmin al-shurb): One who habitually drinks wine with no intention to repent.
توبہ (tawbah): Repentance: abandoning the sin, feeling remorse, and resolving not to return to it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is the testimony of a habitual drinker accepted?
A) Never, even if he repents.
B) After he has abstained from drinking for one year.
C) Immediately after he repents sincerely.
D) After he has been publicly flogged.

Key Takeaway
A habitual drinker's testimony is rejected due to fisq, but sincere repentance immediately restores his 'adalah and renders his testimony acceptable.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
10 min
Professional Singing and Habitual Drinking Nullify 'Adalah
Testimony of professional singer and habitual drinker rejected

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a professional singer and a habitual drinker, and identify the Quranic and hadith proofs that establish their loss of moral probity.

Core Idea
Persistent major sins like professional singing and drinking permanently void 'adalah until repentance.

This lesson unpacks two categories of witnesses whose testimony is rejected in Hanafi fiqh: the professional singer (mugniyah) and the habitual drinker (mudmin al-shurb). The commentary distinguishes occasional acts from persistent professions, and emphasizes that repentance can restore moral probity. You will study the textual proofs from Quran and Sunnah that establish these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the Arabic text and note the two categories: mugniyah (professional singer) and mudmin al-shurb (habitual drinker). Understand the distinction between occasional and persistent commission.
The text explicitly says occasional singing does not nullify 'adalah; only making it a profession does.
2
Locate the primary proof for singing
Examine the Quranic verse (Luqman 31:6) and the interpretation by Ibn Mas'ud that 'lahw al-hadith' means singing. Then study the hadith about singing breeding hypocrisy.
The dalala of the verse is zanni because of the interpretative link, but the hadith provides direct support.
3
Locate the proof for drinking
Find the Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:90) prohibiting intoxicants and the hadith that the drinker is not a believer at the time of drinking. Note the athar from Umar showing that repentance restores testimony.
The imperative 'fajtanibuh' gives qat'i dalala for prohibition.
4
Apply the principle
Conclude that persistent commission of a kabira without repentance destroys 'adalah. The testimony of such persons is rejected unless they repent and reform.
Repentance is a condition for restoration of 'adalah.

حضرت عبداللہ بن مسعود کا قول ہے۔ ھو والله الغناء (الف) (سنن للبیہقی ، باب الرجل يعني فيتخذ الغناء صناعتہ ہوتی علیہ دیا تی له و یکون منسوبااليه مشهورا به معروفا اوالمرأة ، ج عاشر ص ۳۷۷ نمبر ۲۱۰۰۳) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ گانا حرام ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن مسعود قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم الغناء ينبت النفاق في القلب كما ينبت الماء البقل (ب) (سن للبیہقی ، باب الرجل يغني فيتخذ الغناء ضاعتہ یو تی علیه ویا تی ال الخ، ج عاشر ص ۳۷۸ نمبر ۲۱۰۰۸ ر ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی کراہیتہ الغناء، ص نمبر ۴۹۲۷) (۳) ترمذی شریف میں ہے۔عن جابر بن عبد الله قال عبد الرحمن بن عوف ... ولكن عن صوتين احمقين فاجرين صوت عند مصيبة خمش وجوه وشق جيوب ورنة شيطان (ج) ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الرخصة في البكاء على الميت ص ۱۹۵ نمبر ۱۰۰۵) اس حدیث میں رستہ الشیطان سے مراد گانا گانا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ گناہ کبیرہ ہے۔ اس کا پیشہ بنانے سے گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ مدمن الشرب : جو شراب پیتا ہو اور توبہ کرنے کی نیت نہ ہو اس کو مدمن الشرب شراب میں دھت کہتے ہیں۔ شراب پینا گناہ کبیرہ ہے اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ انما الخمر والميسر والانصاب والازلام رجس من عمل الشيطان فاجتنبوا لعلكم تفلحون (1) ( آیت ۹۰ ، سورة المائدة (۵) اس آیت میں شراب پینا حرام قرار دیا گیا ہے (۱) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة أن رسول الله الله قال لايزني الزاني حين يزني وهو مؤمن ولا يشرب الخمر حين يشرب وهو مؤمن (ه) ( بخاری شریف، باب الزنا وشرب الخمر ص ۱۰۰۱ نمبر ۶۷۷۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ شراب پینے سے مؤمن باقی نہیں رہتا۔ اس لئے اس کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ اگر شراب پینے سے توبہ کرلے تو اس کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال كنت مع عمر بن الخطاب في حج ... فامر الناس ان يجالسوه ويواكلوه وان تاب فاقبلوا شهادته و حمله و اعطاه مأتی درهم فاخبر عمران شهادته تسقط بشرب الخمر وانه اذا تاب حينئذ تقبل شهادته (و) (سن للبیہقی ، باب شهادة اہل الاشربہ، ج عاشر ص ۱۳۶۲، نمبر ۲۰۹۴۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ شراب پینے سے تو بہ کرے تو اس کی گواہی قابل قبول ہوگی۔ [۱۲۸۳۲ (۲۳) ولا من يُغَنِى للناس ولا من يأتى بابا من الكبائر التي يتعلق بها الحد ولا من يلعب بالطور ولا يدخل الحمام بغير ازار] لامن يلعب بالطور : پرندوں کو سکھانے اور کھلانے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔ اس سے عدالت ساقط نہیں ہوگی۔ یہاں مراد ہے کہ پرندے کے ذریعہ سے بازی لگاتا ہے۔ اس لئے یہ ایک قسم کا جوا ہے۔ اور اوپر آیت میں گزرا کہ جو احرام ہے۔ يـا ايها الذين آمنوا انما الخمر والميسر والانصاب والازلام رجس من عمل الشيطان فاجتنبوه لعلكم تفلحون (الف) ( آیت ۹۰، سورۃ المائدۃ ۵) اس آیت میں میسر اور از لام سے مراد جوا ہے جو حرام ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان نبي الله له نهي عن الخمر والميسر والكوبة والغبيراء (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما جاء فی السکر ص ۱۶۲، نمبر ۳۶۸۵) اس حدیث میں المیسر یعنی جو احرام قرار دیا۔ اس لئے پرندے کے ذریعہ جو جوا کھیلتا ہے اس کی گواہی قبول نہیں ہے۔ اصول یہ مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ مسلسل گناہ کبیرہ کرنے کی وجہ سے عدات ساقط ہو گئی۔ اور آیت مذکورہ کے اعتبار سے غیر عادل کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ان لوگوں کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی۔ لا یدخل الحمام بغیر ازار : اگر غسل خانہ بند ہو اور ایک آدمی نگا غسل کرے تو اس سے عدالت ساقط نہیں ہوتی۔ لیکن ایسا غسل خانہ ہو جس میں دوسرے لوگ داخل ہوتے ہیں تو ازار کے بغیر داخل ہونا حرام ہے اور اس کی گواہی رد کی جائے گی۔
The Samari Commentary Volume Four, Book of Testimonies. Singer: Sometimes he sings a song or recites a poem occasionally; his moral probity is not nullified. Here, the singer means one who makes singing a profession and invites to dancing and singing. His moral probity is nullified because such singing is a major sin. The evidence is in the verse: 'And of the people is he who buys the amusement of speech to mislead [others] from the way of Allah without knowledge and who takes it in ridicule. Those will have a humiliating punishment' (Surah Luqman, 31:6). In interpretation of this verse, 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud said: 'It is, by Allah, singing.' (Narrated by Bayhaqi). From this verse it is understood that singing is prohibited. (2) Hadith: From 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, the Prophet said: 'Singing causes hypocrisy to grow in the heart just as water causes vegetation to grow.' (Narrated by Bayhaqi and Abu Dawud). (3) In Tirmidhi: From Jabir that 'Abd al-Rahman ibn 'Awf... but about two foolish and sinful voices: a voice at a time of calamity with scratching of faces, tearing of collars, and the howl of Satan. In this hadith, 'howl of Satan' means singing. Therefore it is a major sin. Making it a profession, testimony is not accepted. Habitual drinker: One who drinks wine and has no intention to repent is called a habitual drunkard. Drinking wine is a major sin; its evidence is the verse: 'O you who have believed, indeed, intoxicants, gambling, [sacrificing on] stone alters [to other than Allah], and divining arrows are but defilement from the work of Satan, so avoid it that you may be successful.' (Surah al-Ma'idah, 5:90). This verse declares drinking wine prohibited. (1) Hadith: From Abu Hurairah that the Prophet said: 'The adulterer does not commit adultery while he is a believer, and the drinker does not drink wine while he is a believer.' (Narrated by Bukhari). This hadith shows that drinking wine removes one from faith. Therefore his testimony is not accepted. If he repents from drinking, his testimony will be accepted. Athar: From Ibn 'Umar: 'I was with 'Umar ibn al-Khattab on Hajj... he commanded the people to sit with him, eat with him, and if he repents, accept his testimony, and he gave him a mount and two hundred dirhams.' 'Umar informed that his testimony is nullified by drinking wine, and when he repents, his testimony is accepted. (Narrated by Bayhaqi). So if he repents from drinking, his testimony becomes acceptable. [12832 (23)] And not the testimony of one who sings for people, nor one who commits a major sin to which a prescribed punishment (hadd) applies, nor one who plays with birds, nor one who enters the bathhouse without a waist-wrapper. Explanation of 'one who plays with birds': Teaching and feeding birds is not objectionable; it does not nullify moral probity. Here it means he bets through birds. Therefore it is a type of gambling. The verse mentioned earlier that gambling is prohibited. 'O you who have believed, indeed, intoxicants, gambling, [sacrificing on] stone alters [to other than Allah], and divining arrows are but defilement from the work of Satan, so avoid it that you may be successful.' (Surah al-Ma'idah, 5:90). In this verse, 'gambling' is prohibited. (2) Hadith: From 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar that the Prophet forbade wine, gambling, the drum, and fermented grain drink. (Narrated by Abu Dawud). So playing with birds for betting is prohibited. The principle of these issues is that due to persistent commission of major sins, moral probity is nullified. And according to the mentioned verse, the testimony of a morally corrupt person is not accepted. Therefore their testimony is not accepted. 'One who enters the bathhouse without a waist-wrapper': If the bathhouse is private and one person bathes alone, it does not nullify moral probity. But if it is a bathhouse where other people enter, entering without a waist-wrapper is prohibited, and his testimony will be rejected.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a matn from the Book of Testimonies (Kitab al-Shahadat), explaining which categories of witnesses are rejected due to loss of 'adalah (moral probity). The commentary addresses four types: 1) Professional singer (mugniyah): The text distinguishes between occasional singing (which does not disqualify) and making singing a profession involving invitation to dance and song, which is a major sin (kabira) and thus nullifies 'adalah. The proof is the Quranic verse (Luqman 31:6) interpreted by Ibn Mas'ud as referring to singing, and hadiths stating that singing breeds hypocrisy. 2) Habitual drinker (mudmin al-shurb): One who drinks alcohol persistently without intention to repent loses 'adalah. The Quran (al-Ma'idah 5:90) prohibits alcohol, and hadith says the drinker is not a believer at the time of drinking. The commentary includes an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab showing that repentance restores testimony. 3) Bird gambler (al-la'ib bi'l-tur): Using birds for betting is a form of gambling (maysir), prohibited in the same Quranic verse and hadith. Teaching or feeding birds without betting is permissible. 4) One who enters the bathhouse (hamam) without an izar (waist-wrapper): If the bathhouse is private, it is not a sin; but if it is public, it becomes a major sin (exposure of 'awrah) and disqualifies testimony. The overarching principle is that persistent commission of major sins (kaba'ir) removes 'adalah, and Allah's command in the verse (al-Hujurat 49:6) to verify news from a corrupt person extends to rejecting their testimony. The Hanafi position is clear: such witnesses are rejected unless they repent and reform.

Key Terms
مغنیہ (mugniyah): One who makes singing a profession and invites to dancing and singing; not the occasional singer.
مدمن الشرب (mudmin al-shurb): One who habitually drinks alcohol and has no intention to repent.
عدالت ('adalah): Moral probity required for a witness; based on avoiding major sins and not persisting in minor sins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the minimum condition for the testimony of a habitual drinker to be accepted?
A) He must never have drunk alcohol.
B) He must repent and reform.
C) He must drink only occasionally.
D) He must not drink in public.

Key Takeaway
Persistent major sins like professional singing and habitual drinking void 'adalah, but sincere repentance restores it.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Gambling with Birds and Public Indecency Nullify 'Adalah
Testimony of bird gambler and bathhouse entrant rejected

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why gambling with birds and entering a public bathhouse without a waist-wrapper are major sins that nullify 'adalah, and identify the Quranic and hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Using birds for betting is gambling, and public exposure of 'awrah are both major sins that destroy moral probity.

This lesson covers two additional categories of rejected witnesses: the bird gambler (al-la'ib bi'l-tur) and the one who enters the bathhouse without a waist-wrapper (dukhul al-hamam bi-ghayr izar). The commentary clarifies that teaching/feeding birds is fine, but betting on bird games is a form of maysir (gambling). Entering a public bathhouse naked is exposing 'awrah, a major sin. Both nullify 'adalah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories
Read the Arabic for 'la'ib bi'l-tur' and 'dukhul al-hamam bi-ghayr izar'. Note the distinction between permissible activities (teaching/feeding) and forbidden (betting).
The text explicitly says teaching/feeding birds does not nullify 'adalah; only betting does.
2
Locate the proof for gambling
The Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:90) forbids maysir (gambling). The hadith from Ibn 'Umar prohibits gambling and includes the drum (kubah) as an instrument of gambling.
The imperative 'fajtanibuh' is qat'i in dalala.
3
Locate the proof for public indecency
The text does not cite a specific proof for the bathhouse rule but relies on the general principle that exposing 'awrah without necessity is a major sin. The commentary implies it is a kabira by linking it to the rule that persistent kabira nullifies 'adalah.
The ruling is derived from the general prohibition of uncovering 'awrah (Quran 24:31).
4
Apply the principle
Conclude that both activities are major sins when done persistently or deliberately, thus the 'adalah of the witness is nullified until repentance.
Repentance restores testimony for both.

Athar: From Ibn 'Umar: 'I was with 'Umar ibn al-Khattab on Hajj... he commanded the people to sit with him, eat with him, and if he repents, accept his testimony, and he gave him a mount and two hundred dirhams.' 'Umar informed that his testimony is nullified by drinking wine, and when he repents, his testimony is accepted. (Narrated by Bayhaqi). So if he repents from drinking, his testimony becomes acceptable. [12832 (23)] And not the testimony of one who sings for people, nor one who commits a major sin to which a prescribed punishment (hadd) applies, nor one who plays with birds, nor one who enters the bathhouse without a waist-wrapper. Explanation of 'one who plays with birds': Teaching and feeding birds is not objectionable; it does not nullify moral probity. Here it means he bets through birds. Therefore it is a type of gambling. The verse mentioned earlier that gambling is prohibited. 'O you who have believed, indeed, intoxicants, gambling, [sacrificing on] stone alters [to other than Allah], and divining arrows are but defilement from the work of Satan, so avoid it that you may be successful.' (Surah al-Ma'idah, 5:90). In this verse, 'gambling' is prohibited. (2) Hadith: From 'Abdullah ibn 'Umar that the Prophet forbade wine, gambling, the drum, and fermented grain drink. (Narrated by Abu Dawud). So playing with birds for betting is prohibited. The principle of these issues is that due to persistent commission of major sins, moral probity is nullified. And according to the mentioned verse, the testimony of a morally corrupt person is not accepted. Therefore their testimony is not accepted. 'One who enters the bathhouse without a waist-wrapper': If the bathhouse is private and one person bathes alone, it does not nullify moral probity. But if it is a bathhouse where other people enter, entering without a waist-wrapper is prohibited, and his testimony will be rejected.
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of a matn from the Book of Testimonies (Kitab al-Shahadat), explaining which categories of witnesses are rejected due to loss of 'adalah (moral probity). The commentary addresses four types: 1) Professional singer (mugniyah): The text distinguishes between occasional singing (which does not disqualify) and making singing a profession involving invitation to dance and song, which is a major sin (kabira) and thus nullifies 'adalah. The proof is the Quranic verse (Luqman 31:6) interpreted by Ibn Mas'ud as referring to singing, and hadiths stating that singing breeds hypocrisy. 2) Habitual drinker (mudmin al-shurb): One who drinks alcohol persistently without intention to repent loses 'adalah. The Quran (al-Ma'idah 5:90) prohibits alcohol, and hadith says the drinker is not a believer at the time of drinking. The commentary includes an athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab showing that repentance restores testimony. 3) Bird gambler (al-la'ib bi'l-tur): Using birds for betting is a form of gambling (maysir), prohibited in the same Quranic verse and hadith. Teaching or feeding birds without betting is permissible. 4) One who enters the bathhouse (hamam) without an izar (waist-wrapper): If the bathhouse is private, it is not a sin; but if it is public, it becomes a major sin (exposure of 'awrah) and disqualifies testimony. The overarching principle is that persistent commission of major sins (kaba'ir) removes 'adalah, and Allah's command in the verse (al-Hujurat 49:6) to verify news from a corrupt person extends to rejecting their testimony. The Hanafi position is clear: such witnesses are rejected unless they repent and reform.

Key Terms
يلعب بالطور (yal'abu bi'l-tur): Playing with birds specifically for betting (gambling).
الحمام بغير ازار (al-hamam bi-ghayr izar): Entering a public bathhouse without a waist-wrapper.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the essential element that makes playing with birds a major sin according to the text?
A) Using birds for racing.
B) Betting on the birds.
C) Training birds excessively.
D) Keeping many birds.

Key Takeaway
Gambling and public indecency are major sins that nullify 'adalah, but permissible activities like feeding birds or private bathing do not.

Entering Bathhouse Without Waist-wrapper Invalidates Testimony
Ruling-with-proof: public nudity destroys 'adalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state why public nudity in a bathhouse invalidates 'adalah and explain the Quranic and hadith proofs for this ruling.

Core Idea
Public nudity is a major sin that destroys moral integrity, making testimony invalid.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from Hanafi fiqh: a person who enters a bathhouse (or public swimming area) completely naked before others commits a grave sin that strips him of moral integrity ('adalah). Consequently, his testimony in court is no longer accepted. The author supports this with the Quranic command to take adornment at every mosque and with two hadith prohibiting nudity in sacred contexts. We will trace the reasoning from act to legal consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is the act being discussed? (Entering a bathhouse without any covering over the 'awrah in front of others.) What is the ruling? (Haram, and it invalidates 'adalah.)
Focus on the consequence: loss of moral integrity.
2
Locate the dalil
What evidence does the author cite? The Quranic verse 7:31 (command to take adornment at every mosque) and two hadith from Bukhari prohibiting nudity.
These proofs establish that uncovering the 'awrah is a major sin.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the verse prove the prohibition? The command to 'take adornment' is interpreted as obligating covering of the 'awrah, especially during prayer; uncovering it is thus prohibited.
The hadith explicitly forbid circumambulating the Ka'bah naked and wrapping in a single cloth without covering the private parts.
4
Note the consequence
Why does this act invalidate testimony? Because it is a major sin (kabirah), and committing major sins destroys 'adalah (moral integrity), which is a condition for acceptable testimony.
The passage emphasizes that the sin is committed by exposing the 'awrah in front of the general public.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يدخل الحمام بغير ازار [۲۸۳۳] (۲۴) بہت سے لوگ ایک ساتھ نہاتے ہوں۔ جیسے انگلینڈ میں سوئمنگ پول ہوتا ہے جس کو تمام کہتے ہیں۔ اس میں بالکل ننگا داخل ہو تو چونکہ بغیر ستر کے سب کے سامنے داخل ہوا، اور سب کے سامنے ستر کھولنا حرام ہے اس لئے اس گناہ کبیرہ کی وجہ سے عدالت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ ستر کھولنے کی حرمت اس آیت میں ہے۔ يبني آدم خذوا زينتكم عند كل مسجد (الف) ( آیت ۳۱ ،سورۃ الاعراف ۷ ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ نماز کے وقت زینت اختیار کر د یعنی کپڑا پہنو (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ ثم اردف رسول الله الله عليا فامره ان يوذن ببراءة قال ابو هريرة فاذن معنا على فى اهل منى يوم النحر ، لا يحج بعد العام مشرك ولا يطوف بالبيت عریان (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب مایستر من العورة ، ص ۵۳ ، نمبر ۳۶۹) اس حدیث میں ننگا رہنے سے منع فرمایا (۳) ایک اور حدیث ہے۔ عن ابی سعيد الخدري انه قال نهى رسول الله الا الله عن اشتمال الصماء، وان يحتبى الرجل في ثوب واحد ليس على فرجه منه شيء (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب مایستر من العورة ، ص ۵۳، نمبر ۳۶۷) اس حدیث میں بھی ستر کھولنے سے منع فرمایا۔ اس لئے عام لوگوں کے سامنے غسل خانہ میں ستر کھولنے سے عدالت ساقط ہو جائے گی۔ اور اس کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی۔
He enters the bathhouse without a waist-wrapper. (2833) (24) Many people bathe together. For example, there is a swimming pool in England called 'tamam'. If one enters it completely naked, then since he entered without covering the 'awrah before everyone, and uncovering the 'awrah before everyone is forbidden, therefore due to this major sin, his 'adalah will be invalidated. The prohibition of uncovering the 'awrah is in this verse: 'O children of Adam, take your adornment at every mosque' (al-A'raf 7:31). This verse means to adopt adornment at the time of prayer, i.e., wear clothes. (2) In the hadith: 'Then the Messenger of Allah sent 'Ali behind him and commanded him to proclaim immunity. Abu Hurayrah said: So 'Ali proclaimed with us among the people of Mina on the Day of Sacrifice: No polytheist shall perform Hajj after this year, and no one shall circumambulate the House naked.' (Bukhari, Bab ma yustaru min al-'awrah, p. 53, no. 369). This hadith prohibits being naked. (3) Another hadith: 'From Abu Sa'id al-Khudri: He said the Messenger of Allah forbade al-Ishtimal al-Samma' and that a man wraps himself in a single garment with nothing covering his private parts.' (Bukhari, Bab ma yustaru min al-'awrah, p. 53, no. 367). This hadith also prohibits uncovering the 'awrah. Therefore, uncovering the 'awrah in a bathhouse in front of the general public will invalidate his 'adalah, and his testimony will not be accepted.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof concerning one whose testimony is rejected due to a major sin. The ruling: a person who enters a bathhouse without any covering over his private parts (i.e., completely naked) in the presence of others commits a grave sin (kabirah) that destroys his moral integrity ('adalah), hence his testimony is invalid. The proof is from the Quran: 'O children of Adam, take your adornment at every mosque' (7:31). The Hanafi understanding is that the verse commands covering the 'awrah, especially during prayer, but the general principle is that uncovering the 'awrah is prohibited. Additionally, two hadith are cited: one where the Prophet sent 'Ali to announce that no one will circumambulate the Ka'bah naked, and another forbidding wrapping oneself in a single cloth without covering the private parts. These clearly establish that nudity in public is a major sin. The commentary further illustrates with the example of a modern swimming pool: entering naked is the same as publicly exposing one's 'awrah, which is haram. Therefore, such a person becomes fasiq (transgressor) and his testimony is rejected per Hanafi law. The author emphasizes that this applies to bathhouses where people bathe together, not to private showers.

Key Terms
ستر (satr): Covering the private parts ('awrah) which is obligatory in front of others.
عدالت (adalah): Moral integrity required for a witness; lost by committing major sins or persisting in minor sins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because it is a waste of water.
B) Because it is a major sin of public nudity that destroys 'adalah.
C) Because it disturbs others.
D) Because it is a form of gambling.

Key Takeaway
Public nudity in a bathhouse or similar setting is a major sin that destroys 'adalah, thus the testimony of such a person is rejected in Hanafi law.

Testimony Rejected for Usury and Gambling
Ruling with proof on testimony rejection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that the testimony of a known usurer or gambler is rejected, and identify the condition under which playing chess invalidates testimony.

Core Idea
Usury and gambling are major sins that disqualify a witness; chess only does so if it causes neglect of religious duties.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri discusses three types of conduct that invalidate one's 'adalah (moral integrity) and thus render testimony unacceptable. The author presents textual proofs from the Quran and Hadith for usury and gambling, and then addresses the debated issue of chess.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
List the three acts mentioned: consuming usury (riba), playing backgammon (nard) with stakes, and playing chess (shatranj). For usury and gambling, the ruling is clear: they are major sins that lead to fasiq status and rejection of testimony. For chess, the ruling is conditional.
2
Examine the proofs for usury and gambling
Read the Quranic verses (2:275 for usury, 5:90 for gambling) and the hadith on backgammon. Note how each proof establishes the prohibition and its severity, thus invalidating 'adalah.
The hadith compares playing backgammon to dipping hands in pork flesh and blood.
3
Analyze the dispute on chess
The passage presents two contradictory athar: one permitting chess from Muhammad ibn Sirin and Hisham ibn 'Urwah, and one condemning it from 'Ali and Ibn 'Umar. The author synthesizes: chess is only problematic if it leads to neglect of religious duties.
The Hanafi position weighs the risk of neglect; chess can be permissible if free from gambling and not causing abandonment of duties.
4
Apply the condition to testimony
If chess causes one to miss prayers or obligations, the player becomes a fasiq and testimony is rejected. Otherwise, if played without gambling and without neglecting duties, it may be permissible and 'adalah remains intact.
This is the practical legal effect (thamarah al-khilaf).
5
State the conclusion for each act
For usury and gambling: testimony is always rejected. For chess: testimony rejected only if it leads to neglect of religious duties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۸۳۳) (۲۴) اور نہ اس کی گواہی جو سود کھائے اور نہ جو نرد اور شطرنج کھیلے۔ جو سود کھا تا ہو اور اس میں مشہور ہو وہ فاسق ہو گیا۔ اس لئے اس کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ آیت میں ہے کہ سود کھانا حرام ہے۔ الذين يأكلون الربوا لايقومون الا كما يقوم الذي يتخبطه الشيطان من المس ذلك بانهم قالوا انما البيع مثل الربوا واحل الله البيع وحرم الربوا (و) (آیت ۲۷۵ ، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں سود حرام قرار دیا ہے۔ اس لئے اس کے کھانے والے کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ ولا المقامر بالنرد : نرد ایک قسم کا کھیل ہے۔ اگر اس سے جوا کھیلے تو حرام ہے۔ اور جوا کھیلنے سے عدالت ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔ اس کی دلیل پہلے گزر چکی ہے۔ انما الخمر الميسر والانصاب والازلام رجس من عمل الشيطان فاجتنبوه لعلكم تفلحون ( آیت۹۰، سورۃ المائدۃ ۵) اور اگر جوئے کے بغیر مرد کھیلے تب بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن سليمان بن بريدة عن ابيه ان النبي الا الله قال من لعب بالنرد شير فكانما صبغ يده في لحم خنزیر و دمه (ه) (مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم اللعب بالنردشیر، ج ۲، ص ۲۴۰، نمبر ۲۲۶۰ ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی انھی عن الملعب بالنرد، ص ۱۳۲۷، نمبر ۴۹۳۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نردشیر سے جو کھیلے گویا کہ اپنا ہاتھ سور کے گوشت اور خون میں رنگا۔ اس لئے اس کے کھیلنے والوں کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ والشطر نج : یہ بھی ایک قسم کا کھیل ہے اگر اس میں جوانہ ہوا ہو اور اس میں مشغولیت کی وجہ سے نماز اور دینی فرائض نہ چھوٹتے ہوں تو بعض حضرات نے اس کو مباح قرار دیا ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ انبأ الشافعي قال كان محمد بن سيرين وهشام بن عروة يلعبان بالشطرنج استدبارا(الف)(سنن سیقی ، باب الاختلاف عن ابن عمر انه سئل عن الشطرنج فقال هو شر من النرد (ج) (سن ليبقى ، باب الاختلاف في اللعب بالشطرنج، ج عاشر ص ۳۵۸، نمبر ۲۰۹۳۴/۲۰۹۲۸) ان آثار سے معلوم ہوا کہ شطرنج کھیلنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یوں کہا جائے کہ اس سے دینی فرائض چھوٹتے ہوں تو کھیلنے والے کی عدالت ساقط ہو جائے گی اور فاسق ہونے کی بنا پر گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی۔
(2833) (24) And not the testimony of one who consumes usury, and not the one who gambles with backgammon and chess. One who consumes usury and is well-known for it becomes a fasiq. Therefore his testimony is not accepted. The verse says that consuming usury is forbidden: 'Those who consume usury will not stand except as one who has been touched by Satan with insanity. That is because they say: Trade is like usury. But Allah has permitted trade and forbidden usury' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:275). This verse declares usury forbidden. Therefore the testimony of its consumer is not accepted. 'And the one who gambles with backgammon' (nard): Backgammon is a type of game. If one gambles with it, it is forbidden, and gambling invalidates 'adalah. Its proof has already passed: 'Indeed, intoxicants, gambling, [sacrificing to] stones, and [divining by] arrows are an abomination of Satan's handiwork. So avoid it that you may be successful' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:90). And if one plays without gambling, it is still not permissible. In a hadith: 'From Sulayman ibn Buraydah from his father that the Prophet said: Whoever plays backgammon is as if he has dipped his hand in the flesh and blood of a pig.' (Muslim, Bab tahrim al-lu'b bi al-nardashir, vol. 2, p. 240, no. 2260; Abu Dawud, Bab fin nahyi 'an al-mul'ab bi al-nard, p. 1327, no. 4939). This hadith indicates that playing backgammon is like dipping one's hand in pork and blood. Therefore the testimony of such players is not accepted. As for chess: This is also a type of game. If there is no gambling in it, and due to involvement, prayer and religious obligations are not abandoned, then some scholars have declared it permissible. There is an athar: 'Imam al-Shafi'i informed us: Muhammad ibn Sirin and Hisham ibn 'Urwah used to play chess occasionally.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-ikhtilaf fi al-lu'b bi al-shatranj, vol. 10, p. 1357, no. 20923). From this athar it is understood that playing chess is permissible, because it refreshes the mind, provided that prayer and religious duties are not missed and there is no gambling. But if one is so engrossed that prayer and religious obligations are missed, then 'adalah is invalidated and testimony is not accepted. Athar indicates this: 'From 'Ali that he said: Chess is the gambling of the non-Arabs.' Another narration: 'From Ibn 'Umar that he was asked about chess and said: It is worse than backgammon.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-ikhtilaf fi al-lu'b bi al-shatranj, vol. 10, p. 358, nos. 20934/20928). From these athar it is understood that playing chess is not permissible. Therefore it is said: if religious duties are missed due to it, then the player's 'adalah is invalidated and testimony is not accepted due to being a fasiq.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof concerning three types of people whose testimony is rejected: (1) the consumer of usury (riba), (2) the gambler with backgammon (nard), and (3) the chess (shatranj) player under certain conditions. The ruling: a person known for consuming usury becomes a fasiq (transgressor) and his testimony is unacceptable. Proof: Quran 2:275 explicitly forbids usury and equates its severity with being touched by Satan. Similarly, gambling (maysir) is forbidden by Quran 5:90. The hadith about backgammon, where the Prophet compared it to dipping hands in pork blood, shows it is a major sin. Therefore, playing backgammon with or without gambling is impermissible and invalidates testimony. As for chess, the text presents two views: some early scholars like Muhammad ibn Sirin and Hisham ibn 'Urwah played it without gambling and without neglecting duties, deeming it permissible. Others like 'Ali and Ibn 'Umar condemned it as worse than backgammon. The author harmonizes: if chess leads to missing prayer and religious obligations, it becomes a major sin and testimony is not accepted; otherwise, if free from gambling and not causing neglect, it may be permissible but still not ideal. Thus, the final ruling is that 'adalah is only lost if the game causes dereliction of religious duties.

Key Terms
ربا (riba): Usury or interest; any increase in a loan without corresponding compensation, considered a major sin.
نرد (nard): Backgammon, a game played with dice; playing it with gambling is haram, and even without gambling it is not permissible.
شطرنج (shatranj): Chess; its ruling depends on whether it involves gambling or causes neglect of religious duties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition does playing chess invalidate one's testimony?
A) If the person is a beginner.
B) If there is no gambling and it does not lead to missing prayer or religious duties.
C) If the person wins most games.
D) If it is played in private.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects testimony from those who openly commit major sins like usury and gambling; chess only affects testimony if it leads to neglecting religious duties.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony Rejected for Disgraceful Acts like Urinating on Road
Ruling with proof: disgraceful acts break 'adalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that a person who habitually performs disgraceful acts is considered a zaneen and his testimony is rejected, and identify the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Disgraceful acts break 'adalah; a witness must have haya'.

This lesson addresses a specific category of witnesses whose testimony is rejected: those who habitually engage in degrading behavior, such as urinating or eating in public without dignity. The author connects this to the hadith term 'zaneen'—one suspected in religion—and argues that such shamelessness makes a person likely to lie. Understanding this ruling sharpens your grasp of the conditions of 'adalah (moral integrity) in Hanafi law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Note the specific acts listed: urinating on the road and eating on the road. The ruling is that the testimony of a person who habitually does such disgraceful acts is not accepted.
Habitual is key; occasional lapse may not have the same effect.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
The author explains that such a person will not feel shame even in lying. This links the disgraceful act to a lack of haya' (modesty), which is a foundation of iman and 'adalah.
In Hanafi, 'adalah requires both taqwa and muru'a (dignity).
3
Locate the hadith proof
The passage cites the hadith from 'A'ishah listing categories of unacceptable witnesses, including 'az-zaneen'. Another hadith from Abu Hurayrah explains zaneen as 'one suspected in his religion.'
The word 'zaneen' is the key term linking disgraceful acts to loss of credibility.
4
Apply the ruling to other disgraceful acts
The principle is qiyas: any act that systematically degrades one's dignity and indicates shamelessness falls under this ruling—e.g., spitting in public, making obscene gestures, etc.
The 'illa is lack of shame, not the specific act.
5
Note the cross-madhhab perspective
The Hanafi position is stricter: even minor but disgraceful acts invalidate 'adalah. Some other schools require the act to be a major sin or done openly without remorse.
The thamarah al-khilaf: a witness may be accepted in another school but rejected in the Hanafi.

(۲۸۳۴) (۲۵) ولا من يفعل الافعال المستخفّة كالبول على الطريق والاكل على الطريق. جو حقیر کام کرنے کا عادی ہو وہ جھوٹ بولنے سے بھی عار محسوس نہیں کرے گا۔ اس لئے ایسے آدمی کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ طنین یعنی دین میں متہم آدمی کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله الله لا تجوز شهادة خائن ولا خائنة ولا مجلود حدا ولا مجلودة ولا ذى غمر لاحنة ولا مجرب شهادة ولا القانع اهل البيت لهم ولا ظنين في ولاء ولا قرابة (د) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فیمن لا تجوز شهادته، ج ۲، ص ۵۵ نمبر ۲۲۹۸) اس حدیث میں ہے والا طنین یعنی اس کی گواہی مقبول نہیں جو دین میں متہم ہو۔ چنانچہ اس کی تفسیر حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال بعث رسول الله مناديا في السوق انه لا تجوز شهادة خصم ولا ظنين. قيل وما الظنين ؟ قال المتهم في دینه - دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ ولا مریب(ہ)
(2834) (25) And not the one who does disgraceful acts, like urinating on the road and eating on the road. One who habitually does degrading things will not feel shame even in lying. Therefore the testimony of such a person is not accepted. In a hadith: 'az-Zaneen' — the person suspected in religion — his testimony is not accepted. From 'A'ishah: She said the Messenger of Allah said: 'The testimony of a treacherous man or woman, of one who has received a hadd punishment, of one who harbors rancor, of one who has practiced testimony, of a domestic servant of a household, and of one suspect (zaneen) in patronage or kinship is not valid.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi man la tajuuzu shahadatuhu, vol. 2, p. 55, no. 2298). In this hadith, 'az-zaneen' means one who is suspected in religion. Similarly, its explanation is in another hadith: From Abu Hurayrah: The Messenger of Allah sent a crier in the market: 'The testimony of a litigant (khasm) and of a suspect (zaneen) is not valid.' It was asked: 'What is az-zaneen?' He said: 'One suspected in his religion.' Another narration: 'And nor of a person of doubt (mureeb).'
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof concerning people whose testimony is rejected due to their involvement in disgraceful acts (af'al mustakhiffa). The ruling: a person who habitually performs degrading actions such as urinating or eating in public without consideration of dignity loses 'adalah because such behavior indicates a lack of shame, which makes them likely to lie. The proof is a hadith from 'A'ishah listing several categories of unacceptable witnesses, including 'az-zaneen' (the suspicious in religion). The term 'zaneen' is explained in another hadith as someone suspected in his religion—one whose religious commitment is questionable due to such disgraceful acts. The author concludes that such a person's testimony is not accepted. The lesson emphasizes that 'adalah requires not only avoiding major sins but also maintaining a level of dignity and not engaging in shameless behavior.

Key Terms
ظنين (zaneen): A person who is suspected in matters of religion; one whose religious commitment is questionable due to disgraceful behavior or association.
مستخفّة (mustakhiffa): Acts that are considered disgraceful or degrading, such as urinating on the road or eating in public without dignity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, which category of witnesses is rejected as 'zaneen'?
A) One who has received a hadd punishment
B) One who harbors rancor
C) One who is suspected in religion
D) One who is a domestic servant

Key Takeaway
A witness must possess both taqwa and muru'a; habitual disgraceful acts like urinating on the road strip a person of 'adalah and make his testimony unacceptable.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
6 min
Testimony of Those Who Do Contemptible Acts
Ruling on rejecting testimony of contemptible act doers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a habitual committer of contemptible acts and identify the hadith proof used to derive it.

Core Idea
A witness who habitually does contemptible acts loses probity; his testimony is rejected.

The Hanafi school holds that a witness must possess probity (adalat). This lesson examines a specific category: those who habitually do contemptible acts like urinating or eating in public. The text provides the ruling, discusses examples (backgammon, chess), and cites a hadith to establish that such a person is 'suspected in religion' (dhanin) and thus disqualified from testifying.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states: 'And not the one who does contemptible acts, like urinating on the road and eating on the road.' The ruling is that such a person's testimony is not accepted.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary cites the hadith from Aishah (radiyallahu anha) that lists categories whose testimony is not accepted, including 'ad-dhanin' (the one suspected in religion).
Hadith from Tirmidhi no. 2298.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'dhanin' is interpreted by the Sahaba as 'the one suspected in his religion'. The commentary argues that a person who habitually does contemptible acts falls under this category because such acts indicate lack of moral scruple and therefore suspicion in religion.
Also supported by the hadith of Abu Hurairah defining dhanin.
4
Analyze the examples (backgammon and chess)
The text discusses these games to illustrate how contempibility is context-dependent. For chess, if it leads to neglect of religious duties, it becomes a contemptible act that nullifies probity.
The ruling on chess is conditional; it's not automatically disqualified.
5
Note the cross-madhhab status
The Hanafi position is that testimony is rejected. Hambali and Shafi'i schools may accept it if the witness is otherwise reliable. This difference arises from interpretation of 'adalat' and the concept of 'dhanin'.
Mukhtalaf fih.

[2834 (25)] ولا من يفعل الافعال المُستخفّة كالبول على الطريق والاكل على الطريق [۱۳۲۷، نمبر ۴۹۳۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نردشیر سے جو کھیلے گویا کہ اپنا ہاتھ سور کے گوشت اور خون میں رنگا۔ اس لئے اس کے کھیلنے والوں کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ والشطر نج : یہ بھی ایک قسم کا کھیل ہے اگر اس میں جوانہ ہوا ہو اور اس میں مشغولیت کی وجہ سے نماز اور دینی فرائض نہ چھوٹتے ہوں تو بعض حضرات نے اس کو مباح قرار دیا ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ انبأ الشافعي قال كان محمد بن سيرين وهشام بن عروة يلعبان بالشطرنج استدبارا(الف)(سنن سیقی ، باب الاختلاف في اللعب بالشطرنج، ج عاشر ، ص ۱۳۵۷، نمبر ۲۰۹۲۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ شطرنج کھلینا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کھیل میں دماغ تازہ ہوتا ہے بشرطیکہ نماز اور دینی فرائض نہ چھوٹتے ہوں اور جوا نہ ہوا ہو۔ اور اگر اس میں اتنی مشغولیت ہے کہ نماز اور دینی فرائض چھوٹتے ہوں تو پھر عدالت ساقط ہوگی اور گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی۔ اثر میں اس کی طرف اشارہ ہے۔ عن على انه يقول الشطرنج هو ميسر الاعاجم (ب) دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ عن ابن عمر انه سئل عن الشطرنج فقال هو شر من النرد (ج) (سن ليبقى ، باب الاختلاف في اللعب بالشطرنج، ج عاشر ص ۳۵۸، نمبر ۲۰۹۳۴/۲۰۹۲۸) ان آثار سے معلوم ہوا کہ شطرنج کھیلنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے یوں کہا جائے کہ اس سے دینی فرائض چھوٹتے ہوں تو کھیلنے والے کی عدالت ساقط ہو جائے گی اور فاسق ہونے کی بنا پر گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی۔ (۲۸۳۴) (۲۵) اور نہ اس کی گواہی جو حقیر کام کرتا ہو جیسے راستے پر پیشاب کرنا اور راستے پر کھانا۔ جو حقیر کام کرنے کا عادی ہو وہ جھوٹ بولنے سے بھی عار محسوس نہیں کرے گا۔ اس لئے ایسے آدمی کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ طنین یعنی دین میں متہم آدمی کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت قال رسول الله الله لا تجوز شهادة خائن ولا خائنة ولا مجلود حدا ولا مجلودة ولا ذى غمر لاحنة ولا مجرب شهادة ولا القانع اهل البيت لهم ولا ظنين في ولاء ولا قرابة (د) (ترندی شریف، باب ما جاء فیمن لا تجوز شهادته، ج ۲، ص ۵۵ نمبر ۲۲۹۸) اس حدیث میں ہے والا طنین یعنی اس کی گواہی مقبول نہیں جو دین میں متہم ہو۔ چنانچہ اس کی تفسیر حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال بعث رسول الله مناديا في السوق انه لا تجوز شهادة خصم ولا ظنين. قيل وما الظنين ؟ قال المتهم في دینه - دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ ولا مریب(ہ) حاشیہ : (الف) ہمیں حضرت امام شافعی نے خبر دی کہ محمد ابن سیرین اور ہشام بن عروہ کبھی کبھی شطرنج کھیلتے تھے (ب) حضرت علی نے فرمایا شطرنج عجمیوں کا جوا ہے (ج) حضرت ابن عمر سے شطرنج کے بارے میں پوچھا تو فرمایا وہ مرد سے بھی برا ہے (و) حضور نے فرمایا خائن مرد اور خائنہ عورت کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے اور نہ حد لگے ہوئے مرد کی اور نہ حد لگی ہوئی عورت کی اور نہ بھائی سے کینہ رکھنے والے کی اور نہ شھادت کی مشق کئے ہوئے کی اور گھر کے نوکر کی اور نہ دین میں متہم کی اور نہ قرابت والے کی (ہ) حضور نے بازار میں اعلان کرنے والے کو بھیجا کہ خصم کی گواہی مقبول نہیں اور نظمنین کی۔ پوچھا گیا کہ طنین کیا ہے؟ فرمایا جو دین میں متہم ہو۔ دوسری روایت میں ہے مریب کی یعنی جس کی دینداری میں شک ہو۔
[2834 (25)] And not the one who does contemptible acts, like urinating on the road and eating on the road. [1327, number 4939) In this hadith it is said: Whoever plays backgammon, it is as if he has dipped his hand in the flesh and blood of a pig. Therefore the testimony of those who play it is not accepted. And chess: It is also a kind of game. If there is no gambling in it, and due to engrossment in it, prayer and religious duties are not missed, then some scholars have declared it permissible. There is an athar: Al-Shafi'i informed us, saying: Muhammad ibn Sirin and Hisham ibn Urwa used to play chess occasionally. (a) (Sunan al-Saqi, chapter on disagreement about playing chess, vol. 10, p. 1357, no. 20923) From this athar it is learned that playing chess is permissible because it refreshes the mind, provided that prayer and religious duties are not missed and there is no gambling. And if there is such engrossment that prayer and religious duties are missed, then his probity (adalah) is nullified and his testimony will not be accepted. There is an indication of this in the athar: 'Ali said: Chess is the gambling of the non-Arabs. (b) Another narration: Ibn Umar was asked about chess and he said: It is worse than backgammon. (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on disagreement about playing chess, vol. 10, p. 358, nos. 20934/20928) From these athar it is learned that playing chess is not permissible. Therefore if religious duties are missed due to it, the player's probity is nullified and his testimony is not accepted due to his being a sinner. (2834) (25) And not the testimony of one who does contemptible acts, such as urinating on the road and eating on the road. One who habitually does contemptible acts will not feel shame in lying. Therefore the testimony of such a person is not accepted. There is a hadith: 'Adh-dhanin (the suspicious person), i.e., the one suspected in religion, his testimony is not accepted. 'Aishah reported that the Messenger of Allah said: The testimony of a treacherous man or woman, of one who has received hadd punishment, of one who bears a grudge against his brother, of one who practices giving testimony, of a servant of a household, of one suspected in patronage or kinship, is not accepted. (d) (Tirmidhi, chapter on those whose testimony is not accepted, vol. 2, p. 55, no. 2298) In this hadith it says: 'adh-dhanin, i.e., the one suspected in religion, his testimony is not accepted. Its explanation is in another hadith: Abu Hurairah said: The Messenger of Allah sent a caller in the market saying: The testimony of a litigant and of 'ad-dhanin is not accepted. It was asked: What is 'ad-dhanin? He said: The one suspected in his religion. Another narration says: Nor of al-muraib (the doubtful). (e) Footnotes: (a) Imam Shafi'i informed us that Muhammad ibn Sirin and Hisham ibn Urwa used to sometimes play chess. (b) 'Ali said: Chess is the gambling of the non-Arabs. (c) Ibn Umar was asked about chess and said: It is worse than backgammon. (d) The Prophet said: The testimony of a treacherous man and a treacherous woman, of a man who has been flogged (hadd) and a woman who has been flogged, of one who bears a grudge against his brother, of one who practices testimony, of a servant of the household, of one suspected in patronage or kinship, is not accepted. (e) The Prophet sent a caller to the market: The testimony of a litigant and 'ad-dhanin is not accepted. It was asked: What is 'ad-dhanin? He said: The one suspected in his religion. Another narration says: al-muraib, i.e., the one whose religiosity is doubted.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the rejection of testimony from individuals who habitually engage in contemptible acts. The matn states that the testimony of such a person is not accepted, giving examples like urinating or eating on the road. The commentary expands by explaining that such people lose their sense of shame and thus are prone to lying. The author then discusses two specific games: backgammon (نردشیر) and chess (شطرنج). For backgammon, a hadith is cited indicating that playing it is akin to dipping one's hand in pig's blood, so the player's testimony is rejected. Chess is more nuanced: the author presents different narrations. From Imam Shafi'i, there is an athar that Muhammad ibn Sirin and Hisham ibn Urwa played chess, suggesting permissibility under conditions of no gambling and no neglect of religious duties. However, other narrations from 'Ali and Ibn Umar condemn chess as worse than backgammon. The author harmonizes these by stating that if chess leads to neglect of prayers and duties, then the player becomes a sinner (fasiq) and his testimony is rejected. Otherwise, it may be permissible. The core proof is the hadith of 'Aishah listing categories of people whose testimony is not accepted, including 'ad-dhanin (the one suspected in religion). This hadith is further explained by Abu Hurairah's report that 'ad-dhanin means the one suspected in his religion. Thus, contemptible acts lead to suspicion in religion, disqualifying the person from giving testimony. The commentary also distinguishes between societies: if eating on the road is not considered contemptible in a particular society, it does not affect probity. In summary, the Hanafi position is that persistent engagement in contemptible acts strips a person of moral probity (عدالت) and thus his testimony is rejected.

Key Terms
ظنين (dhanin): A person suspected in his religion due to his actions, such as habitual contemptible acts.
عدالت (adalat): Probity; the quality of being upright and trustworthy, required for a witness's testimony to be accepted.
افعال مستخفّة (af'al mustakhaffah): Contemptible acts that degrade a person's dignity and indicate lack of moral scruple.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this text, what is the ruling on the testimony of a person who habitually eats on the road?
A) Accepted, because it is a personal habit
B) Rejected, because it is a contemptible act that indicates lack of moral scruple
C) Accepted only if the person is wealthy
D) Rejected only if the person is also a gambling addict

Key Takeaway
Habitual contemptible acts negate the probity (adalat) required for a witness, leading to rejection of his testimony.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
The Testimony of Ahl al-Hawa: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Ruling on accepting testimony of ahl al-hawa except Khattabiyyah, with Shafi'i disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on accepting testimony from ahl al-hawa, explain the Shafi'i objection, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Ahl al-hawa are Muslim and their testimony is accepted unless they are proven false, except for the Khattabiyyah who are apostates.

This passage from the matn and its commentary addresses a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: should the testimony of sectarians (like Shia) be accepted against Ahl al-Sunnah? The Hanafi school holds that they are Muslims, and the general rule of Muslim uprightness applies. Imam Shafi'i argues that their enmity makes them unreliable. We'll examine the proofs on both sides and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the ruling from the matn: testimony of ahl al-hawa is accepted, except the Khattabiyyah. Note that ahl al-hawa are defined as groups like Shia who differ in creed but are still Muslims.
The exception of Khattabiyyah is crucial: they are considered apostates due to extreme beliefs.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
Locate the hadith cited: 'المسلمون عدول بعضهم على بعض' (Muslims are upright to each other). This is a general proof that all Muslims are presumed upright unless disqualified by a specific sin (like flogging for qadhf).
The hadith establishes a presumption of uprightness.
3
Identify the Shafi'i counterproof
Find the Shafi'i argument: ahl al-hawa bear enmity (ghimir) towards Ahl al-Sunnah, and a hadith rejects testimony of one who bears a grudge. This is used to exclude their testimony against Sunnis.
The Shafi'i rely on the specific hadith of 'dhu al-ghimir'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is implicit: the general rule takes precedence; enmity is not automatically presumed. Only if actual enmity is proven does the exclusion apply. The Khattabiyyah exception shows that only non-Muslims are categorically excluded.
The Hanafi approach weighs the general hadith over the specific, arguing that the specific hadith only applies when enmity is established.
5
Identify the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis accept testimony from Shia and other sectarians against Sunnis; Shafi'is reject it. This affects court cases where a witness is a known sectarian.
In Hanafi jurisprudence, the testimony is valid; in Shafi'i, it is not accepted against Sunnis.

[2836 (27) وتقبل شهادة اهل الهوى إلا الخطابية. اہل ہواء سے مراد وہ تمام جماعتیں ہیں جو اہل سنت و الجماعہ کے علاوہ ہوں جیسے شیعہ رافضی وغیرہ۔ وہ مسلمان ہیں اگر چہ ان کا عقیدہ اہل سنت والجماعۃ کے علاوہ ہے۔ اس لئے ان کی گواہی اہل سنت والجماعۃ کے خلاف قبول کی جائے گی۔ عن عمرو بن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده قال قال رسول الله الله الله المسلمون عدول بعضهم على بعض الا محدودا في قرية (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی هیبتة ۴ نے من قال لا تجاوز شهادته اذا اتاب، ج رابع ص ۱۳۳۰، نمبر ۲۰۶۵۰ ردار قطنی کتاب عمر الی ابی موسی اشعری ، ج رابع ، ص ۱۳۲، نمبر ۴۴۲۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ مسلمان سب کے سب عادل ہیں اس لئے چاہے تھوڑا بہت اختلاف ہو سچ بولنے کی کوشش کریں گے۔ اس لئے ان کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ان کی گواہی اہل سنت و الجماعۃ کے خلاف مقبول نہیں۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اہل سنت والجماعۃ سے کینہ ہوگا اور کینہ کی وجہ سے جھوٹی گواہی دے سکتے ہیں اس لئے مقبول نہیں (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ کسی آدمی سے کینہ ہو تو اس کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ عن عمرو بن شعیب عن ابيه عن جده ان رسول الله الا الله د شهادة الخائن والخائنة وذى الغمر على اخيه ... وقال ابوداؤد العمر الحقد والشحناء (ج) (ابوداد دشریف، باب من ترد شهادته ص ۱۵۱، نمبر ۳۶۰۰ / ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فیمن لا تجوز شهادته، ج ۲، ص ۵۵، نمبر ۲۲۹۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ عمر والے یعنی کینے والے کی گواہی مقبول نہیں۔ اور دوسرے فرقے والوں کو حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا مسلمان کو گالی دینا فسق ہے اور اس سے قتال کرنا کفر ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا مسلمان بعض بعض پر عادل ہیں مگر تمہت زنا میں حد لگائے ہوئے (ج) آپ نے رو کی خیانت کرنے والے مرد اور خیانت کرنے والی عورت کی اور بھائی کے بارے میں کینہ رکھنے والے کی گواہی.. حضرت امام ابو داؤد نے فرمایا عمر کا معنی کینہ ہے۔
[2836 (27)] And the testimony of ahl al-hawa (people of desires) is accepted except the Khattabiyyah. By ahl al-hawa are meant all groups other than Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, such as Shia, Rafidi, etc. They are Muslims even if their creed differs from Ahl al-Sunnah. Therefore their testimony will be accepted even against Ahl al-Sunnah. 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb narrated from his father from his grandfather that the Messenger of Allah said: Muslims are upright (adul) to each other except one who has been flogged (hadd) in a town? (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, etc.) This hadith indicates that all Muslims are upright, so even if there is slight difference, they try to speak truth. Therefore their testimony is accepted. Imam Shafi'i says: Their testimony is not accepted against Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah. He says they bear grudge against Ahl al-Sunnah and due to grudge may give false testimony, so it is not accepted. (2) There is a hadith that if one bears a grudge against someone, his testimony is not accepted. 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb narrated from his father from his grandfather that the Messenger of Allah rejected the testimony of the treacherous man and woman, and the one who bears a grudge (dhu al-ghimir) against his brother... Abu Dawud said: al-ghimir means hatred and enmity. (c) (Abu Dawud, chapter on those whose testimony is rejected, p. 151, no. 3600; Tirmidhi, chapter on those whose testimony is not accepted, vol. 2, p. 55, no. 2298) This hadith states that the testimony of one who bears a grudge is not accepted. Footnotes: (a) The Prophet said: Abusing a Muslim is fisq and fighting him is kufr. (b) The Prophet said: Muslims are upright to each other except one who has been flogged for slander. (c) The Prophet rejected the testimony of a treacherous man and woman and one who bears a grudge against his brother... Imam Abu Dawud said: al-ghimir means hatred.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage records a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Shafi'i regarding the acceptance of testimony from ahl al-hawa (sectarians such as Shia). The Hanafi position, as stated in the matn, is that their testimony is accepted generally, with the exception of the Khattabiyyah (an extremist sect that considered the Prophet inferior to 'Ali, thus deemed apostates). The reasoning is that ahl al-hawa are still Muslims, and the hadith 'المسلمون عدول' (Muslims are upright) applies to them. Even if they differ in creed, they are assumed to be truthful unless proven otherwise. Imam Shafi'i argues that their testimony against Ahl al-Sunnah is not accepted because they bear enmity (kainah) towards Ahl al-Sunnah, which may lead them to give false testimony. He cites a hadith rejecting testimony of one who bears a grudge (ذو الغمر). The Hanafi response is implied: the general ruling of accepting testimony of Muslims takes precedence, and enmity is not automatically assumed; only if actual enmity is proven might the testimony be rejected. The exception of Khattabiyyah shows that only those who are considered outside the fold of Islam (due to extreme beliefs) are excluded. Thus, the Hanafi school is more lenient in accepting testimony from sectarians.

Key Terms
اهل الهوى (ahl al-hawa): People of desires; sectarians who follow their own opinions contrary to Ahl al-Sunnah, such as Shia.
الخطابية (al-Khattabiyyah): An extremist Shia sect that considered the Prophet inferior to 'Ali or held heretical beliefs; their testimony is rejected because they are outside the fold of Islam.
الغمر (al-ghimir): Grudge or hatred; in this context, it refers to enmity that may lead to false testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, whose testimony among ahl al-hawa is not accepted (exceptional)?
A) The Shia
B) The Khattabiyyah
C) The Rafidah
D) All ahl al-hawa

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts the testimony of ahl al-hawa (except Khattabiyyah) based on the general presumption of Muslim uprightness, while Shafi'is reject it due to presumed enmity.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
6 min
Testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa and the Khattabiyyah Exception
Ruling on testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa with exception for Khattabiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa, explain the exception for Khattabiyyah, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on enmity.

Core Idea
A Muslim's testimony is accepted unless they sanction lying for their faith.

This lesson examines a key area of divergence between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: the acceptance of testimony from Muslims who follow sects other than Ahl al-Sunnah. The Hanafi position is that such testimony is generally accepted, with one critical exception — the Khattabiyyah, who permit and even mandate lying for religious purposes. The Shafi'i school, however, rejects such testimony entirely due to presumed enmity. This dispute highlights the Hanafi principle that default probity (ʿadālah) applies to all Muslims unless proven otherwise.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling and its evidence
State the Hanafi position: testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa is accepted. Identify the hadith cited: 'Muslims are udul against each other' (ʿAmr ibn Shuʿayb). Understand that this establishes a default of probity.
The hadith is a dalīl naqlī (textual evidence).
2
Analyse the Shafi'i objection and its evidence
State the Shafi'i position: testimony against Ahl al-Sunnah is not accepted due to enmity. Identify their evidence: hadith rejecting testimony of one who harbors rancor (dhū al-ghimr). Note the thamarah al-khilaf: in practice, Hanafis accept a Shi'i's testimony against a Sunni, Shafi'is do not.
The Shafi'i argument is based on the assumption that differing beliefs create enmity.
3
Explain the exception for Khattabiyyah
Identify the Khattabiyyah sect and their belief: they permit and even obligate lying for the sake of their religion. Explain that because of this clear permission of lying, the default probity is overridden, and their testimony is rejected. This exception is unique to the Hanafi school.
The exception is not based on enmity but on the sanction of lying itself.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Summarize the practical difference: Hanafi courts admit testimony from most non-Sunni Muslims (e.g., Shiʿa) unless they belong to a sect that permits lying; Shafiʿi courts reject all such testimony against Sunnis.
The dispute is one of legitimate ikhtilaf, with both schools having valid concerns.
