شهادة اهل الهواء الا الخطابية
چونکہ اہل سنت کے خلاف کینہ ہو گا اس لئے اس کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔
الا الخطابية : یہ رافضیوں کا عالی فرقہ ہے۔ یہ ابی خطاب محمد بن وہب الا جدع کی طرف منسوب ہے۔ ان کا اعتقاد یہ ہے کہ اپنے مذہب کے علاوہ پر جھوٹ بولنا جائز ہے بلکہ مذہب کو چھپانے یا بچانے کے لئے جھوٹ بولنا واجب ہے۔ تو چونکہ جھوٹ بولنے کا شبہ ہے اس لئے اس کی گواہی دوسرے مذہب والے کے خلاف مقبول نہیں ہے۔
ات اهل الهواء : خواہش والے، یہاں مراد ہے اہل سنت والجماعہ کے علاوہ کے مذاہب
And the testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa (people of desires) is accepted, except for the Khattabiyyah. By 'Ahl al-Ahwa' are meant all groups besides Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, such as the Shi'a, Rawafid, etc. They are Muslims even if their belief differs from Ahl al-Sunnah. Therefore their testimony is accepted against Ahl al-Sunnah. From 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather: The Messenger of Allah said: Muslims are upright (udul) against each other, except one who has been flogged for qadhf... This hadith indicates that all Muslims are upright, so even if there is slight difference, they will strive to tell the truth. So their testimony is accepted. Imam al-Shafi'i says: Their testimony against Ahl al-Sunnah is not accepted. He argues that they bear enmity towards Ahl al-Sunnah, and due to enmity they might give false testimony, so it is not accepted. (2) A hadith: 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that the Messenger of Allah rejected the testimony of a treacherous man and woman, and of one who harbors rancor against his brother... Abu Dawud said: 'al-ghimr' means rancor and spite. This hadith indicates that the testimony of one who harbors rancor is not accepted. And the other sects... The testimony of Ahl al-Ahwa except the Khattabiyyah. Since they have enmity against Ahl al-Sunnah, their testimony is not accepted. The Khattabiyyah are an extremist sect of the Rawafid, attributed to Abu al-Khattab Muhammad ibn Wahb al-Ajd'. Their belief is that lying is permissible for the sake of their religion, and even obligatory to conceal or protect their religion. Since there is suspicion of lying, their testimony against someone of a different religion is not accepted. 'Ahl al-Ahwa': people of desires, here meaning the sects other than Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the acceptance of testimony from Ahl al-Ahwa (followers of heretical sects) who are still Muslims. The Hanafi position is that their testimony is accepted because they are Muslims and the default is that Muslims are upright (udul). The author cites a hadith that Muslims are udul against each other. Then he presents the Shafi'i objection: their testimony against Ahl al-Sunnah is not accepted because they harbor enmity, and enmity leads to false testimony, citing a hadith rejecting testimony of one who bears rancor. The Hanafi response is not explicitly stated but the text maintains the ruling, except for Khattabiyyah, a sect that considers lying permissible. The exception is because of clear suspicion of lying. The commentary explains that Khattabiyyah are a branch of Rawafid who believe lying for the sake of religion is not only permissible but obligatory. Therefore, their testimony is not accepted. The Hanafi school thus distinguishes between ordinary Ahl al-Ahwa, who are still trustworthy, and extremists who permit lying.

Key Terms
أهل الهواء (ahl al-ahwa): People of desires; here meaning all Muslim sects other than Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah, e.g., Shi'a, Rawafid.
الخطابية (al-khattabiyyah): An extremist sect of the Rawafid, followers of Abu al-Khattab, who believe lying for the sake of their religion is permissible and even obligatory.
عدول (udul): Upright, just; a witness must be ʿadl (upright) for testimony to be accepted.
ذو الغمر (dhu al-ghimr): One who harbors rancor or spite against another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the testimony of Khattabiyyah rejected according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because they are not Muslims
B) Because their beliefs allow and even obligate lying for religious purposes
C) Because they are enemies of Ahl al-Sunnah
D) Because they are not considered 'udul due to their heresy

Key Takeaway
Hanafis accept testimony from Ahl al-Ahwa (non-Sunni Muslims) except those who sanction lying, such as the Khattabiyyah.

Shahadat — Testimony

Testimony of Dhimmis Against Each Other: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i/Maliki
Ruling on dhimmi testimony with inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on dhimmi testimony across different religions and distinguish it from the Shafi'i/Maliki position by citing the key proofs.

Core Idea
A dhimmi's testimony against another dhimmi is accepted in Hanafi law even across religions, based on a clear prophetic permission.

This passage addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: can a Christian dhimmi testify against a Jewish dhimmi? While the Hanafi school accepts such testimony based on the Prophet's explicit permission, the Shafi'i and Maliki schools reject it due to the perpetual enmity between the two communities. Let's examine the proofs and reasoning of both sides.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling
Identify the core ruling from the matn: testimony of dhimmis is accepted against each other even if their religions differ.
This is the starting point for the dispute.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
Locate the hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah where the Prophet permitted the People of the Book's testimony against each other.
A clear textual evidence (dalil naqli).
3
Present the opposing position
Note that Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik reject cross-religion dhimmi testimony.
They argue based on enmity and another hadith.
4
Analyze the opposing proofs and Hanafi response
Examine the opposing dalil: Quran 5:14 (enmity) and the hadith 'no testimony across religions except the religion of Muhammad'. Understand how the Hanafi school responds that the explicit hadith from Jabir takes precedence and that dhimmis are one legal category.
The Hanafi response emphasizes the specificity of the Jabir hadith.

(۱۲۸۳۷ (۲۸) زمیوں کی گواہی بعض کی بعض کے خلاف جائز ہے چاہے وہ آپس میں مختلف ہوں۔
یہودی یا نصرانی جو دارالاسلام میں ٹیکس دیکر رہتے ہوں ان کو ذمی کہتے ہیں وہ ایک دوسرے کے خلاف گواہی دیں تو جائز ہے۔ نصرانی نصرانی کے خلاف گواہی دے تو دونوں ایک مذہب کے ہوئے اس لئے جائز ہے۔ اور نصرانی یہودی کے خلاف گواہی دے تب بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ دونوں ذمی ہیں۔ اور گویا کہ غیر مسلم ہونے کے اعتبار سے ایک مذہب ہوئے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔عن جابر بن عبد الله بعضهم على ان رسول الله له اجاز شهادة اهل الكتاب بعضهم على بعض (الف ) ( ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب شھادۃ اہل الکتاب بعض بص ۱۳۴۰ نمبر ۲۳۷۴ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شهادة اهل الملل بعضهم على بعض وشهادة المسلم علیهم ، ج عامن بص ۳۵۷ نمبر ۱۵۵۲۷) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اہل کتاب جو ذمی ہوتے ہیں بعض کی گواہی بعض کے خلاف جائز ہے۔
نا امام شافعی اور امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ ذمی میں بھی ایک مذہب والے کی گواہی دوسرے کے خلاف قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ (1) پیچھے گزر چکا ہے کہ جن کے درمیان کینہ ہو اس کی گواہی مقبول نہیں۔ اور یہود اور نصاری کے درمیان دائمی کینہ ہے اس لئے یہودی کی گواہی نصرانی کے خلاف اور نصرانی کی گواہی یہودی کے خلاف مقبول نہیں۔ آپس کی دشمنی کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ فاغرينا بينهم العداوة والبغضاء الى يوم القيامة (ب) ( آیت ۱۴ سورة المائدة (۵) اس آیت میں ہے کہ اس کے آپس میں عداوت اور بغض ڈال دیا ہے۔ اس لئے ایک ملت کی گواہی دوسری ملت کے لئے مقبول نہیں ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابی ھریرة قال قال رسول الله الله لايتوارث اهل ملتين شيء ولا تجوز شهادة ملة على ملة الا ملة محمد فانها على غيرهم (ج) (سن للبیہقی ، باب من رد شهادة اهل الذمته ، ج عاشر ص ۲۷۴ نمبر ۲۰۶۱/ مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شهادة اهل الملل بعضهم على بعض عشهادة المسلم عليهم ، ج ثامن ، ص ۱۳۵۶، نمبر ۱۵۵۲۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک مذہب والا دوسرے مذہب کے خلاف گواہی نہ دے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضور نے جائز قرار دی اہل کتاب کی گواہی بعض کی بعض پر (ب) ہم نے ان کے آپس میں قیامت تک دشمنی اور بغض بھڑ کا دی (ج ) آپ نے فرمایا دولت والے ایک دوسرے کے کچھ بھی وارث نہیں ہوں گے ۔ اور کسی ملت کی گواہی کسی دوسری ملت پر جائز نہیں سوائے ملت محمد کی اس لئے کہ وہ اس کے غیر پر بھی جائز ہے۔
The testimony of the people of dhimmah is accepted, some against others, even if their religions differ. Because they harbor enmity against Ahl al-Sunnah, therefore their testimony is not accepted. Except the Khattabiyyah: they are a sect of the Rafidah, attributed to Abu al-Khattab Muhammad ibn Wahb al-Ajdah. Their belief is that lying against other than their own sect is permissible, rather it is obligatory to lie to conceal or protect their sect. So due to the suspicion of lying, their testimony against someone of another sect is not accepted. As for Ahl al-Hawa: people of desires, here meaning sects other than Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah. (28) The testimony of dhimmis against some of them is permissible even if they are different among themselves. Jew or Christian who live in Dar al-Islam paying tax are called dhimmi; they may testify against each other. If a Christian testifies against a Christian, both are of the same religion, so it is permissible. And if a Christian testifies against a Jew, it is also permissible because both are dhimmis, and they are, as it were, of one religion by virtue of being non-Muslim. (2) There is a hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah that the Messenger of Allah permitted the testimony of the People of the Book against each other. This hadith indicates that the testimony of the People of the Book who are dhimmis is permissible against each other. Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik say that among dhimmis, testimony of one religion against another is not accepted. (1) It has passed that testimony between those who have enmity is not accepted, and between Jews and Christians there is perpetual enmity, so a Jew's testimony against a Christian and a Christian's testimony against a Jew is not accepted. The proof for their mutual enmity is the verse: 'We have stirred up among them enmity and hatred until the Day of Resurrection' (5:14). This verse shows that enmity and hatred have been placed between them. Therefore the testimony of one nation against another is not accepted. (2) There is a hadith from Abu Hurairah that the Messenger of Allah said: 'People of two religions do not inherit from each other, and the testimony of one religion against another is not permissible, except the religion of Muhammad, for it is permissible against others.' This hadith indicates that one religion should not testify against another.
Source pages p. 159

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the acceptance of testimony among dhimmis (protected non-Muslims) in a Hanafi legal context. The passage begins by stating the ruling: 'The testimony of the people of dhimmah is accepted, some against others, even if their religions differ.' This is the Hanafi position. The commentary then explains that the Khattabiyyah sect (a Rafidi group) is excluded because they believe lying is permissible to protect their sect, leading to suspicion. The term 'ahl al-hawa' here refers to sects other than Ahl al-Sunnah. The second part clarifies that dhimmis (Jews and Christians living under Islamic rule) can testify against each other whether of the same or different religions, because their shared non-Muslim status makes them effectively one community. The Hanafi evidence is a hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah where the Prophet permitted the People of the Book's testimony against each other. The passage then presents the opposing view of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Malik, who argue that testimony between Jews and Christians is not accepted due to perpetual enmity between them, citing the Quranic verse (5:14) and a hadith from Abu Hurairah. The Hanafi response is implied by the initial ruling: the hadith from Jabir and the legal principle that dhimmis are considered one group for testimony purposes. The commentary follows the author's order, first stating the ruling, then giving the exception for Khattabiyyah, then expanding on dhimmis, citing the hadith, and finally presenting the inter-madhhab dispute.

Key Terms
اهل الذمة (ahl al-dhimmah): Protected non-Muslims (Jews, Christians, etc.) living under Islamic rule who pay jizyah.
الخطابية (al-Khattabiyyah): A Rafidi sect that believes lying is permissible to protect their sect.
اهل الهواء (ahl al-hawa): People of desires; here referring to sects other than Ahl al-Sunnah wal-Jama'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only if the Muslim ruler permits it.

Key Takeaway
A dhimmi's testimony against another dhimmi is accepted in Hanafi law even across religions, based on the Prophet's explicit permission in the hadith of Jabir.

Testimony of a Harbi Against a Dhimmi: Ruling and Proof
Ruling on rejecting testimony of a harbi against a dhimmi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of a harbi against a dhimmi and explain the proof from hadith and qiyas.

Core Idea
A harbi's testimony against a dhimmi is rejected due to status inferiority and the principle that one religion cannot testify against another.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position that the testimony of a harbi (a non-Muslim from enemy territory) against a dhimmi (a protected non-Muslim) is not accepted. We will trace the proof from a hadith and an athar from Shuraih, and understand the qiyas that extends the rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? It is the testimony of a harbi against a dhimmi. The ruling is that it is not accepted (la tu'qbal).
The ruling is negative: testimony is rejected.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith: 'Testimony of one religion against another is not permissible except the religion of Muhammad.' This directly prohibits cross-religion testimony except when Muslims are involved.
The hadith is ahad and zanni al-thubut, but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Examine the athar from Shuraih
Shuraih did not permit Jews to testify against Christians or vice versa, but permitted Muslims against all. This shows the principle applied by early authorities.
The athar supports the hadith and provides an explicit case.
4
Apply qiyas
The ruling from Jew vs Christian is extended to harbi vs dhimmi by analogy. The illa (effective cause) is difference of religion/millah and the lower status of the testifier.
The text explicitly states that if Jew vs Christian is rejected, then a fortiori harbi vs dhimmi is rejected.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The ruling applies to two scenarios: a musta'min (harbi with aman) testifying against a dhimmi, and a dhimmi in Dar al-Harb being testified against by a harbi. In both, the testimony is rejected.
The reason given is that the harbi's status is lower than the dhimmi's.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۳۸ (۲۹) ولا تُقبل شهادة الحربي على الذمی [۲۸۳۹] (۳۰) وان كانت الحسنات اغلب من السيئات والرجل ممن يجتنب الكبائر قبلت شهادته وان الم [۲۸۳۸] (۲۹) حربی کی گواہی ذمی کے خلاف قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔
ذمی سے مراد مستامن ہے یعنی وہ حربی جو امن لیکر دار الاسلام آیا ہو۔ یا دوسری شکل یہ ہے کہ ذمی کسی کام کے لئے دار الحرب گیا اور کوئی بات ہو گئی اب حربی ذمی کے خلاف گواہی دے رہا ہے تو یہ گواہی مقبول نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ حربی کا درجہ کم ہے اور ذمی دار الاسلام میں رہنے کی وجہ سے اعلی ہے۔ اس لئے حربی کی گواہی ذمی کے خلاف مقبول نہیں ہے (۲) او پر حدیث گزری کہ ایک ملت کی گواہی دوسرے کے خلاف مقبول نہیں۔اس لئے ذمی اور حربی کے بارے میں اس پر عمل کیا جائے گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ کان شريح يـجـيـز شهادة كل ملتها ولا يجيز شهادة اليهودى على النصراني ولا النصراني على اليهودى الا المسلمين فانه كان يجيز شهادتهم على الملل كلها (الف) (سن للبیہقی ، باب من اجاز شهادۃ اہل الذمة على الوصية في السفر عند عدم من شهد عليها من المسلمین ، ج عاشر ص ۲۷۹، نمبر ۲۰۶۲۸ مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب شهادة اهل الملل بعضهم على بعض وشهادة السلم عليهم ، ج ثامن ، ص ۳۵۷ نمبر ۱۵۵۲۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ یہودی کی گواہی نصرانی کے خلاف اور نصرانی کی گواہی یہودی کے خلاف قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ جب ان دونوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی تو اسی پر قیاس کر کے حربی کی گواہی ذمی کے خلاف قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔
(29) The testimony of a harbi against a dhimmi is not accepted. By dhimmi here is meant a musta'min, i.e., a harbi who has entered Dar al-Islam with aman. Or another form: a dhimmi went to Dar al-Harb for some work, and something happened; now a harbi is giving testimony against the dhimmi—this testimony is not accepted. Because the status of a harbi is lower, and the dhimmi is higher due to living in Dar al-Islam. Therefore the testimony of a harbi against a dhimmi is not accepted. (2) The hadith passed earlier that the testimony of one nation against another is not accepted. So in the case of dhimmi and harbi, this will be acted upon. (2) There is an athar: Shuraih used to permit testimony of every nation, but would not permit the testimony of a Jew against a Christian nor a Christian against a Jew, except Muslims, for he would permit their testimony against all nations. This athar indicates that the testimony of a Jew against a Christian and a Christian against a Jew is not accepted. And when the testimony of these two is not accepted, then by analogy the testimony of a harbi against a dhimmi is not accepted.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling that the testimony of a harbi (a non-Muslim from enemy territory) against a dhimmi (a protected non-Muslim) is not accepted. The commentator explains two scenarios: first, a harbi who has entered Dar al-Islam with aman (safe conduct) is considered a musta'min, and his testimony against a dhimmi is rejected. Second, if a dhimmi goes to Dar al-Harb and a harbi testifies against him, it is also rejected. The reason given is that the harbi's status is lower, while the dhimmi has a higher status due to being under Islamic protection. The commentary then references a previous hadith about one nation not testifying against another, and applies it here. It also cites an athar (report) from Shuraih, who would not allow Jews and Christians to testify against each other, and uses qiyas (analogy) to extend that ruling to harbi vs. dhimmi. The passage is a clear statement of the Hanafi position with proof from hadith and qiyas.

Key Terms
حربي (harbi): A non-Muslim who is in a state of war with Muslims, not under Islamic protection.
مستامن (musta'min): A harbi who has been granted aman (safe conduct) to enter Dar al-Islam temporarily.
اثر (athar): A report from a Companion or a early authority like Shuraih, used as proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the harbi is not trustworthy.
B) Because the harbi has a lower status than the dhimmi.
C) Because the dhimmi is a non-Muslim.
D) Because the harbi is a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The testimony of a harbi against a dhimmi is not accepted due to inferior status and the rule that one religion cannot testify against another.

Testimony Based on Predominance of Good Deeds
Ruling with proof on testimony conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for accepting testimony and apply them to scenarios involving minor and major sins.

Core Idea
A witness' testimony is accepted if good deeds predominate and major sins are avoided.

In Islamic law, the integrity ('adalah) of a witness is crucial for accepting testimony. The Hanafi school adopts a practical approach: rather than requiring sinlessness, it focuses on the overall character and avoidance of major sins. This lesson examines the precise conditions and their evidence.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the core ruling: the testimony of a person whose good deeds outweigh bad deeds and who avoids major sins is accepted, even if he commits minor sins.
2
Identify the conditions
List the two conditions: (1) predominance of good deeds over bad, and (2) avoidance of major sins (kaba'ir). Minor sins are overlooked.
3
Understand the rationale
The commentator explains that requiring complete avoidance of minor sins would make it impossible to find witnesses, so the criterion is practical.
4
Analyze the proof
Examine the athar from Caliph Umar: he flogged three men for qadhf (false accusation) but stated that if they repented, their testimony would be accepted. This shows that repentance restores 'adalah even after a major sin.
The dalil is a Qawl Sahabi (saying of a Companion), which is zanni in transmission and meaning.
5
Apply the ruling
Consider scenarios: a person who commits a major sin but repents; or a person who occasionally commits minor sins but avoids major ones. In both cases, testimony is accepted according to the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۳۹] (۳۰) وان كانت الحسنات اغلب من السيئات والرجل ممن يجتنب الكبائر قبلت شهادته وان الم [۲۸۳۸] (۲۹) حربی کی گواہی ذمی کے خلاف قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ (۲۸۳۹) (۳۰) اگر اچھائیاں برائیاں پر غالب ہوں اور آدمی گناہ کبیرہ سے پر ہیز کرتا ہو تو اس کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی اگر چہ گناہ صغیرہ کر لیتا ہو۔
کسی آدمی کے اچھے اعمال غالب ہوں اور برے اعمال کم ہوں اور گناہ کبیرہ سے پر ہیز کرتا ہو تو چاہے صغیرہ گناہ کر لیتا ہو پھر بھی اس کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔
تمام گناہ صغیرہ سے پر ہیز کرنا تو آدمی کے لئے مشکل ہے اس لئے یہ قید لگا ئیں کہ بالکل گناہ صغیرہ نہ کرے تو گواہ کے لئے کوئی آدمی نہیں ملے گا ۔ اس لئے یہی کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ اچھائیاں غالب ہو اور گناہ کبیرہ سے پر ہیز کرتا ہو بہ گواہی دینے کے لئے اتنا کافی ہے۔ بلکہ گناہ کبیرہ کر لیا لیکن بعد میں اس سے توبہ کر لی تب بھی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔
اثر میں ہے۔ وجلد عمر ابا بكرة وشبل بن معبد ونافعا بقذف المغيرة ثم استتابهم وقال من تاب قبلت شهادته ... وقال الشعبى وقتادة اذا اكذب نفسه جلد وقبلت شهادته (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب شهادة القاذف والسارق والزانی،
(30) If good deeds are more numerous than bad deeds, and the man avoids major sins, his testimony is accepted even if he commits minor sins. If a man's good deeds predominate and his bad deeds are few, and he avoids major sins, even if he commits minor sins, his testimony is still accepted. To avoid all minor sins is difficult for a man, so if they placed the condition of completely avoiding minor sins, no one would be found for testimony. Therefore it can be said that if good deeds predominate and he avoids major sins, this is sufficient for giving testimony. Rather, even if he committed a major sin but later repented from it, his testimony will be accepted. In an athar: Umar flogged Abu Bakra, Shibl ibn Ma'bad, and Nafi' for qadhf against al-Mughirah, then he gave them the opportunity to repent and said, 'Whoever repents, his testimony is accepted.' And al-Sha'bi and Qatadah said: If he accuses himself, he is flogged and his testimony is accepted.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This passage addresses the condition for the acceptance of a witness's testimony in terms of moral character ('adalah). The ruling states that if a person's good deeds outweigh his bad deeds, and he avoids major sins (kaba'ir), his testimony is accepted even if he occasionally commits minor sins (sagha'ir). The commentator explains that requiring complete avoidance of minor sins would make it impossible to find witnesses, so the practical criterion is predominance of good deeds and avoidance of major sins. Furthermore, even if a person commits a major sin but sincerely repents, his testimony is accepted after repentance. The proof is an athar (report) from Caliph Umar, who flogged three individuals for false accusation (qadhf) but told them that if they repented, their testimony would be accepted. The commentary also cites al-Sha'bi and Qatadah who held that if the accuser admits his guilt, he is flogged and his testimony is accepted afterward. This passage emphasizes the Hanafi leniency in accepting repentance and focusing on the overall character rather than minor lapses.

Key Terms
كبيرة (جمع: كبائر) (kabirah (pl. kaba'ir)): Major sins; avoiding them is a condition for testimony.
صغيرة (جمع: صغائر) (saghairah (pl. sagha'ir)): Minor sins; committing them does not disqualify testimony if one avoids major sins and good deeds predominate.
استتابة (istitabah): Giving an opportunity to repent; after repentance, testimony is accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is the testimony of a person who commits minor sins accepted?
A) Only if he never commits any sin.
B) If his good deeds outweigh his bad deeds and he avoids major sins.
C) Only if he repents from all minor sins.
D) Never, because any sin disqualifies him.

Key Takeaway
Testimony is accepted if good deeds predominate and major sins are avoided; repentance restores testimony after major sins.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Testimony Accepted When Good Deeds Prevail and Major Sins Avoided
Ruling with proof from Umar's policy and athar on repentance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a witness's testimony to be accepted according to the Hanafi school and identify the proofs from Umar's practice and the athar on repentance.

Core Idea
A witness's testimony is accepted if his good deeds dominate and he avoids major sins; minor sins do not disqualify.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on accepting testimony based on a witness's apparent character. The text clarifies that perfection is not required; rather, a preponderance of good deeds and avoidance of major sins suffice. The proofs are drawn from Umar's policy of judging by outward actions and from the practice of accepting repentance after qadhf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and conditions
State the ruling: testimony is accepted if the witness's good deeds outweigh his bad deeds and he avoids major sins. Note that minor sins are overlooked as long as they are not habitual.
This is the Hanafi position, distinct from stricter schools.
2
Examine the proof from Umar's policy
Read the athar from Umar: after revelation ceased, judgment is based on apparent deeds. If someone shows good, he is trusted and his testimony accepted; his inner state is left to Allah.
This establishes that outward righteousness is the criterion, not inner perfection.
3
Understand the effect of repentance
The text mentions that even if a person commits a major sin but repents, his testimony becomes acceptable. The example of Umar flogging the qadhf accusers and then accepting their repentance supports this.
Repentance restores adala (uprightness) in the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the criterion: apparent righteousness
Consider a contemporary scenario: a witness frequently prays and gives charity, but occasionally gossips. He avoids major sins like theft or slander. His testimony is accepted because good deeds dominate and major sins are avoided.
The ruling is practical and avoids imposing impossible standards.

(۳۰) اگر اچھائیاں برائیاں پر غالب ہوں اور آدمی گناہ کبیرہ سے پر ہیز کرتا ہو تو اس کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی اگر چہ گناہ صغیرہ کر لیتا ہو۔ کسی آدمی کے اچھے اعمال غالب ہوں اور برے اعمال کم ہوں اور گناہ کبیرہ سے پر ہیز کرتا ہو تو چاہے صغیرہ گناہ کر لیتا ہو پھر بھی اس کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔ تمام گناہ صغیرہ سے پر ہیز کرنا تو آدمی کے لئے مشکل ہے اس لئے یہ قید لگا ئیں کہ بالکل گناہ صغیرہ نہ کرے تو گواہ کے لئے کوئی آدمی نہیں ملے گا ۔ اس لئے یہی کہا جا سکتا ہے کہ اچھائیاں غالب ہو اور گناہ کبیرہ سے پر ہیز کرتا ہو بہ گواہی دینے کے لئے اتنا کافی ہے۔ بلکہ گناہ کبیرہ کر لیا لیکن بعد میں اس سے توبہ کر لی تب بھی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔ اثر میں ہے۔ وجلد عمر ابا بكرة وشبل بن معبد ونافعا بقذف المغيرة ثم استتابهم وقال من تاب قبلت شهادته ... وقال الشعبى وقتادة اذا اكذب نفسه جلد وقبلت شهادته (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب شهادة القاذف والسارق والزانی، حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت شریح جائز قرار دیتے تھے ایک ملت کی گواہی دوسری ملت پر اور نہیں جائز قرار دیتے تھے یہودی کی گواہی نصرانی پر اور نہ نصرانی کی گواہی یہودی پر مگر مسلمان کی گواہی پس وہ ان کی گواہی تمام مذاہب پر جائز قرار دیتے تھے (ب) حضرت مرنے کوڑے لگائے ابو بکر و اور شبل بن معبد اور نافع پر حضرت مغیرہ پر تہمت لگانے کی وجہ سے۔ پھر اس سے تو بہ کرنے کے لئے کہا اور فرمایا جو تو بہ کرے گا اس کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی ... حضرت شعمی اور قتادہ نے فرمایا اگر اپنے آپ کو جھٹلائے تو حد لگے گی اور اس کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔ سمعت عمر بن الخطاب يقول ان اناسا كانوا يوخذون بالوحي في عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وان الوحى قد انقطع وانما ناخذكم الآن بما ظهر لنا من اعمالكم، فمن اظهر لنا خيرا امناه وقربناه وليس الينا من سريرته شيء الله يحاسب في سريرته ومن اظهر لنا سوءا لم نامنه ولم نصدقه ، وان قال ان سريرته حسنة ( الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الشهداء والعدول ،ص۱۳۵۰، نمبر (۲۶۴) اس اثر میں حضرت عمر نے فرمایا ظاہری طور پر اچھے اعمال نظر آتے ہوں تو اس پر اعتماد کریں گے اور اس کو قریب کریں گے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اس کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی۔ الم بمعصیۃ : اگر گناہ کرے، اس سے مراد گناہ صغیرہ کا ارتکاب کرنا ہے
(30) If good deeds outweigh evil deeds and a person avoids major sins, his testimony is accepted even if he commits minor sins... (Urdu explanation) In an athar: Umar flogged Abu Bakrah, Shibl ibn Ma'bad, and Nafi' for qadhf of al-Mughirah, then gave them the opportunity to repent and said: 'Whoever repents, his testimony will be accepted.' ... And al-Sha'bi and Qatadah said: 'If he accuses himself (i.e., admits false accusation), he is flogged and his testimony is accepted.' ... I heard Umar ibn al-Khattab say: 'Indeed, people used to be taken by revelation in the time of the Messenger of Allah, and revelation has ceased. Now we take you by what appears to us of your deeds. Whoever shows us good, we trust him and bring him near; we have nothing to do with his inner self; Allah will account him for his inner self. And whoever shows us evil, we do not trust him nor believe him, even if he says his inner self is good.' ... In this athar, Umar said that if good deeds are apparent, we will trust him and bring him near. From this it is understood that his testimony is accepted. 'al-mu bima'siyah': if he commits sin, meaning committing minor sins.
Source pages p. 160

Commentary
This is a ruling on the acceptance of testimony based on the witness's apparent character. The matn states that if a person's good deeds outweigh his bad deeds and he avoids major sins (kabair), his testimony is accepted even if he commits minor sins (sagha'ir). The commentary explains that it is impractical to expect complete avoidance of minor sins; therefore, the standard is dominance of good deeds and avoidance of major sins. Furthermore, if a person commits a major sin but repents, his testimony becomes acceptable after repentance. The proof includes the action of Umar ibn al-Khattab who flogged those who committed qadhf and then gave them the opportunity to repent, and said that whoever repents his testimony is accepted. Also, Sha'bi and Qatadah stated that if the accuser admits his false accusation, he is flogged and his testimony is accepted. Another athar from Umar states that in the absence of revelation, judgment is based on apparent deeds; if someone shows good, he is trusted and his testimony accepted, and his inner state is left to Allah. This establishes that apparent righteousness is the criterion for accepting testimony.

Key Terms
گناہ کبیرہ (kabirah): Major sins such as murder, zina, theft, etc., which have prescribed punishments or are explicitly condemned.
گناہ صغیرہ (saghirah): Minor sins that do not have prescribed punishments; committing them does not disqualify a witness if the person avoids major sins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What reasoning did Umar ibn al-Khattab give for judging witnesses based on their apparent deeds?
A) Because inner righteousness is impossible to know.
B) Because revelation has ceased, so judgment is based on outward actions.
C) Because all people are trustworthy.
D) Because the Prophet ordered that judgment be based on outward deeds.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, witness testimony is accepted if the person avoids major sins and his good deeds outweigh his bad deeds, based on the principle that judgment is based on outward behavior.

Testimony of the Uncircumcised, Eunuch, Illegitimate Child, and Hermaphrodite
Ruling with proof from athar of Umar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the testimony of the aqlaf, khasi, walad al-zina, and khuntha, and explain the proof from the athar of Umar that judgment is based on apparent deeds.

Core Idea
Testimony is accepted based on apparent righteousness, not physical condition or parentage.

This lesson expands on the principle that a witness's integrity (adala) is judged by outward deeds, not by physical status or lineage. Building on the previous ruling, we now examine four specific cases—uncircumcised, eunuch, illegitimate child, and hermaphrodite—all of whose testimony is accepted in Hanafi fiqh. The legal proof is the same athar of Umar ibn al-Khattab, emphasizing that what matters is what is apparent to the qadi, not hidden matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four categories and the ruling
List the four individuals: aqlaf (uncircumcised), khasi (eunuch), walad al-zina (illegitimate child), and khuntha (hermaphrodite). The ruling is that their testimony is accepted (maqbulah).
These categories share no inherent defect in adala; the common factor is that none reflects personal sin or deficiency.
2
Locate the dalil: the athar of Umar
The proof is the same athar used earlier: Umar's statement that after revelation ceased, judgment is based on apparent deeds. This is recorded in Sahih al-Bukhari.
The athar serves as a general principle: outward righteousness qualifies a witness, regardless of physical condition or birth.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Umar's rule 'we take you by what appears to us of your deeds' implies that a witness is deemed trustworthy if he appears good. Physical conditions (uncircumcised, eunuch) and parentage (illegitimate) do not affect outward adala. Thus, testimony is accepted.
The key is apparent good deeds (zahir al-a'mal al-saliha).
4
Note cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
While Hanafis accept unconditionally, some schools (e.g., Shafi'is) may require additional scrutiny for walad al-zina, considering potential social stigma. However, Hanafis hold that the child bears no sin, so his adala is intact.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in a Shafi'i court, the testimony of a walad al-zina might be rejected or subject to further investigation, whereas in a Hanafi court it is accepted if he appears righteous.

Source Text

وتُقبل شهادة الاقلف والخصى وولد الزنا و شهادة الخنثى (۳۱) اس اثر میں ہے کہ گناہ کبیرہ کر کے تو بہ کرے تو اس کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی۔ اور ظاہری طور پر اچھے اعمال کرتے ہوں تو گواہی مقبول ہوگی اس کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے۔ سمعت عمر بن الخطاب يقول ان اناسا كانوا يوخذون بالوحي في عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وان الوحى قد انقطع وانما ناخذكم الآن بما ظهر لنا من اعمالكم، فمن اظهر لنا خيرا امناه وقربناه وليس الينا من سريرته شيء الله يحاسب في سريرته ومن اظهر لنا سوءا لم نامنه ولم نصدقه ، وان قال ان سريرته حسنة (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب الشهداء والعدول ،ص۱۳۵۰، نمبر (۲۶۴) اس اثر میں حضرت عمر نے فرمایا ظاہری طور پر اچھے اعمال نظر آتے ہوں تو اس پر اعتماد کریں گے اور اس کو قریب کریں گے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اس کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی۔ الم بمعصیۃ : اگر گناہ کرے، اس سے مراد گناہ صغیرہ کا ارتکاب کرنا ہے
And the testimony of the aqlaf (uncircumcised), and the khasi (eunuch), and the walad al-zina (illegitimate child), and the khuntha (hermaphrodite) is accepted. (31) In this athar: whoever repents after a major sin, his testimony is accepted. And if he appears to do good deeds, his testimony is accepted, and the proof is this athar: I heard Umar ibn al-Khattab say: 'Indeed, people used to be taken by revelation in the time of the Messenger of Allah, and revelation has ceased. Now we take you by what appears to us of your deeds. Whoever shows us good, we trust him and bring him near; we have nothing to do with his inner self; Allah will account him for his inner self. And whoever shows us evil, we do not trust him nor believe him, even if he says his inner self is good.' ... In this athar, Umar said that if good deeds are apparent, we will trust him and bring him near. From this it is understood that his testimony is accepted. 'al-mu bima'siyah': if he commits sin, meaning committing minor sins.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This is a ruling stating that the testimony of an aqlaf (uncircumcised man), a khasi (eunuch), a walad al-zina (illegitimate child), and a khuntha (hermaphrodite) is accepted. The commentary explains that these conditions do not affect a person's adala (integrity). The proof is the same athar of Umar that was used for the previous ruling, showing that judgment is based on apparent deeds, not physical condition or parentage. Thus, if such a person appears righteous, his testimony is accepted.

Key Terms
اقلف (aqlaf): An uncircumcised male; lack of circumcision does not affect his adala.
خصی (khasi): A eunuch, one whose testicles have been removed; this does not affect his adala.
ولد الزنا (walad al-zina): A child born out of wedlock; his parentage is a sin for his parents, not for him, so his adala is intact.
خنثی (khuntha): A hermaphrodite whose gender is ambiguous; testimony is accepted based on apparent deeds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts testimony based on apparent righteousness, regardless of physical condition or parentage, as supported by the athar of Umar.

Shahadat — Testimony
beginner
12 min
Acceptance of Testimony from Those with Physical or Lineage Conditions
Ruling with proofs and response to Imam Malik's objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the testimony of the uncircumcised, eunuch, child of fornication, and hermaphrodite, and evaluate the Hanafi response to the Maliki objection.

Core Idea
Testimony is based on integrity, not physical condition or lineage — even a child of fornication can be a valid witness.

In this passage, the Hanafi school addresses a common question: does a person's physical condition or birth status affect their ability to be a credible witness? The ruling affirms that integrity ('adalah) is the sole criterion, and the testimony of four specific categories — the uncircumcised, eunuch, child of fornication, and hermaphrodite — is accepted. The passage also confronts a Maliki objection regarding the child of fornication, providing textual evidence and reasoning to uphold the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
First, note that the Hanafi school accepts testimony from all four categories: the uncircumcised (aqlaf), the eunuch (khasi), the child of fornication (walad al-zina), and the hermaphrodite (khuntha). The key principle is that justice is based on a person's own actions, not physical defects or lineage.
The word 'aqlaf' refers to an uncircumcised man; 'khasi' to a eunuch; 'walad al-zina' to a child born out of wedlock; and 'khuntha' to a person with ambiguous gender characteristics.
2
Identify the proofs for each category
For the uncircumcised: lack of circumcision does not remove integrity. For the eunuch: a report from Umar accepting Alqamah's testimony. For the child of fornication: hadith 'Believers are Allah's witnesses on earth' and reports from Ata and Sha'bi. For the hermaphrodite: they are between male and female, and testimony is accepted from both; but better not to accept in hudud and qisas due to uncertainty.
The hadith 'al-mu'minun shuhada' Allah fi al-ard' is a general principle that believers are witnesses for Allah, implying validity unless proven otherwise.
3
Note the Maliki objection
Imam Malik rejects the testimony of a child of fornication, citing the hadith 'Walad al-zina sharru thalatha' (the child of fornication is the worst of three). He interprets this as indicating wickedness.
This hadith is found in al-Hakim's Mustadrak. The Maliki school considers it as evidence of lack of integrity.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the hadith means worst in lineage comparison, not necessarily sinful character. The child's own deeds determine integrity, and he is not responsible for his parents' sin.
The Hanafi position relies on the principle that no soul bears the sin of another (Quran 6:164).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In a Hanafi court, a child of fornication who is upright can testify; in a Maliki court, his testimony would be rejected regardless of his character.
This difference affects the admissibility of evidence in legal proceedings.

Source Text

الم بمعصیۃ : اگر گناہ کرے، اس سے مراد گناہ صغیرہ کا ارتکاب کرنا ہے

[2840] (31) اور قبول کی جائے گی غیر ختنہ والے کی گواہی اور خصی کی گواہی اور ولد الزنا کی گواہی اور خنثی کی گواہی بھی جائز ہے۔ تان جس آدمی کا ختنہ نہ ہوا ہو اس کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔
چونکہ ختنہ نہ کرنے سے عدالت ساقط نہیں ہوئی اور نہ فاسق ہوا۔ اس لئے اس کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی۔
خصی : جس آدمی کا خصیہ نکال لیا گیا ہو اس کو خصی کہتے ہیں۔ اس کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی۔ خصیہ نکال لینے کی وجہ سے اس کی عدالت ساقط نہیں ہوئی اس لئے اس کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی (2) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن سیرین ان عمر اجاز شهادة علقمة الخصی علی ابن مظعون (ب) (ابن ابي شيبة 563، في شهادة الخصی ، جلد خامس، ج 9، نمبر 23209 سن البیہقی ، باب من وجد منه ریح شراب اوقی سکران ، ج ثامن میں 549 نمبر 17175) اثر میں ہے کہ علقمہ خصی کی گواہی کی وجہ سے حد شرب جاری کی گئی جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ خصی کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔
گناہ اس کے ماں باپ کا ہے اس لڑکے کا گناہ نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے اس کی عدالت ساقط نہیں ہوگی اور اس کی گواہی مقبول ہوگی (2) انس بن مالک ان النبی صلی الله عليه وسلم قال المؤمنون شهداء الله في الارض وروينا عن عطاء والشعبي انهما قالا :تجوز شهادة ولد الزنا (ب) (سن سمیتی ، باب زهادة ولد الزنا۔ ج عاشر ص 121، نمبر 21180) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ولد الزنا کی گواہی جائز ہے۔

جائزه

شهادة الخنثى جائزة : جونہ عورت ہو اور نہ مرد بلکہ دونوں کے درمیان ہو تو اس کی گواہی مقبول ہے۔ جب مرد کی گواہی مقبول ہے اور عورت کی گواہی مقبول ہے تو دونوں کے درمیان کی گواہی بھی مقبول ہوگی ۔ البتہ اس کے عورت ہونے کا بھی شبہ ہے اس لئے حدود اور قصاص میں اس کی گواہی قبول نہ کرے تو اچھا ہے۔

امام مالک فرماتے ہیں کہ ولد الزنا کی گواہی مقبول نہیں۔
ان کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ولد الزنا شر الثلاثة (الف) (مستدرک للحاکم کتاب العتق ، ج ثانی، ص 233، نمبر 2853) اس حدیث میں ولد الزنا کو شریر کہا گیا ہے اس لئے اس کی گواہی مقبول نہیں :

حاشیه : (الف) ولد الزنا تین میں کے برے ہیں۔
Book of Testimonies. (31) The testimony of the uncircumcised, the eunuch, the child of fornication, and the hermaphrodite is accepted. Explanation: If he commits a sin, meaning a minor sin... (details in Urdu)... The testimony of the uncircumcised is accepted because lack of circumcision does not remove integrity nor make him a sinner. The eunuch: his testimony is accepted because removing testicles does not remove integrity. A report: Ibn Sirin that Umar accepted the testimony of Alqamah the eunuch against Ibn Muzun. The sin of the child of fornication belongs to his parents, not him, so his integrity is not lost. A report: Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet said: 'Believers are Allah's witnesses on earth.' We also have from Ata and Sha'bi that the testimony of a child of fornication is permissible. Hashya: Umar said: In the time of the Prophet people were taken by revelation, but now we judge by apparent deeds. Abdullah ibn Umar accepted the testimony of Alqamah the eunuch. The Prophet said: 'Believers are Allah's witnesses on earth.' Ata and Sha'bi allowed the testimony of a child of fornication. The testimony of a hermaphrodite is accepted because it is neither man nor woman, but between, and testimony is accepted from both, so from between. However, it is better not to accept his testimony in hadd and qisas due to doubt of being a woman. Imam Malik says testimony of a child of fornication is not accepted; his proof is hadith: 'The child of fornication is the worst of three.'
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage addresses the acceptance of testimony from individuals with specific physical conditions or birth status. The Hanafi school rules that testimony is accepted based on apparent justice and religious commitment, not physical defects or lineage. The uncircumcised man's testimony is valid since circumcision is not a condition of integrity. Similarly, a eunuch's testimony is valid; the hadith of Umar accepting Alqamah the eunuch's testimony proves this. A child born of fornication (walad al-zina) is not sinful himself, so his testimony is valid; the hadith 'believers are witnesses of Allah' is cited. The hermaphrodite's testimony is also accepted because they are between man and woman; but due to uncertainty, it is better not to accept in hudud and qisas. The passage then addresses Imam Malik's objection: he argues that the hadith 'walad al-zina is the worst of three' implies he is wicked, so testimony rejected. The Hanafi response is that this hadith refers to worst in lineage comparison, not necessarily sinfulness, and the child's own integrity is not affected.

Key Terms
اقلف (aqlaf): An uncircumcised man; one who has not undergone circumcision.
خصی (khasi): A eunuch; a man whose testicles have been removed.
ولد الزنا (walad al-zina): Child born out of wedlock; a child of fornication.
خنثی (khuntha): A hermaphrodite; a person with ambiguous gender organs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the reason for accepting the testimony of a child of fornication?
A) Because he is repentant for his parents' sin.
B) Because he is not sinful; his parents' sin does not affect his integrity.
C) Because the hadith 'walad al-zina is the worst of three' is weak.
D) Because he has no father to object.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts testimony from uncircumcised, eunuch, child of fornication, and hermaphrodite because integrity is judged by deeds, not physical condition or birth.

Testimony Must Match the Claim
Rule that testimony must conform to the claim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule that testimony must conform to the claim and apply it to identify when testimony is rejected.

Core Idea
Testimony that contradicts the claim is rejected – it must affirm the same subject.

In judicial proceedings, testimony serves to support the claim. If it contradicts the claim in subject matter, it fails its purpose and must be rejected. This lesson establishes the foundational rule of conformity between testimony and claim.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim
Determine exactly what the plaintiff is asserting. This is the subject of the lawsuit.
The claim defines what needs to be proven.
2
Identify the testimony
State what the witness testifies. Note the subject and details.
Witnesses are called to confirm the claim.
3
Compare the subject
Check whether the core subject of the testimony matches the core subject of the claim.
Minor differences in details may be excused if the subject is the same.
4
Apply the rule
If the testimony supports the same subject, accept it. If it contradicts or differs, reject it.
The ruling is clear: conformity leads to acceptance, opposition leads to rejection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[2841] (32) واذا واقفت الشهادة الدعوى قبلت وان خالفتها لم تقبل

یعنی اگر شہادت دعوی کے موافق ہو تو قبول کی جائے گی اور اس کے مخالف ہو تو قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ شہادت دعوی کی تائید کے لئے ہوتی ہے اس لئے جو دعوی ہو گواہی کے ذریعہ اس کی تائید ہو تو گواہی مقبول ہوگی ورنہ رد کر دی جائے گی۔ مثلا مدعی کہتا ہے کہ میری گائے چرائی گئی ہے اور گواہ گواہی دے رہا ہے کہ اس کی بھینس چوری ہوئی ہے تو دعوی کچھ اور ہے اور گواہ کی گواہی کچھ اور ہے۔ اس لئے گواہ کی گواہی رد کر دی جائے گی۔
(32) And if the testimony conforms to the claim, it is accepted; and if it opposes it, it is not accepted. That is, if testimony agrees with the claim, it is accepted; if it contradicts, it is rejected. Testimony is to support the claim, so whatever the claim is, if it is supported by testimony, it is accepted; otherwise it is rejected. For example: the plaintiff says 'my cow was stolen' and the witness testifies 'his buffalo was stolen' — the claim is one thing, the testimony another, so the testimony is rejected.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage states a foundational rule in judicial testimony: the testimony must exactly match the claim in subject matter. The function of testimony is to support the claim; if it contradicts, it fails to perform that function. An example is given: if the plaintiff claims theft of a cow but the witness testifies to theft of a buffalo, the testimony is rejected because it does not support the claim. This rule is applied strictly in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
الشهادة (al-shahādah): Testimony given by a witness in court.
الدعوى (al-daʿwā): The claim or lawsuit presented by the plaintiff.
قبلت (qubilat): Accepted (referring to testimony considered valid by the judge).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When it contradicts the claim

Key Takeaway
Testimony must support the claim in its core subject; otherwise, it is rejected.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Agreement of Witnesses in Wording and Meaning
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness agreement requirement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on witness agreement and apply the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) to a scenario where witnesses give different amounts.

Core Idea
Witnesses must agree in meaning; Abu Hanifa also requires identical wording, but the Sahibayn accept different wording if the meaning matches.

In Hanafi testimony law, the validity of a claim often hinges on the witnesses' agreement. This lesson examines a classic intra-madhhab difference: what happens when two witnesses testify to different amounts? Imam Abu Hanifa requires both the exact words (lafz) and the meaning (ma'na) to match, while his two leading disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), require only agreement in meaning. This distinction has a clear practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
The claim is for 2000 dirhams. One witness testifies '1000,' the other '2000.' Note that the lesser amount is included in the greater.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that testimony requires agreement in both lafz (wording) and ma'na (meaning). Since the wording differs ('1000' vs '2000'), the testimony is rejected entirely, even for the lesser amount.
Abu Hanifa's reasoning emphasizes precision to avoid uncertainty.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
The Sahibayn require only agreement in meaning. Since the lesser amount (1000) is contained within the greater (2000), the witnesses agree in meaning on 1000. Thus the testimony is accepted and judgment is given for 1000.
The Sahibayn prioritize substance over exact wording.
4
Analyze the reasoning of each side
Abu Hanifa argues that verbal precision ensures the integrity of testimony; the Sahibayn argue that inclusion of the lesser in the greater shows meaningful agreement.
Both views are recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under Abu Hanifa, the entire claim fails; under the Sahibayn, the claim succeeds for the lesser amount. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that of the Sahibayn, as it is more practical.
This illustrates how a difference in usul can dramatically affect court outcomes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[2842] (33) ويعتبر اتفاق الشاهدين في اللفظ والمعنى عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى فان شهد احدهما بالف والآخر بالفين لم تقبل شهادتهما عند ابي حنيفة وقال ابو يوسف و محمد تقبل بالف

یعنی اعتبار کیا جائے گا دونوں گواہوں کا متفق ہونا لفظ اور معنی میں بھی امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ۔ پس اگر ایک گواہ گواہی دے ایک ہزار کی اور دوسرے نے دو ہزار کی تو دونوں کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک، اور فرمایا صاحبین نے قبول کی جائے گی ایک ہزار پر

ایک آدمی نے دعوی کیا کہ میرے فلاں پر دو ہزار درہم ہیں۔ ایک گواہ نے گواہی دی کہ ایک ہزار ہے اور دوسرے نے گواہی دی کہ دو ہزار ہیں۔ تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک ایک ہزار کا بھی فیصلہ نہیں کیا جائے گا بلکہ دونوں کی گواہی رد ہو جائے گی۔ ایک ہزار اگر چہ دو ہزار میں داخل ہے اس لئے دوسرے گواہ نے دو ہزار کی گواہی دی تو معنوی طور پر گویا کہ ایک ہزار کی بھی گواہی دی اس لئے ایک ہزار پر دو گواہ ہو گئے۔ لیکن لفظی طور پر ایک ہزار اور دو ہزار الگ الگ الفاظ ہیں اس لئے لفظی طور پر دونوں گواہوں کے اتفاق نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے دونوں گواہ رو ہو جائیں گے۔ کیونکہ امام ابو حنیفہ کا اصول یہ ہے کہ معنی کے ساتھ الفاظ میں بھی دونوں گواہ متفق ہوں۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک ایک ہزار پر فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ لفظ کے اعتبار سے مختلف ہے لیکن معنی کے اعتبار سے دونوں گواہ ایک ہزار پر متفق ہیں۔ کیونکہ دو ہزار کی گواہی میں ایک ہزار داخل
(33) Agreement of the two witnesses in wording and meaning is required according to Abu Hanifa. So if one testifies to one thousand and the other to two thousand, their testimony is not accepted according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: it is accepted for one thousand. That is, agreement is required in both wording and meaning according to Imam Abu Hanifa. If one witness testifies to one thousand and the other to two thousand, their testimony is not accepted according to Abu Hanifa, but the Sahibayn say it is accepted for one thousand. Explanation: A man claimed that another owed him two thousand dirhams. One witness testified to one thousand, the other to two thousand. According to Abu Hanifa, even one thousand is not decided; both testimonies are rejected. One thousand is included in two thousand, so the second witness, by testifying to two thousand, effectively testified to one thousand as well, so there are two witnesses for one thousand in meaning. But in wording, one thousand and two thousand are different, so due to lack of agreement in wording, both are rejected according to Abu Hanifa's principle that witnesses must agree in both meaning and wording. According to the Sahibayn, judgment is given for one thousand because although they differ in wording, they agree in meaning, as one thousand is included in two thousand.
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents a known intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the requirement of agreement between witnesses. The scenario: a plaintiff claims a debt of two thousand dirhams; one witness testifies to one thousand, the other to two thousand. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that testimony must agree in both lafz (wording) and ma'na (meaning) for it to be accepted. Since one said 'one thousand' and the other 'two thousand,' the words differ, so the testimony is rejected entirely — even the lesser amount cannot be established. The reasoning: although the two thousand includes one thousand, the different verbal expressions prevent the necessary concurrence. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree: they require agreement only in meaning, not wording. Since the lesser amount is contained in the greater, the witnesses agree in meaning on one thousand, so the judgment is given for one thousand. The practical consequence is that under Abu Hanifa's view, the entire claim fails, while under the Sahibayn, the claim succeeds for one thousand. The relied-upon position in the school is often the Sahibayn's view, as it is more practical and avoids total loss of the claim.

Key Terms
لفظ (lafz): The exact words uttered by the witness.
معنی (ma'na): The intended meaning or substance of the testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens if one witness testifies to 1000 dirhams and another to 2000 dirhams?
A) The testimony is accepted for the smaller amount
B) The testimony is accepted for the larger amount
C) The testimony is rejected entirely
D) The judge decides the amount

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the relied-upon position is that witnesses need only agree in meaning, not identical wording, so if one testifies to a smaller amount implied by another's larger amount, the claim succeeds for the smaller amount.

When Witnesses Disagree: Wording vs. Meaning
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witness testimony agreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding witness agreement, and apply the mufta bihi position to a testimony conflict scenario.

Core Idea
When witnesses differ in wording but agree in meaning, Abu Hanifa rejects both; the Sahibayn accept the lower amount.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on witness testimony requirements. The core question is whether witnesses must use identical words or whether substantive agreement suffices. Imam Abu Hanifa insists on both, while his two disciples, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, prioritize meaning over literal wording. Understanding this difference is essential for applying Hanafi procedural law correctly.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and positions
Describe the hypothetical: one witness says 1000, the other says 2000. Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling (reject both) and the Sahibayn's ruling (accept 1000).
2
Analyze the reasoning
Understand why Abu Hanifa requires exact wording (to avoid doubt) and why the Sahibayn accept agreement in meaning (since 1000 is included in 2000).
The inclusion principle is key.
3
Examine the supporting evidence
Look at the athar of Shuraih, cited by the Sahibayn, where he accepted the lower amount when witnesses differed on ten and twenty.
This is a dalil naqli (narrative proof).
4
Determine the practical consequence
Apply the difference: under Abu Hanifa the case is dismissed; under the Sahibayn a partial payment is ordered.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in later Hanafi practice is that of the Sahibayn, because it is more practical and supported by the athar.
The commentary inclines towards the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

It is required that the two witnesses agree in wording and meaning according to Abu Hanifa. If one witnesses for a thousand and the other for two thousand, their testimony is not accepted according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: it is accepted for one thousand. A man claimed that another owed him two thousand dirhams. One witness testified for one thousand, the other for two thousand. According to Abu Hanifa, even one thousand will not be decreed; both testimonies are rejected. The reasoning: although one thousand is included within two thousand, so in meaning the witnesses agree on one thousand, but the words differ. Abu Hanifa requires agreement in both wording and meaning. The Sahibayn decree one thousand because the witnesses agree in meaning. An athar: Shuraih said about two differing witnesses, one for twenty, the other for ten: 'The ten is taken.'
Source pages p. 162

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The core issue is whether witnesses must testify using exactly the same words or whether agreement in substance suffices. Imam Abu Hanifa requires both verbal and substantive agreement; if one says 'a thousand' and the other 'two thousand', the testimony is rejected entirely because the words differ, even though one thousand is included in two thousand. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider substantive agreement sufficient: since the witnesses agree on at least one thousand, the court can decide on one thousand. They support their view with the practice of the early judge Shuraih, who in a similar case accepted the lower amount. The practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa, the court would dismiss the case for lack of valid testimony; under the Sahibayn, the defendant would be ordered to pay the lower amount.

Key Terms
اللفظ (al-lafz): The actual wording used by the witness in testimony.
المعنى (al-ma'na): The substantive meaning or content of the testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The court orders payment of 1500

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the operative ruling is that witnesses need only agree in meaning; the doctrine of precise wording (Abu Hanifa's view) is not applied in practice.

Testimony When Witnesses Disagree on Amount
Ruling on testimony when witnesses differ and the lesser is included in the greater

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when witnesses testify to different amounts and the lesser is contained in the greater, and apply it to court scenarios.

Core Idea
When witnesses differ but the lesser is included in the greater, the court decrees the common amount.

This lesson addresses a common courtroom scenario: two witnesses testify, one says 1000, the other says 1500. The plaintiff claims 1500. How does the court decide? The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the wording of the testimony. Let's explore the reasoning and the exact rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the plaintiff's claim
First, note what the plaintiff is claiming. Here, the plaintiff claims 1500 dirhams.
2
Identify each witness's testimony
Witness A testifies to 1000. Witness B testifies to 1500.
Witness B's testimony includes the 1000 plus an extra 500.
3
Determine the common amount
Look for the amount both witnesses explicitly state in their wording. Both say '1000'. The extra 500 is only stated by one witness.
Witness A says '1000'; witness B says '1000' as part of '1500'.
4
Apply the Hanafi rule
The court decrees the amount on which both witnesses agree in wording. Here, that is 1000. The additional 500 is unproven because only one witness testifies to it.
This is consistent with Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.
5
State the final ruling
The court will decide 1000 dirhams in favor of the plaintiff.
The plaintiff still receives something, but only what is mutually corroborated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۴۳] (۳۴) وان شهد أحدهما بألف والآخر بألف وخمس مائة والمدعى يدعى ألفا وخمس مائة قبلت شهادتهما بألف. مدعی نے دعوی کیا کہ میرے فلاں پر ایک ہزار پانچ سو درہم ہیں۔ اس پر ایک گواہ نے گواہی دی کہ ایک ہزار ہے اور دوسرے نے گواہی دی کہ ایک ہزار پانچ سو ہے تو ایک ہزار کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ لفظ کے اعتبار سے دونوں گواہ ایک ہزار پر متفق ہیں۔ اور دوسرا گواہ الگ سے پانچ سو کی گواہی دے رہا ہے۔ اس لئے ایک ہزار کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔

The plaintiff claimed that the defendant owes him 1500 dirhams. One witness testified for 1000 and the other for 1500. The court will decide on 1000 because both witnesses agree on 1000 in wording. The second witness testified separately for 500, so the common amount 1000 is decided.
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This is a refinement of the previous rule. Here, the lesser amount (1000) is explicitly stated by both witnesses. The second witness adds an extra 500, but that is not corroborated. Since both witnesses say '1000' in wording, they agree on that amount. The court will decree 1000. Note that this ruling is consistent with both Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn because the wording agrees on 1000. The additional 500 is not proven because only one witness testifies to it.

Key Terms

ألف (alf): One thousand (dirhams in the context).

8 min
Testimony Accepted for Agreed Amount: Wording vs. Meaning
Ruling on acceptance of differing testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when witnesses differ in amount and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding agreement in wording vs. meaning.

Core Idea
When witnesses differ in quantity, testimony is accepted for the agreed amount; the dispute is whether wording agreement is required or meaning alone suffices.

In this ruling from the Book of Testimony, we encounter a common scenario: two witnesses testify to different amounts of a debt. The Hanafi school provides a clear principle—accept the testimony for the amount on which both agree. But is agreement in wording necessary, or does agreement in meaning suffice? This lesson unpacks the ruling, its proof, and the internal Hanafi debate between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the passage and note the specific claim: one witness testifies to 1000, the other to 1500, and the claimant claims 1500. The ruling: testimony accepted for 1000. Understand why the 1000 is the agreed amount.
The ruling is clear: the common portion is upheld.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The author cites an athar from Shurayh: when two witnesses differed (one said 20, the other 10), Shurayh said 'the ten is taken'. Identify this as the proof (dalil) for the principle.
This athar is a precedent from a prominent judge.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the athar supports the ruling: both witnesses agreed on 10 dirhams in meaning (though wording differed: 'ten' vs 'twenty'). The ruling takes the lesser common amount.
The athar shows agreement in meaning suffices for Shurayh; Abu Hanifa requires wording agreement.
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note the dispute: Imam Abu Hanifa requires the witnesses to agree in both wording and meaning. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) suffice with agreement in meaning alone. Understand the basis of each view.
The dispute hinges on whether the testimony must be precise in expression or flexible in substance.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Apply the difference to a scenario: if one witness says 'I lent 1000' and the other says 'I lent one thousand' (different wording, same meaning), Sahibayn accept; Abu Hanifa would not. Recognize the practical consequence.
The thamarah is the validity of the testimony in such cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۴۳] (۳۴) وان شهد احدهما بالف والآخر بالف وخمس مائة والمدعى يدعى الفا وخمس مائة قبلت شهادتهما بالف (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عـن شـريـح فـي شـاهـديـن يختلفان فشهد احدهما على عشرين والآخر على عشرة قال يوخذ بالعشرة (الف) (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ۸۳ في الشاهد بن مختلفان، ج رابع ص ۱۳۳۵ نمبر۲۰۷۱۳/۲۰۷۱۱) اس اثر میں عشرۃ اور عشرین لفظ کے اعتبار سے متفق نہیں ہیں صرف معنی کے اعتبار سے متفق ہیں پھر بھی دس درہم کا فیصلہ کیا۔ ۱۲۸۴۳ (۳۴) اور اگر ان میں سے ایک نے گواہی دی ایک ہزار کی اور دوسرے نے ایک ہزار پانچ سو کی اور مدعی دعوی کرتا ہے ایک ہزار پانچ سو کا تو دونوں کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی ایک ہزار پر۔ مدعی نے دعوی کیا کہ میرے فلاں پر ایک ہزار پانچ سو درہم ہیں۔ اس پر ایک گواہ نے گواہی دی کہ ایک ہزار ہے اور دوسرے نے گواہی دی کہ ایک ہزار پانچ سو ہے تو ایک ہزار کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔ ے لفظ کے اعتبار سے دونوں گواہ ایک ہزار پر متفق ہیں۔ اور دوسرا گواہ الگ سے پانچ سو کی گواہی دے رہا ہے۔ اس لئے ایک ہزار کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ معنی کے اعتبار سے اور لفظ کے اعتبار سے بھی دونوں گواہ ایک ہزار پر متفق ہیں۔ ان دونوں گواہ لفظ اور معنی کے اعتبار سے متفق ہوں تو گواہی مقبول ہوگی۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک صرف معنی کے اعتبار سے دونوں گواہ متفق ہوں تب بھی گواہی مقبول ہوگی۔
And if one of them testifies to a thousand and the other to a thousand and five hundred, and the claimant claims a thousand and five hundred, their testimony is accepted for a thousand. [There is an effect from Shurayh: 'Two witnesses differed, one testified for twenty, the other for ten; he said: the ten is taken.'] [Urdu commentary explains that the ruling is based on agreement in wording; the Sahibayn consider agreement in meaning sufficient.]
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Book of Testimony. When two witnesses differ in the amount they testify to, the testimony is accepted for the amount on which they agree in wording. Imam Abu Hanifa requires agreement in both wording and meaning, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) suffice with agreement in meaning alone. The athar from Shurayh supports the principle that when witnesses differ, the lesser amount is taken.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court to establish a claim
اختلاف الشاهدين (ikhtilaf al-shahidayn): Difference between two witnesses in the amount or subject of testimony

Key Takeaway
When witnesses differ in the amount of a claim, the testimony is accepted for the common portion they agree on, with an internal Hanafi dispute on whether wording agreement is necessary.

Testimony: Partial Payment Claim Requires Separate Witnesses
Ruling on testimony with one witness claiming payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a witness adds a claim of partial payment after testifying to a debt, and identify the number of witnesses required for each claim.

Core Idea
A partial payment claim is a separate issue needing two witnesses; one witness does not reduce the debt.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in testimony: two witnesses confirm a debt, but one of them also mentions that the debtor paid part of it. The Hanafi rule is clear: the main debt is established by the two witnesses, but the claim of payment is not accepted unless supported by a second witness. This prevents a single witness from unilaterally altering the debt amount.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two claims
The passage presents two distinct claims: the original debt of 1000 dirhams and a subsequent partial payment of 500 dirhams.
These are separate legal facts requiring independent proof.
2
Count witnesses for each claim
For the debt, there are two witnesses (original testifiers). For the payment, only one witness (the same person who added the statement).
3
Apply the witness requirement rule
Hanafi fiqh generally requires two male witnesses (or one male and two females) for financial claims. Since the payment claim has only one witness, it is not established.
The rule is from Quran 2:282.
4
State the outcome
The court judges the debt of 1000 dirhams as proven. The claim of 500 dirhams payment is not heard unless the other witness also testifies to it.
The debt is not reduced by the unsupported statement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۴۴] (۳۵) واذا شهدا بالف وقال احدهما قضاه منها خمس مائة قبلت شهادتهما بالف ولم يسمع قوله انه قضاه منها خمس مائة الا ان يشهد معه الآخر. (Urdu commentary: ان دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ فلاں کا فلاں پر ایک ہزار درہم ہے۔ بعد میں ان میں سے ایک نے یہ بھی گواہی دی لیکن فلاں نے ایک ہزار میں سے پانچ سوادا کر دیا ہے تو ایک ہزار کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا اور پانچ سو درہم کی ادائیگی پر کوئی فیصلہ نہیں ہوگا اور نہ پانچ سو درہم کم ہوگا۔ ایک ہزار پر دو گواہ ہیں۔ اس لئے ایک ہزار کا فیصلہ ہوگا۔ اور اس میں سے پانچ سو ادا کرنے پر صرف ایک گواہ ہے۔ اس لئے پانچ سوکی ادا ئیگی کا فیصلہ نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ ہاں اس گواہ کے ساتھ دوسرا گواہ بھی ہو جائے تو چونکہ اب دو گواہ ہو گئے اس لئے پانچ سوکی ادائیگی کا فیصلہ کیا جائے گا)
And if both testify for a thousand and one of them says: 'He paid from it five hundred,' their testimony is accepted for a thousand, and his statement that he paid from it five hundred is not heard unless the other testifies with him. [Urdu commentary: The two witnesses testified that the defendant owes the claimant a thousand dirhams. Later, one of them also testified that the defendant paid five hundred from it. So judgment is given for a thousand, and there is no decision regarding the payment of five hundred, nor will the thousand be reduced. For the thousand there are two witnesses, so judgment is given for a thousand. For the payment of five hundred, there is only one witness, so no judgment is given. Yes, if another witness joins him, then there would be two witnesses, so judgment would be given for the payment of five hundred.]
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This ruling addresses when a witness adds a statement about partial payment after testifying about the debt. Since there are two witnesses for the thousand, the testimony for the thousand is accepted. But the claim of payment has only one witness, so it is not accepted unless another witness joins. This is a straightforward application of the principle that established claims require two witnesses, and partial payment is a separate claim.

Key Terms
قضاه (qada): He paid it (past tense)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Both testimonies are rejected
C) The judgment is for 1000, and the payment claim is not heard unless joined by another witness
D) The payment is accepted because it is part of the same testimony

Key Takeaway
A partial payment claim is a separate issue that requires its own two witnesses; a single witness's statement does not reduce the proven debt.

Ethical Guidance for Witnesses: Withholding Testimony to Prevent Injustice
Ethical guidance for a witness aware of partial payment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended conduct for a witness who knows of partial payment and explain how it prevents injustice.

Core Idea
A witness should not testify for the full debt if he knows part has been paid, until the claimant admits it.

Sometimes a witness knows that part of a claimed debt has already been paid, but that knowledge comes from sources that may not be legally conclusive. This lesson teaches the ethical response: the witness should withhold testimony on the full amount until the claimant acknowledges the partial payment, thereby protecting the defendant from an unfair burden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the witness's knowledge
The witness knows that a portion of the debt has been paid, but this is not yet confirmed by the claimant's admission.
Knowledge can come from personal observation or reliable information.
2
Recognize the legal limitation
A single witness's testimony about payment is not sufficient to legally establish the payment. Therefore, the payment remains unproven in court.
In Hanafi fiqh, two witnesses or one witness plus an oath are needed to prove payment.
3
Apply the recommended action
The witness should not testify for the full debt. Instead, he should wait until the claimant admits to receiving the partial payment.
This is a recommended (sunnah) ethical conduct, not an obligation.
4
Understand the rationale
By refusing to testify for the full amount, the witness prevents the defendant from being ordered to pay a debt that has already been partially satisfied.
The goal is to avoid injustice and uphold fairness in testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۴۵] (۳۶) وينبغي للشاهد اذا علم ذلك ان لا يشهد بالف حتى يقر المدعى انه قبض خمس مائة. (Urdu commentary: انش دو گواہوں میں سے ایک جانتا تھا کہ ایک ہزار میں سے پانچ سو مدعی کو ادا کر دیا گیا ہے۔ لیکن اس پر ایک گواہی کی وجہ سے ادا کرنے کی بات نہیں چلے گی۔ تو ایسی صورت میں اس کو چاہئے کہ جب تک پانچ سو وصول کرنے کا لوگوں کے سامنے اقرار نہ کرے ایک ہزار پر گواہی نہ دے تا کہ مدعی علیہ کو صرف پانچ سو ہی ادا کرنا پڑے۔)
And it is appropriate for the witness, when he knows that, not to testify for a thousand until the claimant admits that he received five hundred. [Urdu commentary: One of the two witnesses knew that five hundred of the thousand had been paid to the claimant. But because of the rule that a single witness's statement about payment is not accepted, the payment claim will not be established. In such a situation, the witness should not testify for the thousand until the claimant publicly admits to receiving the five hundred, so that the defendant only has to pay five hundred.]
Source pages p. 163

Commentary
This is a recommendation (adab) for the witness. If he knows that part of the debt has been paid, he should not testify for the full amount until the claimant acknowledges the payment, to avoid injustice to the defendant. The witness should not inadvertently cause the defendant to pay a debt that has already been partially discharged.

Key Terms
ينبغي (yanbaghi): It is appropriate/recommended

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

C) Testify only for the unpaid portion
D) Inform the judge without testifying

Key Takeaway
A witness's ethical duty is to prevent injustice by not testifying for a full debt when partial payment is known, until the claimant admits it.
