Conflicting Testimony on Time and Place Rejected
Ruling when witnesses contradict on location of event

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why contradictory testimony on a material fact (like location) is rejected in Hanafi law, and apply the ruling to scenarios of irreconcilable witness statements.

Core Idea
If two sets of witnesses contradict each other on a material fact making the event impossible, both testimonies are rejected.

In this lesson, we examine a key principle in Hanafi testimony law: when witnesses disagree on an essential fact such as the location of a crime, and the event cannot have occurred in both places, their testimony becomes inadmissible. This ruling is not about doubting the honesty of the witnesses but about the impossibility of reconciling their statements. We will look at a classic example and the proof from the early salaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage and identify the two sets of witnesses and what they claim. Note the contradictory elements: location (Mecca vs Kufa) and same time.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that both testimonies are rejected (lam yuqbal al-shahadatayn). Understand that this is a definitive rejection, not a suspension.
3
Understand the rationale
The contradiction is on a material fact that makes the event physically impossible (a person cannot be in two distant places simultaneously). Therefore, the testimony is inherently unreliable.
4
Examine the dalil
The proof is an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: four witnesses differed on the location of an alleged adultery (Kufa vs Basra), and the hadd punishment was dropped. This shows that such contradiction invalidates the testimony.
The athar is mursal but sufficient for this principle in Hanafi law.
5
Apply the principle
Consider other scenarios: contradiction on time alone, contradiction on non-material details. Distinguish which contradictions nullify testimony and which do not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۴۶] (۳۷) واذا شهد شاهدان ان زیدا قتل يوم النحر بمكة وشهد آخران انه قتل يوم النحر بالكوفة واجتمعوا عند الحاكم لم يقبل الشهادتين. (Urdu commentary: ر یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ فیصلہ سے پہلے گواہوں میں اختلاف ہو جائے تو دونوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ اب صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ دو گواہوں نے گاہی دی کہ زید دسویں ذی الحجہ کو مکہ مکرمہ میں قتل کیا گیا ہے۔ ابھی اس پر فیصلہ بھی نہیں کیا گیا تھا کہ دوسرے دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ زید دسویں ذی الحجہ کو کوفے میں قتل کیا گیا ہے۔ اب ایک ہی آدمی ایک ہی تاریخ میں دو مختلف جگہوں پر قتل کیا جائے اور دونوں جگہیں اتنی دور ہیں کہ دونوں جگہوں پر ہونا نا ممکن ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں قسم کے گواہ مردود ہو جائیں گے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهيم في اربعة شهدوا على امرأة بالزنا ثم اختلفوا في الموضع، فقال بعضهم بالكوفة وقال بالبصرة قال يدراء عنهم جميع ا(الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شهادة اربعة على امرأة بالزنا واختلاأنهم في الموضع ، ج سابع ،ص ۱۳۳۴ نمبر ۱۳۳۸۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جگہ کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے گواہی رد ہوگئی ہے۔)
And if two witnesses testify that Zayd was killed on the Day of Sacrifice in Mecca, and two others testify that he was killed on the Day of Sacrifice in Kufa, and they all gather before the judge, both testimonies are not accepted. [Urdu commentary: This issue is based on the principle that if witnesses differ before judgment, both testimonies are not accepted. Here, two witnesses say Zayd was killed in Mecca on 10th Dhul Hijjah, and two others say in Kufa on the same day. It is impossible for a person to be in two distant places at the same time. Therefore, both groups of witnesses are rejected. There is an effect from Ibrahim: Four witnesses testified against a woman for adultery, then differed on the location—some said Kufa, some said Basra. He said: The hadd is dropped from all of them.]
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This ruling deals with contradictory testimony on a factual impossibility. Since the two sets of witnesses contradict each other on a material point (location) that makes the event impossible, both testimonies are rejected. The principle is that if witnesses cannot agree on a fact that is impossible to reconcile, their testimony is unreliable. This is supported by an athar from Ibrahim where witnesses differed on the place of adultery, leading to the dropping of the hadd punishment.

Key Terms
اختلاف الشهادة (ikhtilaf al-shahada): Contradiction between testimonies on a essential fact

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Two witnesses testify that Zayd was killed in Mecca on Eid al-Adha, and two others testify that he was killed in Kufa on the same day. They all appear before the judge. What is the ruling?
A) The judge accepts the first pair
B) The judge accepts the second pair
C) Both testimonies are accepted and the judge averages the locations
D) Both testimonies are rejected

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, if witnesses contradict each other on a material fact that makes the event physically impossible, their testimony is rejected regardless of their credibility.

Testimony After Judgment: The Rule of Finality
Ruling on subsequent contradictory testimony after judgment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting later contradictory testimony after a judgment and explain the rationale of judicial finality.

Core Idea
Once judgment is passed, later contradictory testimony cannot overturn it.

This lesson addresses a simple but critical procedural rule: when two conflicting testimonies arise sequentially, the one that leads to a final judgment bars the other. The principle ensures that judicial decisions are not endlessly challenged, maintaining stability in legal outcomes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two witnesses testify first, judgment is passed; later another set gives contradictory testimony.
The first testimony was accepted and a judgment was made.
2
State the ruling
The later testimony is not accepted (ghayr maqbul).
This is the core holding of the passage.
3
Understand the rationale
The ruling upholds the finality of judicial decisions (qada al-qudat la yunqad).
Even if the later testimony is true, it cannot reverse a completed judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۴۷] (۳۸) فان سبقت احديهما وقضى بها ثم حضرت الأخرى لم تقبل الشهادة. (Urdu commentary: انتری دو آدمیوں نے پہلے گواہی دی کہ مکہ میں قتل کیا گیا ہے۔ اور اس پر فیصلہ کر دیا گیا۔ بعد میں دو گواہ آئے اور گواہی دی کہ اس کو بصرہ میں قتل کیا ہے تو چونکہ پہلی گواہی پر فیصلہ ہو چکا ہے اس لئے دوسری گواہی کی وجہ سے پہلے فیصلہ کو توڑ نہیں جائے گا۔)
If one of the two (testimonies) precedes and judgment is passed with it, then the other arrives, the testimony is not accepted. [Urdu commentary: Two people first testified that he was killed in Mecca, and judgment was passed. Later, two witnesses came and testified that he was killed in Basra. Since judgment has already been passed on the first testimony, the second testimony cannot break the first judgment.]
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This ruling prevents reopening a case after a final judgment has been made. The first testimony was accepted and judgment based on it was implemented. The later contradictory testimony is disregarded to maintain the finality of judgments. This is a principle of judicial stability (qada al-qudat la yunqad).

Key Terms
قضى بها (qada biha): Judgment was passed based on that testimony

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is accepted and the judgment is overturned
B) It is accepted and both judgments apply
C) It is not accepted because the case is already decided
D) It is accepted only if the first witnesses retract

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle of judicial finality bars acceptance of later contradictory testimony after a judgment is rendered.

Witness Conduct When Partial Payment Is Known
Advises a witness to withhold testimony until partial payment is acknowledged

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the proper conduct of a witness in a debt case where partial payment is known and explain the reason for withholding testimony until acknowledgment.

Core Idea
A witness must not testify to a full debt if part is paid, to prevent injustice to the defendant.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Hanafi school on a specific ethical duty of a witness. When a witness knows that part of a debt has already been paid to the plaintiff, he must not testify to the full amount unless the plaintiff first admits the partial payment. This principle safeguards the defendant from being ordered to pay more than he owes. We will unpack the ruling and its rationale, and apply it to practical scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Read the passage and identify the factual situation: a witness knows that part of a debt has been repaid to the plaintiff, but the plaintiff demands the full amount in court.
The key is the witness's knowledge of partial payment.
2
Extract the ruling
State the ruling: the witness should not testify for the full debt until the plaintiff acknowledges the receipt of the partial payment.
The ruling is an ethical obligation (wajib) to withhold testimony.
3
Understand the rationale
The reason is to avoid injustice: testifying to the full amount would cause the defendant to be ordered to pay what was already paid, harming the defendant.
The principle is 'la darar wa la dirar' (no harm shall be inflicted or reciprocated).
4
Apply to a similar case
Consider a scenario where a witness knows a debt of 1000 dirhams was incurred, but 300 have been repaid. The witness should not testify for 1000 until the plaintiff admits the 300 repayment.
The same ruling applies regardless of the amount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وينبغي للشاهد اذا علم ذلك ان لا يشهد بالف حتى يقر المدعى انه قبض خمس مائة اور مناسب ہے گواہ کے لئے کہ اگر ادا کرنے کو جانے تو ہزار کی گواہی نہ دے یہاں تک کہ مدعی اقرار کرے کہ اس نے پانچ سو پر قبضہ کیا ہے۔ انش دو گواہوں میں سے ایک جانتا تھا کہ ایک ہزار میں سے پانچ سو مدعی کو ادا کر دیا گیا ہے۔ لیکن اس پر ایک گواہی کی وجہ سے ادا کرنے کی بات نہیں چلے گی۔ تو ایسی صورت میں اس کو چاہئے کہ جب تک پانچ سو وصول کرنے کا لوگوں کے سامنے اقرار نہ کرے ایک ہزار پر گواہی نہ دے تا کہ مدعی علیہ کو صرف پانچ سو ہی ادا کرنا پڑے۔
It is proper for the witness, if he knows that, not to testify with one thousand until the plaintiff admits that he received five hundred. And it is appropriate for the witness that if he knows of the payment, he should not testify for a thousand until the plaintiff admits that he has taken possession of five hundred. For example, one of the two witnesses knew that five hundred of the thousand had been paid to the plaintiff, but due to the testimony of one, the matter of payment will not proceed. So in such a case, he should not testify for a thousand until the plaintiff publicly admits to receiving the five hundred, so that the defendant only has to pay five hundred.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement concerning the ethical conduct of a witness in debt cases. According to the Hanafi school, if a witness knows that part of the debt has already been paid to the plaintiff, he should not testify for the full amount unless the plaintiff acknowledges the partial payment. The reason is that testimony is meant to establish the truth; testifying to the full amount would cause injustice to the defendant, who would then be ordered to pay the entire sum despite partial payment. The witness must ensure that the plaintiff first admits the receipt of the partial payment, so the defendant is only liable for the remaining balance. This is based on the principle of avoiding harm and upholding justice.

Key Terms
شاهد (shāhid): A person who gives testimony in court; a witness.
اقرار (iqrār): Acknowledgment or admission by a party, especially of a debt or receipt of payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a witness do if he knows that the plaintiff has already received part of the debt for which he is asked to testify?
A) Testify to the full debt amount
B) Refuse to testify altogether
C) Testify only after the plaintiff acknowledges the partial payment
D) Inform the judge privately of the partial payment

Key Takeaway
A witness with knowledge of partial payment must withhold full testimony until the plaintiff acknowledges the payment, to prevent an unjust judgment.

Shahadat — Testimony

Contradictory Testimonies on Place: Both Rejected
Conflicting testimonies about place led to both being rejected

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that contradictory testimonies on a material fact (e.g., place) are both rejected before judgment and explain the evidence from the early scholars.

Core Idea
Contradictory testimonies cancel each other; both are invalid if they conflict on essential facts like place.

What happens when two sets of trustworthy witnesses give perfectly conflicting accounts of the same event? The Hanafi school addresses this with a clear rule: if the contradiction is on a material fact (like the place of a death) and emerges before the judge issues a ruling, both testimonies are thrown out. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its rationale, and the proof from the noble successor Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
Read the source carefully: two witnesses claim Zaid was killed in Makkah on the day of Nahr; two others claim he was killed in Kufa on the same day. They appear before the same judge. Note the key element: the same event, same time, but different places.
The distance between Makkah and Kufa makes it impossible for Zaid to be in both places at once.
2
State the Hanafi ruling
The judge rejects both testimonies. Neither set is accepted. The hukm level is batil (invalid). This is the mufta bihi position.
Apply the principle: irreconcilable contradiction before judgment voids all testimonies.
3
Understand the principle
The contradiction indicates that at least one set of witnesses is lying or mistaken. Since we cannot determine which one is false, both must be rejected to avoid basing a judgment on false evidence.
This preserves the integrity of the court and upholds the higher objective of justice.
4
Examine the evidence (dalīl)
The source cites an athar from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i: four witnesses testified against a woman for zina, then disagreed on the place (some said Kufa, some Basra). Ibrahim ruled that the hadd punishment is averted from all of them. This shows that inconsistency on place voids testimony by analogy.
The athar is zannī in transmission (thubūt) but its meaning (dalāla) is clear for this ruling.
5
Note cross-madhhabs differences
Some other schools might accept one testimony if there is a possibility of reconciliation (e.g., that Zaid was moved). The Hanafi school insists on rejection because the contradiction is essential and irreconcilable.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilāf) is that in Hanafi courts both witnesses are disqualified, while in other schools one might be accepted with additional verification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا شهد شاهدان ان زيدا قتل يوم النحر بمكة وشهد آخران انه قتل يوم النحر بالكوفة واجتمعوا عند الحاكم لم يقبل الشهادتين اگر دو آدمیوں نے گواہی دی کہ زید قتل کیا گیا ہے بقر عید کے دن مکے میں اور دوسرے دو نے گواہی دی کہ وہ قتل کیا گیا ہے بقر عید کے دن کوفے میں ۔ اور سب حاکم کے پاس جمع ہو گئے تو دونوں گواہیاں قبول نہیں کی جائیں گی۔ ر یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ فیصلہ سے پہلے گواہوں میں اختلاف ہو جائے تو دونوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ اب صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ زید دسویں ذی الحجہ کو مکہ مکرمہ میں قتل کیا گیا ہے۔ ابھی اس پر فیصلہ بھی نہیں کیا گیا تھا کہ دوسرے دو گواہوں نے گواہی دی کہ زید دسویں ذی الحجہ کو کوفے میں قتل کیا گیا ہے۔ اب ایک ہی آدمی ایک ہی تاریخ میں دو مختلف جگہوں پر قتل کیا جائے اور دونوں جگہیں اتنی دور ہیں کہ دونوں جگہوں پر ہونا نا ممکن ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں قسم کے گواہ مردود ہو جائیں گے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهيم في اربعة شهدوا على امرأة بالزنا ثم اختلفوا في الموضع، فقال بعضهم بالكوفة وقال بالبصرة قال يدراء عنهم جميعا (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شهادة اربعة على امرأة بالزنا واختلاأنهم في الموضع، ج سابع،ص ۱۳۳۴ نمبر ۱۳۳۸۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جگہ کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے گواہی رد ہوگئی ہے۔
And if two witnesses testify that Zaid was killed on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) in Makkah, and another two testify that he was killed on the day of Nahr in Kufa, and they all gather before the judge, the two testimonies are not accepted. If two men testified that Zaid was killed on the day of Eid-ul-Adha in Makkah, and two others testified that he was killed on the same day in Kufa, and all came before the judge, both testimonies are not accepted. This issue is based on the principle that if witnesses differ before judgment, both testimonies are not accepted. Now the case is that two witnesses testified that Zaid was killed on 10th Dhul Hijjah in Makkah, and before judgment, another two testified that he was killed on 10th Dhul Hijjah in Kufa. Since a single person cannot be killed in two distant places at the same time, both sets of witnesses are rejected. There is an athar (from Ibrahim): Four witnesses testified against a woman for zina, then they differed about the place; some said in Kufa, some said in Basra. He said: the hadd punishment is averted from all of them. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq). This athar shows that due to the difference in place, the testimony is rejected.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on contradictory testimonies and provides its evidence. According to Hanafi law, if two sets of witnesses give contradictory testimonies on the same event—such as the same death occurring in two different cities too distant for the person to be in both—then both testimonies are invalid. The reason is that the contradiction indicates at least one set is false, and since neither can be verified, both are rejected. The ruling is supported by an athar (narration) from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, who ruled that if four witnesses for zina differ on the location, the hadd penalty is dropped. This demonstrates that inconsistency in testimony voids it. The key principle is that testimonies must be consistent in essential facts; otherwise, they lose credibility.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony given in court by a witness.
اختلاف (ikhtilāf): Disagreement or contradiction among witnesses on material facts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The judge accepts the first testimony
B) Both testimonies are accepted and the judge chooses one
C) Both testimonies are rejected
D) The judge allows the witnesses to reconcile

Key Takeaway
Irreconcilable contradiction on a material fact (like place) before judgment makes both testimonies invalid in Hanafi law.

Later Testimony After Judgment Not Accepted
Rules that a subsequent contradictory testimony is not accepted if judgment has already been passed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on the finality of a judicial judgment when contradictory testimony appears later and identify the hadith evidence supporting it.

Core Idea
Once a judge passes judgment, later contradictory testimony cannot overturn it—finality protects legal certainty.

This lesson completes the discussion on contradictory testimony by focusing on timing. If one testimony is presented first and the judge rules, a later contradictory testimony is rejected even if it would have been preferred earlier. The principle of finality of judgment protects the authority of the court and prevents endless litigation. We will examine the textual evidence—a mursal hadith and an athar—that the Hanafi school relies upon.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi ruling: if one testimony precedes and judgment is passed, a later contradictory testimony is not accepted and cannot reverse the judgment.
This applies even if the later testimony is stronger or more numerous.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the two evidences cited: a mursal hadith from Ibn al-Musayyab and an athar from al-Thawri.
The hadith is mursal, but Hanafis accept it when supported by practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each evidence proves the rule. The hadith prioritizes the first testimony; the athar confirms finality after judgment.
The key phrase 'then the ruling is executed' from the athar.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Recognize that some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) might allow reopening the case if the later testimony is compelling, but the Hanafi position prioritizes finality.
The ikhtilaf is legitimate and based on different weight given to legal stability vs. truth-seeking.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand that the Hanafi school relies on the principle that a final judgment brings certainty (qaḍā' qāṭiʿ). The two evidences are treated as sufficient, and later testimony is rejected to prevent endless litigation.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان سبقت احديهما وقضى بها ثم حضرت الأخرى لم تقبل الشهادة. پس اگر دو میں سے ایک کی گواہی پہلے ہو گئی اور اس کا فیصلہ ہو گیا پھر دوسرے حاضر ہوئے تو گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی۔ انتری دو آدمیوں نے پہلے گواہی دی کہ مکہ میں قتل کیا گیا ہے۔ اور اس پر فیصلہ کر دیا گیا۔ بعد میں دو گواہ آئے اور گواہی دی کہ اس کو بصرہ میں قتل کیا ہے تو چونکہ پہلی گواہی پر فیصلہ ہو چکا ہے اس لئے دوسری گواہی کی وجہ سے پہلے فیصلہ کو توڑ نہیں جائے گا۔ پہلی گواہی کو تر جیح ہوگئی ہے کہ اس پر فیصلہ ہو گیا ہے اس لئے دوسری گواہی کی وجہ سے پہلی گواہی تو ڑی نہیں جائے گی۔ حدیث مرسل عن ابن المسيب قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم اذا شهد الرجل بشهادتين قبلت الاولى وتركت الآخرة، وانزل منزلة الغلام (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل يشهد بشهادة ثم يشهد بخلافها، ج ثامن، ص 1352 نمبر 15508) اس حدیث مرسل میں ہے کہ آدمی نے دو مرتبہ گواہی دی تو پہلی گواہی مقبول ہوگی اور دوسری رد کر دی جائے گی۔ اور پہلے پر فیصلہ ہو گیا تو بدرجہ اولی وہ مقبول ہوگی اور دوسری گواہی مردود ہوگی۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن الشورى في رجل اشهد على شهادته رجلا فقضى القاضي بشهادته ثم جاء الشاهد الذي شهد على شهادته فقال لم اشهد بشيء قال يقول اذا قضى القاضى مضى الحكم (مصنف بد الرزاق، باب الشاهد مرجع عن شهادته او یشھد ثم سجد ، ج ثامن، ص 1353، نمبر 15513) اس اثر میں ہے کہ پہلی گواہی پر قاضی کا فیصلہ ہو گیا اب اس کو دوسری گواہی سے رد نہیں کیا جاسکتا۔
If one of them (the testimonies) preceded and judgment was passed upon it, then the other appears, the testimony is not accepted. So if one of the two testimonies came first and judgment was given, then the others came, their testimony will not be accepted. For example, two men first testified that the killing happened in Makkah, and judgment was given. Later two witnesses came and testified that he was killed in Basra. Since judgment has already been passed on the first testimony, the second testimony cannot overturn the first judgment. The first testimony is given precedence because judgment was passed on it, so the second testimony cannot break the first. A mursal hadith: from Ibn al-Musayyab that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: When a man gives two testimonies, the first is accepted and the latter is left, and he is lowered to the level of a boy. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq). In this mursal hadith, if a man gives testimony twice, the first is accepted and the second rejected. And if judgment was passed on the first, then all the more it is accepted and the second is rejected. There is also an athar from al-Thawri about a man who made someone a witness to his testimony, then the judge passed judgment on his testimony, then the witness who was made a witness came and said: I did not testify anything. Al-Thawri said: When the judge has passed judgment, the ruling is executed. (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq). This athar indicates that once judgment is given, it cannot be overturned by subsequent testimony.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage builds on the previous rule by considering the timing of contradictory testimonies. If one testimony is presented first and the judge passes judgment, a later contradictory testimony is not accepted even if it would have invalidated the first had it come earlier. The reason is the finality of judgment: once the judge has ruled, the matter is settled to preserve legal stability. The passage cites two evidences: a mursal hadith from Ibn al-Musayyab that the first testimony is accepted and the second left aside, and an athar from al-Thawri that a judgment stands even if the witness later retracts. In Hanafi fiqh, this is the established position: a judgment based on testimony cannot be reversed by later contradictory evidence. This protects the authority of the court and prevents endless litigation.

Key Terms
قضاء (qaḍā'): Judgment or judicial decision by a judge
مرسل (mursal): A hadith where the Companion is omitted from the chain

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The new testimony is accepted and the case is retried
B) The new testimony is accepted only if it is from more reliable witnesses
C) The new testimony is not accepted because the judgment is final
D) The judge compares the testimonies and decides which is stronger

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a final judgment based on testimony is conclusive and cannot be overturned by later contradictory testimony, ensuring legal stability and finality.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate

Judge Does Not Accept Unsubstantiated Impugning of Witness
Statement on the inadmissibility of general jarh without specification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on accepting jarh (impugning of witnesses) and apply it to distinguish between valid and invalid challenges.

Core Idea
A general accusation of witness corruption is ignored; only specific, proven impugning matters.

In a courtroom, a litigant might try to disqualify a witness by claiming they are sinful. But Islam presumes Muslims are just. This lesson explains the Hanafi rule that a judge must disregard vague allegations and only act when the challenger specifies a sin and provides proof. We'll examine the hadith that underpins this rule and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of jarh
Distinguish between general (mutlaq) impugning (e.g., 'this witness is fasiq' without cause) and specific (muqayyad) impugning (e.g., 'he drank wine and I have witnesses'). The judge rejects the former and considers the latter with proof.
General jarh is also called 'jarh bi ghayri sabab'.
2
Locate the hadith evidence
The source cites the hadith: 'Muslims are just to one another, except one who has been subjected to hadd for slander.' This is from Amr ibn Shu'ayb's narration.
The hadith is ahad but accepted as proof in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyse how the hadith supports the ruling
The hadith establishes a default of 'adalah (justice) for Muslims. A general accusation does not overturn this default. Only when a specific sin is proven (especially one incurring hadd) can the witness be deemed fasiq and rejected.
The word 'illā (except) indicates the only way to break the default.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools may allow a judge to investigate general challenges or require less specificity. The Hanafi school insists on precise specification to protect witnesses from frivolous attacks.
This difference affects procedural efficiency.
5
Apply the ruling to a concrete scenario
If a litigant says 'the witness is a thief' without detailing when or where, the judge ignores it. But if the litigant says 'he stole at noon from the shop and here are two witnesses,' the judge investigates and may disqualify if proved.
The proof required could be witnesses or other evidence accepted in court.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يسمع القاضى الشهادة على جرح ولا نفى ولا يحكم بذلك الا ما استحق عليه. اور قاضی نہ سنے گواہی جرح پر اور نہ اس کا حکم لگائے مگر جس کا استحقاق ثابت ہو جائے۔ ار مدعی علیہ مدعی کے گواہ کے بارے میں یوں گواہی دلوائے کہ یہ گواہ فاسق ہیں۔ اور فاسق ہونے کا کوئی سبب بیان نہ کرے کہ شراب پینے کی وجہ سے یا چوری کرنے کی وجہ سے فاسق ہو گئے ہیں۔ تو ایسے جرح کے سلسلے میں قاضی کوئی توجہ نہ دے، نہ نفی کرے اور نہ اثبات کرے اور نہ فسق کے نفی یا اثبات کا فیصلہ کرے۔ حدیث گزرچکی ہے کہ مسلمان بعض بعض پر عادل ہیں۔ عن عمرو بن شعیب عن ابيه عن جده قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم المسلمون عدول بعضهم على بعض الا محدودا في فرية (مصنف ابن ابی شیبہ 74 من قال لا تجوز شهادته اذا تاب، ج رابع ص 1330، نمبر 20650 ردار قطنی ، کتاب عمر الی ابی موسی اشعری، جلد رابع ص 132 نمبر 4425) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ظاہری طور پر تمام مسلمان عادل ہیں۔ اس لئے صرف یہ کہ دینا کہ فلاں گواہ فاسق ہے اور اس کا سبب نہ بتانا کہ حقوق اللہ یا حقوق العباد توڑنے کی وجہ سے فاسق ہے اس کی طرف توجہ نہیں دی جائے گی۔ اور مدعی کے گواہ مقبول شمار کئے جائیں گے۔ اگر اسباب بتائے بغیر کہے کہ یہ گواہ فاسق ہیں تو ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ فسق سے تو بہ کر چکا ہو اور ابھی عادل بن کر گواہی دینے پیش ہوا ہو۔ جس کی وجہ سے قاضی ان کی گواہی رد نہیں کر سکتا۔ الا ما استحق علیہ : اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جرح مقید کرے تو قاضی اس کی طرف توجہ دیگا۔ مثلا کہے کہ اس نے شراب پیا ہے اور اس پر حد لگانے کا مطالبہ کرے اور اس پر دو گواہ لائے جس کی وجہ سے مدعی کے گواہوں پر حد لگ جائے۔ چونکہ حقوق اللہ توڑنے میں حد لگ گئی اس لئے اب فاسق ہو گیا۔ اس لئے مدعی کے اس گواہ کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی۔ اس صورت میں شراب پینا سبب جتلا کر فسق کا دعوی کیا جو جرح مقید ہے اس
And the judge shall not hear testimony regarding impugning (jarh) nor reject, nor shall he pass judgment upon it except what is established against it. And the judge should not listen to testimony on impugning nor pass judgment regarding it except when liability is proven. For example, the defendant brings witnesses that the plaintiff's witnesses are corrupt (fasiq) without specifying the cause, such as drinking wine or theft. Then the judge pays no attention to such impugning, neither rejecting nor accepting, nor deciding on their corruption. A hadith has passed that Muslims are just to one another. From Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Muslims are just to one another, except one who has been subjected to hadd for slander. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, etc.). This hadith indicates that outwardly all Muslims are just. Therefore, merely saying a witness is corrupt without specifying a cause is not heeded, and the plaintiff's witnesses are accepted. If someone says without specifying causes that these witnesses are fasiq, it is possible that they have repented from corruption and are now just. The judge cannot reject their testimony. The exception "except what is established against it" means that if the impugning is specific, the judge will consider it. For example, he says that the witness drank wine and demands that hadd be imposed on him, and he brings two witnesses to that effect, so that the plaintiff's witnesses are subject to hadd. Since he has violated the rights of Allah (hadd), he becomes fasiq, and his testimony is not accepted. In this case, he has specified the cause of wine drinking, making the impugning specific.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on the admissibility of challenges to a witness's integrity (jarh). According to Hanafi law, a general accusation that a witness is fasiq (sinful) without specifying the particular sin is not entertained by the judge. The reason is that Muslims on the surface are considered just ('udul) based on a hadith that deems Muslims trustworthy witnesses. A vague accusation could be false or the witness might have repented. Therefore, the judge ignores it and accepts the testimony of the challenged witness. However, if the challenger specifies the sin (e.g., drinking wine) and provides proof (like two witnesses) to establish it, then the judge must act: if the specified sin incurs a hadd penalty and it is proven, the witness becomes fasiq and his testimony is rejected. The key distinction is between general (mutlaq) and specific (muqayyad) impugning. This ruling protects witnesses from frivolous attacks while allowing legitimate challenges.

Key Terms
جرح (jarḥ): Impugning or challenging the credibility of a witness, alleging they are not just.
فاسق (fāsiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, rendering their testimony invalid until repentance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi law, when does a judge accept a challenge (jarh) against a witness?
A) Whenever any party claims the witness is fasiq
B) Only when the specific sin is mentioned and proven
C) Only if the witness confesses to being corrupt
D) Never, because all witnesses are considered just

Key Takeaway
A judge must not act on general allegations of witness corruption; only specific, proven impugning can disqualify a witness.

The Qadi's Rule on Unspecified Jarh
Ruling on when a Qadi accepts testimony discrediting a witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that unspecified jarh is not heard by the qadi, explain the proof from hadith, and apply the exception of specified jarh to scenarios involving rights of Allah and rights of people.

Core Idea
A qadi ignores unspecified claims of fisq; only specified jarh with proof can overturn the presumption of uprightness.

This lesson examines a key rule in Hanafi court procedure: the qadi does not accept testimony that merely discredits a witness without specifying the cause. Based on the presumption that all Muslims are upright unless proven otherwise, the school requires the jarh to be specified and proven. We will explore the ruling, its proof, and the practical application through examples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The matn states that the qadi does not hear testimony regarding jarh (discrediting) or nafi (negation) except when a right (istihqaq) is established. Determine the specific prohibition: unspecified jarh is ignored.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'Muslims are upright over each other except one who has been flogged for slander.' This establishes a general presumption of uprightness.
The hadith is quoted in full and referenced to Ibn Abi Shaybah and Darequtni.
3
Understand the Wajh al-Dalalah
The hadith implies that a mere claim of fisq does not overcome the presumption. For the qadi to act, the jarh must be specified (muqayyad) with a cause that can be proven, thus meeting the ‘right’ exception.
See the commentary's discussion on the exception 'illa ma istahaqqa 'alayh'.
4
Apply the Exception
The exception covers specified jarh where the defendant brings proof of a specific cause of fisq, such as drinking wine (rights of Allah) or taking a bribe (rights of people). In such cases, the qadi hears the jarh and rejects the witness's testimony.
The commentary provides two concrete examples to illustrate rights of Allah and rights of people.

طور پر تمام مسلمان عادل ہیں۔ اس لئے صرف یہ کہ دینا کہ فلاں گواہ فاسق ہے اور اس کا سبب نہ بتانا کہ حقوق اللہ یا حقوق العباد توڑنے کی وجہ سے فاسق ہے اس کی طرف توجہ نہیں دی جائے گی۔ اور مدعی کے گواہ مقبول شمار کئے جائیں گے (۲) اگر اسباب بتائے بغیر کہے کہ یہ گواہ فاسق ہیں تو ایسا ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ فسق سے تو بہ کر چکا ہو اور ابھی عادل بن کر گواہی دینے پیش ہوا ہو ۔ جس کی وجہ سے قاضی ان کی گواہی رد نہیں کر سکتا۔ الا ما استحق علیه : اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ جرح مقید کرے تو قاضی اس کی طرف توجہ دیگا۔ مثلا کہے کہ اس نے شراب پیا ہے اور اس پر حد لگانے کا مطالبہ کرے اور اس پر دو گواہ لائے جس کی وجہ سے مدعی کے گواہوں پر حد لگ جائے۔ چونکہ حقوق اللہ توڑنے میں حد لگ گئی اس لئے اب فاسق ہو گیا۔ اس لئے مدعی کے اس گواہ کی گواہی مقبول نہیں ہوگی۔ اس صورت میں شراب پینا سبب جتلا کر فسق کا دعوی کیا جو جرح مقید ہے اس لئے قاضی اس پر توجہ بھی دے گا اور گواہوں کے درد کا فیصلہ بھی کرے گا۔ یہ جرح قاضی کے لئے قابل سماعت ہے۔ حقوق العباد میں جرح مقید کی مثلا : مدعی علیہ نے دعوی کیا کہ میں نے مدعی کے گواہ کو سو درہم دیتے ہیں اور اس پر اتفاق ہوا تھا کہ وہ میرے خلاف گواہی نہیں دے گا۔ اس کے باوجود گواہی دیدی۔ اس لئے مجھے سو درہم واپس دلوائے جائیں۔ اور ان دونوں باتوں پر مدعی علیہ نے گواہ پیش کر دیئے۔ چونکہ رقم واپس کرنے کا مطالبہ ہے اس لئے قاضی کو گواہی کی بنیاد پر رقم واپس کروانے کا حق ہے۔ اور چونکہ رشوت ثابت ہو جائے گی، اس لئے مدعی کے گواہ فاسق کے زمرے میں آجائیں گے اور ان کی گواہی رد ہو جائے گی۔ رقم واپس کروانے کا مطالبہ بندے کی جانب سے ہے اس لئے یہ حقوق العباد میں جرح مقید کی مثال ہوئی۔ الا ما استحق علیه : کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مدعی کے گواہوں پر اللہ کے حقوق توڑنے مثلا زنا کرنے ،شراب پینے یا چوری کرنے کو ثابت کر دیا جائے۔ یا بندے کے حقوق دبانے کو ثابت کر دے تو قاضی اس جرح کو سنے گا اور فسق کی نفی یا اثبات کا فیصلہ بھی کرے گا۔
The qadi does not hear testimony regarding discrediting (jarh) nor regarding negation (nafi), nor does he pass judgment on that, except for what is established as a right (istihqaq). (39) And the qadi should not listen to testimony on jarh nor pass judgment on it except when a right is established. If the defendant brings testimony about the plaintiff's witnesses saying 'these witnesses are fasiq' without mentioning a cause (like drinking wine or stealing), then the qadi pays no attention to such jarh, neither negating nor affirming, nor does he decide on the negation or affirmation of fisq. The hadith has passed that Muslims are upright (udul) over each other. 'Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Muslims are upright over each other, except one who has been flogged for slander.' (Mushaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, etc.) From this hadith it is understood that apparently all Muslims are upright. Therefore merely saying 'so-and-so is fasiq' without giving a cause—that the fisq is due to violating the rights of Allah or the rights of people—is not given attention, and the plaintiff's witnesses are considered acceptable. (2) If he says without giving causes: 'these witnesses are fasiq', it is possible that they have repented from fisq and now come as upright to give testimony, so the qadi cannot reject their testimony. 'Except what is established as a right' (illa ma istahaqqa 'alayh): its meaning is that if he makes the jarh specified (muqayyad), then the qadi will pay attention. For example, he says that the witness drank wine and demands the hadd penalty on him, and brings two witnesses for that, causing the plaintiff's witnesses to have the hadd imposed. Since by violating the rights of Allah, hadd is imposed, he becomes fasiq. Therefore the testimony of that witness of the plaintiff is not accepted. In this case, alleging wine drinking as a cause for fisq is specified jarh, so the qadi pays attention and also decides on the rejection of the witnesses. This jarh is hearable by the qadi. An example of specified jarh in matters of the rights of people: The defendant claimed that he gave the plaintiff's witness one hundred dirhams and it was agreed that he would not testify against him, yet he testified. So he demands the return of the one hundred dirhams. And on both matters the defendant brought witnesses. Since the demand for return of money is made, the qadi has the right to order the return on the basis of testimony. And since bribery is proven, the plaintiff's witness falls into the category of fasiq and his testimony is rejected. The demand for return of money comes from the servant, so this is an example of specified jarh in the rights of people. 'Except what is established as a right' (illa ma istahaqqa 'alayh): its meaning is that if the plaintiff's witnesses are proven to have violated the rights of Allah, like committing zina, drinking wine, or stealing, or to have suppressed the rights of people, then the qadi will hear this jarh and also decide on the negation or affirmation of fisq.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This is a ruling statement with proof. The matn states that the qadi does not accept testimony regarding jarh (discrediting a witness) or nafi (negation) and does not pass judgment on it, except when a right (istihqaq) is established. The commentary explains that if a defendant merely claims that the plaintiff's witnesses are fasiq without specifying the cause (e.g., wine drinking or theft), the qadi ignores it. The basis is a hadith that Muslims are presumed upright ('udul) unless they have been flogged for slander. Thus, unspecified jarh is not sufficient to reject testimony. However, if the jarh is specified (muqayyad) by mentioning a specific act that leads to fisq, such as drinking wine (rights of Allah) or taking a bribe to testify falsely (rights of people), and if that act can be proven (e.g., by witnesses or hadd), then the qadi considers it and the witness's testimony is rejected. The commentary gives examples: for rights of Allah, if it is proven that a witness drank wine and was punished with hadd, he becomes fasiq; for rights of people, if a witness took a bribe to testify, that is proven and he is fasiq. The exception (illa ma istahaqqa 'alayh) refers to the defendant establishing his right by proving the specified cause of fisq.

Key Terms
جرح (jarh): Discrediting a witness by alleging fisq or other disqualification.
استحقاق (istihqaq): The right of the defendant to have the jarh considered because he establishes a specific cause of fisq.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A defendant tells the qadi that the plaintiff's witness is fasiq but does not explain why. How should the qadi respond according to this ruling?
A) Reject the witness immediately.
B) Ask the defendant to bring proof of the witness's fisq.
C) Ignore the statement and accept the witness's testimony.
D) Investigate the witness's character.

Key Takeaway
The presumption of uprightness (asl al-adalah) protects Muslim witnesses; only specified and proven fisq can disqualify them.

Five Exceptions to Direct Observation in Testimony
Listing exceptions to the rule that testimony requires direct observation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that testimony requires direct observation, list the five exceptions, and explain the rationale of necessity.

Core Idea
Testimony normally requires direct sight, but for lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and judgeship, reliable hearsay suffices due to necessity.

In Hanafi law, a witness must generally have directly observed the event he testifies about. However, for five specific matters, the law permits testimony based on widespread reports or circumstantial evidence. This lesson explains those exceptions and the reasoning behind them.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the default requirement from the matn: a witness cannot testify about something he did not directly witness (mu'ayanah).
This is the baseline principle.
2
List the five exceptions
Memorize the five matters: lineage (nasab), death (mawt), marriage (nikah), consummation (dukhul), and appointment of a qadi (wilayat al-qadi).
These are the only cases where hearsay is allowed.
3
Understand the rationale
Explain why these exceptions exist: these events often occur in private or with few witnesses, and testimony may be needed after a long time; requiring direct observation would create legal hardship.
Necessity (darurah) and tawatur (widespread report) are key.
4
Analyze the evidentiary basis
The general rule is derived from a Quranic verse (17:36) prohibiting testifying without knowledge. The exceptions are justified by necessity and supported by hadith (e.g., the Prophet's testimony about his wet nurse Thuwaybah).
The hadith illustrates accepting hearsay when direct memory is absent.
5
Apply to modern scenarios
Recognize when hearsay testimony is acceptable, e.g., testifying about marriage based on cohabitation, or death based on reliable reports.
Modern equivalents: hospital records, public announcements, etc.

Source Text

[۲۸۴۹ (٤٠) ولا يجوز للشاهد ان يشهد بشيء لم يعاينه الا النسب والموت والنكاح والدخول وولاية القاضى فانه يسعه ان يشهد بهذه الاشياء اذا اخبره اور گواہوں کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ بغیر دیکھے گواہی دے مگر نسب کی اور موت اور نکاح اور دخول اور قاضی کی ولایت کی ۔ اس لئے کہ اس کو گنجائش ہے کہ ان چیزوں کی گواہی دے اگر اس کو کوئی اعتماد والا آدمی خبر دیدے۔ ر او پر آیت سے ثابت کیا گیا ہے کہ اصل قاعدہ تو یہی ہے کہ کسی چیز کو دیکھے پھر اس کے ہونے کی گواہی دے۔ لیکن کچھ چیزیں ایسی ہیں کہ ان کے ہوتے وقت ایک دو آدمی ہوتے ہیں اور زمانہ دراز کے بعد اس کی گواہی دینے کی ضرورت پڑتی ہے۔ اس لئے اصل حقیقت کو دیکھنے والے گواہ موجود نہیں ہوتے ۔ اس لئے لوگوں سے سن کر اور علامات کے ذریعہ یقین کر کے ان کی گواہی دینا جائز ہے۔ مثلا نسب، بچہ پیدا ہوتے وقت ایک دائی اور ایک دو عورتیں ہوتی ہیں۔ پھر زمانہ دراز کے بعد کبھی گواہی دینے کی ضرورت پیش آتی ہے کہ فلاں فلاں کا بیٹا ہے۔ ایسی صورت میں گواہ سنتے آئے ہیں کہ فلاں فلاں کا بیٹا ہے اس نے پیدا ہوتے وقت نہیں دیکھا ہے پھر بھی سن کر گواہی دینا جائز ہے کہ فلاں فلاں کا بیٹا ہے۔ موت : موت کے وقت بھی ایک دو آدمی ہوتے ہیں۔ پھر لوگوں سے سن کر یقین کرتے ہیں کہ فلاں کا انتقال ہو گیا ہے۔ پھر زمانہ دراز کے بعد سنی سنائی پر گواہی دیتے ہیں کہ فلاں کا انتقال ہو گیا ہے۔ اس لئے موت کا بغیر معائنہ کئے ہوئے صرف سن کر گواہی دینا جائز ہے۔ نکاح دخول : ولایت قاضی کا بھی یہی حال ہے کہ نکاح کے وقت ایک دو آدمی ہوتے ہیں پھر میاں بیوی کو ساتھ رہتے ہوئے دیکھتے ہیں تو گواہی دیتے ہیں کہ یہ دونوں میاں بیوی ہیں۔ دخول کے وقت تو کوئی نہیں ہوتا صرف قرینے سے گواہی دیتے ہیں کہ بیوی سے دخول ہو گیا ہے۔ ولایت قاضی کا بھی یہی حال ہے کہ قاضی بناتے وقت ایک دو آدمی ہوتے ہیں۔ پھر لوگ دیکھتے ہیں کہ یہ مجلس قضا کے عہدے پر بیٹھا ہے اور فیصلہ کرتا ہے اس لئے لوگ گواہی دیتے ہیں کہ یہ قاضی ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے بچپنے میں حضرت ثوبیہ سے دودھ پیا جبکہ آپ کو یاد بھی نہیں ہوگا لیکن بعد میں سن کر آپ نے فرمایا کہ مجھے اور
(40) It is not permissible for a witness to testify about something he did not witness except for lineage (nasab), death (mawt), marriage (nikah), consummation (dukhul), and the appointment of a qadi (wilayat al-qadi). For he is permitted to testify about these things if someone reliable informs him. (Commentary:) It is established from the verse that the basic principle is that one should only testify after seeing something. But some matters are such that at the time of their occurrence only one or two people are present, and after a long time, the need to testify about them arises, so the original eyewitnesses are not available. Therefore, it is permissible to testify based on hearing from people and attaining certainty through signs. For example, lineage: at the time of a child's birth, there is a midwife and one or two women. Then after a long time, the need to testify that so-and-so is the son of so-and-so arises. In such a case, the witness has heard that so-and-so is the son of so-and-so; he did not witness the birth, but it is still permissible to testify based on hearsay. Death: at the time of death also, one or two people are present. Then people hear and become certain that so-and-so has died. Then after a long time, they testify based on hearsay that so-and-so has died. So it is permissible to testify about death without direct observation, only by hearing. Marriage and consummation and the appointment of a qadi are similar: at the time of marriage, one or two people are present; then they see the husband and wife living together, so they testify that they are married. At the time of consummation, no one is present; they testify based on circumstantial evidence (qarinah) that consummation has occurred. Similarly, for the appointment of a qadi: at the time of appointment, one or two people are present; then people see him sitting in the seat of judgment and passing verdicts, so they testify that he is the qadi. There is a hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) drank milk from Thuwaybah in his childhood, though he did not remember it, but later he said (based on hearing)...
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The matn states the general rule: a witness may only testify about what he has directly seen, except for five matters: lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and the appointment of a qadi. For these, it is sufficient to testify based on reliable hearsay (tawatur or widespread report). The commentary explains that the basis is a Quranic verse (likely 'do not pursue that of which you have no knowledge') establishing that testimony must be based on certain knowledge. However, for these five matters, direct observation is often impossible due to the passage of time or the private nature of the event. Instead, one relies on widespread reports and circumstantial evidence. Examples: lineage is known through continuous reports and public knowledge; death is established through hearsay after a period; marriage is known by seeing the couple living as husband and wife; consummation is inferred from being alone with the spouse; the judge's appointment is known by seeing him perform judicial functions. The hadith about the Prophet and Thuwaybah is mentioned as an example of relying on hearsay (though the full lesson is cut off).

Key Terms
معاينة (mu'ayanah): Direct observation with one's own eyes, required as the basis for most testimony.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or family relationship; exception where hearsay testimony is allowed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man is asked to testify in court about a couple's marriage. He did not attend the wedding but knows the couple has lived together for years. Is his testimony valid?
A) Yes, because marriage is one of the exceptions where hearsay is allowed.
B) No, because he did not directly witness the marriage contract.
C) Yes, but only if he has a written marriage certificate.
D) No, because testimony requires two male witnesses.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, testimony based on hearsay is accepted for five specific matters due to necessity, while direct observation is required for everything else.

Testimony Without Sight: Five Exceptional Cases
Ruling and proofs for exceptional hearsay testimony in five matters.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five exceptional matters for hearsay testimony in Hanafi fiqh and explain the proofs supporting this ruling.

Core Idea
Testimony without direct sight is permissible for lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and judge's authority.

The general rule in Hanafi law is that a witness must have directly observed what he testifies about. However, for five specific matters—lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and a judge's authority—this rule is relaxed due to necessity. In this lesson, we will examine the proofs from the Sunnah and scholarly consensus that establish these exceptions, and understand why hearsay testimony is considered reliable for these matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule and the Exceptions
Note the opening statement: a witness cannot testify without direct sight except for five specified matters. Commit these five to memory: lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and judge's authority.
The exception is based on need—these matters are often only known through hearsay.
2
Analyze the First Proof: The Prophet's Testimony on Breastfeeding
The Prophet (PBUH) stated that Thubayyah nursed him and Abu Salamah. He was not an eyewitness (being an infant), yet he testified based on reliable information. This establishes that hearsay can be valid for establishing lineage and relationships.
This hadith demonstrates practical application of hearsay testimony.
3
Analyze the Second Proof: Lineage Determination by Signs
In the hadith of Anas ibn Malik, the Prophet (PBUH) used physical attributes to determine paternity. This shows that testimony can be based on signs and reliable reports, not solely on direct observation.
The ruling on the child of Hilal and Sharik is a key precedent.
4
Consider the Scholarly Consensus (Ijma)
Early scholars like al-Sha'bi, Ibn Sirin, 'Ata, and Qatada accepted 'hearing as testimony.' Their practice adds weight to the Hanafi position that hearsay is valid for these matters.
Al-Hasan al-Basri also related testimony based on what he heard, not what he saw.
5
Understand the Rationale: Necessity and Reliable Hearsay
The five matters are recurrent events often witnessed by few people. Requiring direct sight would make many legitimate claims impossible. The condition is that the informant be trustworthy (man yathiqu bihī).
This is an application of istihsan (juristic preference) based on necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
استحق علیه ۲۸۴۹ (۴۰) ولا يجوز للشاهد ان يشهد بشيء لم يعاينه الا النسب والموت والنكاح والدخول وولاية القاضى فانه يسعه ان يشهد بهذه الاشياء اذا اخبره بها من يثق به. وقال النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم ارضعتنى وابا سلمة ثوبية. عن ابن عباس قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في بنت حمزة لا تحل لى يحرم من الرضاعة ما يحرم من النسب،هي ابنة اخي من الرضاعة. وقال الشعبي او ابن سيرين وعطاء وقتادة السمع شهادة وكان الحسن يقول لم يشهدوني على شيء ولكن سمعت كذا وكذا. مسالت انس بن مالک .... فقال رسول الله ابصروها فان جاءت به ابيض سبطا قضى العينين فهو لهلال بن امية وان جائت به اکحل جعد احمش الساقين فهو لشريك بن سحـمـاء. قال فانبأت انها جاءت به اکحل جعد حمش الساقين.
And it is not permissible for a witness to testify to something he did not witness except lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and the authority of the judge. For it is permissible for him to testify to these things if someone he trusts informs him of them. The Prophet (PBUH) said: 'Thubayyah nursed me and Abu Salama.' Ibn Abbas narrated that the Prophet (PBUH) said regarding the daughter of Hamzah: 'She is not permissible for me; breastfeeding makes unlawful what lineage makes unlawful; she is the daughter of my brother through breastfeeding.' And al-Sha'bi or Ibn Sirin, 'Ata, and Qatada said: 'Hearing is testimony.' And al-Hasan used to say: 'They did not make me testify to anything, but I heard such and such.' The case of Anas ibn Malik... the Messenger of Allah said: 'Look at her; if she gives birth to a white, straight-haired child with prominent eyes, then it belongs to Hilal ibn Umayyah; if she gives birth to a dark-eyed, curly-haired child with thin shanks, then it belongs to Sharik ibn Sahma.' He said: 'I was informed that she gave birth to a dark-eyed, curly-haired child with thin shanks.'
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of testifying without direct sight in specific matters. The general principle is that a witness must have directly observed what he testifies about. However, necessity dictates exceptions for five matters: lineage, death, marriage, consummation, and the authority of a judge. In these cases, testimonies are often required long after the event, and only a few people are present at the time. Therefore, a witness may rely on widespread hearsay or reliable information from trustworthy individuals. The author supports this with several proofs: first, the Prophet (PBUH) himself testified about his breastfeeding relationship with Thubayyah based on hearing it from others, even though he was too young to remember. Second, the Prophet (PBUH) ruled on the marriage prohibition due to breastfeeding for the daughter of Hamzah, establishing that lineage-through-breastfeeding is like real lineage. Third, the practice of early scholars like al-Sha'bi, Ibn Sirin, 'Ata, and Qatada who accepted 'hearing' as valid testimony. Fourth, the hadith of the Prophet (PBUH) regarding the child of Hilal and Sharik, where he determined lineage by physical signs, showing that testimony can be based on attributes and signs rather than direct observation. The Hanafi school uses these proofs to establish that in these five matters, testimonio based on reliable hearsay is acceptable. This is a principle of istihsan based on necessity and widespread practice.

Key Terms
معاينة (mu'ayana): Direct visual observation of the event by the witness.
شهادة سماعية (shahada samaiyya): Testimony based on hearsay rather than direct sight.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, hearsay testimony is acceptable for five matters due to necessity and the nature of these events.

Secondary Testimony: Scope in Rights Not Subject to Doubt
Ruling on secondary testimony and its scope of acceptance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on secondary testimony and identify which rights qualify for its acceptance.

Core Idea
Secondary testimony is accepted in financial rights but not in hudud or qisas because those are invalidated by doubt.

In Islamic legal procedure, testimony is a primary means of proof. But what if the original witness cannot appear? The Hanafi school permits a representative witness (shahada ala shahada) in certain cases. This lesson explains the scope of this permission and the underlying proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine the legal act being discussed (shahada ala shahada) and its ruling (ja'iz/permissible).
The ruling is permission, not obligation.
2
Locate the Scope Condition
Note the condition: 'fi kulli haqq la yusqat bil-shubha' – in every right that is not invalidated by doubt. Understand what this excludes.
Hudud and qisas are explicitly excluded because they fall under shubha.
3
Examine the Dalil
Read the hadith from Ibn Abbas: 'You hear, and it will be heard from you.' Consider how this supports transmission of testimony.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning is clear (qati al-dalala).
4
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the phrase 'yusma' minkum' indicates that information can be relayed, thus justifying secondary testimony.
The Hanafi school uses this as evidence for permissibility.
5
Apply to Real Cases
Consider practical scenarios: debt claims (accepted) vs. retaliation cases (rejected).
This step consolidates the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشهادة على الشهادة جائزة فى كل حق لا يسقط بالشبهة، ولا تقبل في الحدود والقصاص. عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله الله تسمعون ويسمع منكم.
Testimony upon testimony is permissible in every right that is not invalidated by doubt, and it is not accepted in hudud and qisas. Ibn Abbas narrated that the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) said: 'You hear, and it will be heard from you.'
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on the validity of secondary testimony (shahada ala shahada). The principle is that a witness may delegate another to testify on his behalf if he is unable to attend. This is permissible only for rights that are not invalidated by doubt, meaning financial rights and claims that are not subject to evidentiary suspicion. Therefore, it is not allowed in hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation), because these are invalidated by doubts (shubhat). The proof is the hadith where the Prophet (PBUH) said, 'You hear, and it will be heard from you,' indicating that information can be transmitted. The Hanafi school accepts this practice based on necessity and ease.

Key Terms
شهادة على الشهادة (shahada ala shahada): Secondary testimony: a witness delegates another to testify on his behalf.
حق لا يسقط بالشبهة (haqq la yusqat bil-shubha): A right that is not rendered invalid by evidentiary doubt, typically financial rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Secondary testimony is a permitted delegation in Hanafi law, but its scope is limited to rights not subject to evidentiary doubt, excluding hudud and qisas.

Testimony upon Testimony: Valid in Financial Rights, Invalid in Hudud
Ruling with proof: permissibility of shahada 'ala al-shahada and its limits.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shahada 'ala al-shahada, distinguish between rights where it is valid and invalid, and cite the textual evidence.

Core Idea
Testimony upon testimony is valid only in rights not nullified by doubt; hudud and qisas are excluded.

In Islamic legal procedure, direct testimony is the norm, but circumstances may require indirect testimony through a chain of witnesses. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on 'testimony upon testimony' (shahada 'ala al-shahada), where a secondary witness testifies to hearing the primary witness testify. The passage clarifies that this form of testimony is valid for financial and property rights but not for hudud and qisas, based on prophetic tradition and companion practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is 'testimony upon testimony' (shahada 'ala al-shahada). The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) and valid in every right that is not nullified by doubt (shubha). It is not accepted in hudud and qisas.
The text uses 'ja'iz' to indicate permissibility/validity in Hanafi terms.
2
Analyze the Limitation: Rights Not Nullified by Doubt
The key condition is that the right must be of a type that is not dropped by doubt. Financial claims, debts, property rights are examples. Hudud and qisas are dropped by doubt due to the principle 'al-hudud tudra'u bi al-shubuhat' (hudud are repelled by doubts).
This distinction is crucial for understanding the scope of the ruling.
3
Examine the First Proof: Hadith from Ibn Abbas
The hadith 'You hear and it will be heard from you from those who hear from you' indicates the permissibility of transmitting testimony from one person to another. The implication (wajh al-dalalah) is that hearing is sufficient for transmission, just as the Prophet's words can be transmitted.
This hadith is general; the limitation comes from the athar.
4
Examine the Second Proof: Athar from Masruq and Shurayh
The athar explicitly excludes hudud and qisas from testimony upon testimony. It also mentions that kafalah (suretyship) is not allowed in hadd cases, reinforcing the principle that hudud require certainty and cannot be based on indirect evidence.
The athar serves as a specific evidence (mukhasis) to the general hadith.
5
Apply the Ruling
In practice, if a primary witness is unavailable, a secondary witness who heard the primary testify may testify in financial disputes. But in cases of theft or murder requiring hadd or qisas, only direct testimony is accepted.
This ruling has practical implications for court procedure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۵۰] (۴۱) والشهادة على الشهادة جائزة فى كل حق لا يسقط بالشبهة ولا تقبل في الحدود والقصاص. والدليل: عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: تسمعون ويسمع منكم ممن يسمع منكم. وعن مسروق وشريح انهما قالا لا تجوز شهادة على شهادة في حد ولا يكفل في حد.
[2850] (41) And testimony upon testimony is permissible in every right that is not nullified by doubt, and it is not accepted in hudud and qisas. The evidence: from Ibn Abbas who said that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'You hear and it will be heard from you from those who hear from you.' And from Masruq and Shurayh that they said: 'Testimony upon testimony is not permissible in a hadd, nor is kafalah (suretyship) in a hadd.'
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on ‘testimony upon testimony’ (shahada ‘ala al-shahada), a form of indirect testimony where a witness (al-far’) testifies to the testimony of the original witness (al-asl). The ruling is that it is valid in all rights that are not voided by doubt (shubha), such as financial rights, but not in hudud (prescribed punishments) and qisas (retaliation) because these are dropped by doubt. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) indicates that a testimony can be transmitted from one to another, and an athar (report from companions) explicitly excludes hudud and qisas from this practice. The difference between rights that are and are not subject to shubha is key: hudud and qisas require certainty, and second-hand testimony introduces doubt.

Key Terms
الشهادة على الشهادة (ash-shahāda ‘alā ash-shahāda): Testimony of a secondary witness (far’) that he heard the primary witness (asl) testify to a fact.
لا يسقط بالشبهة (lā yasquṭu bi ash-shubha): Rights that are not nullified by doubt, such as debts or property claims.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Qisas for murder
C) Financial debt claim
D) Hadd punishment for adultery

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, shahada 'ala al-shahada is a valid form of indirect evidence only for rights that are not nullified by doubt; hudud and qisas are excluded due to their reliance on certainty.

Two Secondary Witnesses Suffice for Testimony Upon Testimony
Specifies the number of witnesses required for testimony upon testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of secondary witnesses required in testimony upon testimony and explain the evidence from the athar of al-Sha'bi.

Core Idea
Two secondary witnesses can testify on behalf of two primaries—one secondary witness is never enough.

In Islamic court procedure, testimony upon testimony (شهادة على شهادة) allows secondary witnesses to confirm that they heard primary witnesses testify. The Hanafi school sets a clear minimum: two secondary witnesses must testify on each primary. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof from the Salaf, and the disagreement with the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'testimony upon testimony' (شهادة على شهادة). The ruling is that it is permissible (جائز) only if there are two secondary witnesses (شاهدين) testifying on the testimony of two primary witnesses. One secondary witness is not accepted.
The text uses 'يجوز' (permissible) but in the context of court procedure, it indicates a condition for validity.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites an athar from al-Sha'bi transmitted by Isma'il al-Azraq: 'The testimony of a witness upon a witness is not valid until they are two.' This is a qawl sahabi (saying of a Companion) used as evidence.
Al-Sha'bi was a prominent tabi'i whose statements are considered a source in Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'until they are two' (حتى يكونا اثنين) indicates that two is the minimum number of secondary witnesses. It does not specify a ratio to primaries; thus two secondary witnesses can cover multiple primaries as long as they testify on each.
The Hanafi school interprets the general wording to allow the same two secondary witnesses for any number of primaries.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed, requiring two separate secondary witnesses for each primary witness (total four for two primaries). His basis is qiyas on original testimony, which requires two witnesses per fact.
The Hanafi response: secondary witnesses testify to the act of testimony, not the original fact, so the number is fixed at two.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The text sides with the Hanafi view, relying on the literal athar. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that under Hanafi, two secondary witnesses can cover many primaries, while under Shafi'i each primary needs its own pair.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the position stated here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۵۱] (۴۲) ويجوز شهادة شاهدين على شهادة شاهدين ولا تقبل شهادة واحد على شهادة واحد. والدليل: عن اسمعيل الازرق عن الشعبي قال: لا تجوز شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد حتى يكونا اثنين. وهذه خلاف قول الشافعي رحمه الله.
[2851] (42) And it is permissible for two witnesses to testify upon the testimony of two witnesses, and the testimony of one upon the testimony of one is not accepted. The evidence: from Isma’il al-Azraq from al-Sha’bi who said: ‘The testimony of a witness upon a witness is not valid until they are two.’ And this is contrary to the statement of al-Shafi’i (may Allah have mercy on him).
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage sets the required number of witnesses in ‘testimony upon testimony’. The ruling is that two secondary witnesses (furaw’) must testify on behalf of each primary witness (asl). Thus, if there are two primary witnesses, the secondary witnesses can be the same two for both, but each primary must have two secondary witnesses testifying on his testimony. The minimum number of secondary witnesses is two; one alone is insufficient. The proof is an athar from al-Sha’bi. The text notes that Imam al-Shafi’i disagreed, requiring two separate secondary witnesses for each primary witness, making a total of four distinct secondary witnesses. The Hanafi position is that two secondary witnesses suffice for both primary witnesses, as long as they testify to hearing each primary’s testimony.

Key Terms
شاهد على شهادة (shāhid ‘alā shahāda): A secondary witness who testifies that he heard the primary witness give testimony.
شاهدين على شهادة شاهدين (shāhidayn ‘alā shahādat shāhidayn): Two secondary witnesses testifying to the testimonies of two primary witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Two secondary witnesses
C) Four secondary witnesses
D) No secondary witnesses are needed

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, two secondary witnesses suffice for any number of primary witnesses in testimony upon testimony, based on the athar of al-Sha'bi.

Testimony on Testimony: Ruling in Hudud, Qisas, and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
States ruling and proof for shahada ala shahada in hudud/qisas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on accepting testimony on testimony in hudud and qisas, explain the doubt-based reason, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position on the required number of branch witnesses.

Core Idea
Testimony on testimony is accepted in rights but not in hudud and qisas because these penalties are dropped by doubt.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on shahada ala al-shahada (testimony on testimony) – a rule that draws a sharp line between serious criminal cases (hudud and qisas) and regular civil rights. We will first understand why branch testimony is acceptable in the latter but barred in the former, then turn to a classic inter-madhhab dispute: how many branch witnesses are needed? The source passage we will study presents the Hanafi view alongside the Shafi'i objection, supported by hadith, athar, and qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Two Contexts
Locate the ruling: testimony on testimony is not accepted in hudud and qisas, but is accepted in rights (huquq). Note the key distinction.
The passage explicitly states 'ولا تُقبل في الحدود والقصاص' and later gives the reason.
2
Extract the Reason (Ta'lil)
Find the reason why it is not accepted in hudud/qisas: 'الحد والقصاص يسقطان بالشبهة' (hudud and qisas are dropped by doubt). Branch testimony contains doubt because it is not direct observation.
This is a core Hanafi principle: shubuhat drop hadd.
3
Trace the Dalil (Evidence)
Identify the evidence: hadith (Abu Dawud) allowing transmission by hearing, athar from Masruq and Shuraih, and the practical necessity (illness of original witness).
The hadith is used by qiyas (analogy) to justify testimony by transmission in general.
4
Map the Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Identify the issue: number of branch witnesses. Hanafi: same two branch witnesses can testify for both original witnesses. Shafi'i: each original requires two separate branch witnesses (total four). Note each school's dalil.
The dispute centers on the athar of al-Sha'bi and its interpretation.
5
Derive the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
Understand the practical difference: under Hanafi, only two branch witnesses are needed; under Shafi'i, four. This affects court procedures and cost.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

الشهادة على الشهادة في حدود الله ج عاشر ص ۴۲۳ نمبر ۶ ۲۱۱۸ مصنف ابن ابی همية ، ۱۴۷ فى الشهادة على الشهادة في حد ، ج خامس، ص ۵۴۸ نمبر ۲۸۹۰۱ / مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب شهادة الرجل على الرجل ، ج ثامن ص ۱۳۳۹ نمبر ۱ ۱۵۴۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ حدود و قصاص میں شہادت پر شہادت جائز نہیں ہے۔ [۲۸۵۱] (۴۲) جائز ہے دو گواہوں کا گواہی دینا دو گواہوں کی گواہی پر۔ اور نہیں قبول کی جائے گی ایک کی گواہی ایک کی گواہی پر۔ شہادت پر شہادت کا قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ ایک اصل گواہ دو آدمیوں کو گواہ بنائے اور دوسرا اصل گواہ بھی دو آدمیوں کو گواہ بنائے ، اس طرح فرع گواہ چار ہو جائیں گے۔ لیکن یہ ممکن ہے کہ ایک اصل گواہ نے جن دو گواہوں کو گواہ بنایا ان ہی کو دوسرا اصل بھی اپنی گواہی پر گواہ بنادے اس طرح فرع گواہ بھی دور ہیں گے۔ پہلے اصل گواہ کے بھی یہی دو گواہ اور دوسرے اصل گواہ کے بھی یہی دو گواہ ۔ البتہ یہ جائز نہیں ہے کہ ایک اصل ایک ہی فرع کو اپنی گواہی پر گواہ بنائے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن اسمعيل الازرق عن الشعبي قالا لا تجوز شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد حتى يكونا اثنين(ج) سن للمبتی ، باب ما جاء فی عدد شهود الفرع ، ج عاشر ص ۲۲۴، نمبر ۲۱۱۹ مصنف ابن ابی هیبتة ۳۸۰۰ في شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد ، ج رابع ، ص ۵۵۴، نمبر ۲۳۰۷۰ / مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب شهادة الرجل على الرجل، ج ثامن ، ص ۱۳۳۹، نمبر ۱۵۴۵۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک اصل گواہ پر دو فرع گواہ چاہئے (۲) اصل کی گواہی منتقل کرنا ہے اس لئے آیت و استشهدوا شهيدين من رجالكم ( آیت ۲۸۲ ، سورة البقرۃ ۲) کے اعتبار سے دو گواہ چاہئے۔ نانه امام شافعی اوپر کے اثر کی وجہ سے فرماتے ہیں کہ ہر اصل گواہ کے لئے دو الگ الگ فرع گواہ ہوں۔ اس اعتبار سے دو اصل گواہ کے لئے چارا الگ الگ فرع گواہ ہونا ضروری ہے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا آج تم سن رہے ہو اور تم سے لوگ سنیں گے ۔ اور جنہوں نے تم سے سنا ہے ان سے لوگ سنیں گے (ب) حضرت مسروق اور شریح نے فرمایا حد میں نہ شہادت پر شہادت جائز ہے اور نہ کفالت لینا جائز ہے (ج) حضرت مفتی نے فرمایا حادة على الشهادة جائز نہیں جب تک کہ دو گواہ نہ ہو جائیں ۔
And it is not accepted in hudud and qisas [2851 (42)] And the testimony of two witnesses on the testimony of two witnesses is permissible, and the testimony of one on the testimony of one is not accepted. [...] The hadith (Abu Dawud) says: those who hear hadith will convey it to others, and others will hear from them. Just as hearing by transmission is allowed in hadith, similarly in testimony it is allowed. And it is needed because sometimes the original witness is so ill that he cannot go to the court, so there is need to make a branch witness on his testimony. The reason that testimony on testimony is not accepted in hudud and qisas is that hadd and qisas are dropped by doubt, and branch testimony contains doubt, so testimony on testimony is not allowed. There is an athar from Masruq and Shuraih that they said: testimony on testimony is not valid in hadd, nor surety in hadd. From this athar it is known that testimony on testimony in hudud and qisas is not allowed. [2851] (42) It is permissible for two witnesses to testify on the testimony of two witnesses, and the testimony of one on the testimony of one will not be accepted. The rule for testimony on testimony is that one original witness makes two people witnesses, and the other original witness also makes two people witnesses, so the branch witnesses become four. But it is possible that the two witnesses whom one original witness made witnesses, the other original also makes them witnesses on his own testimony, so the branch witnesses are also two. The same two witnesses are for the first original witness and for the second original witness. However, it is not permissible for one original to make only one branch witness on his testimony. There is an athar from Ismail al-Azraq from al-Sha'bi that they said: testimony of a witness on a witness is not valid until they become two. From this athar it is known that for one original witness, two branch witnesses are required. (2) Because the testimony is being transferred, so according to the verse 'and call two witnesses from among your men' (Ayat 282, Surah al-Baqarah 2), two witnesses are required. Then Imam al-Shafi'i, due to the above athar, says that for each original witness there must be two separate branch witnesses. Thus for two original witnesses, four separate branch witnesses are necessary. Hashiya: (a) The Prophet said: Today you hear, and people will hear from you, and those who hear from you will be heard by others. (b) Hadrat Masruq and Shuraih said: In hadd, testimony on testimony is not valid, nor is taking surety valid. (c) Hadrat Mufti said: Testimony on testimony is not valid until there are two witnesses.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding testimony on testimony (shahada ala al-shahada). The Hanafi position is that such testimony is accepted in rights (huquq) but not in hudud and qisas. The reason given is that hudud and qisas are dropped by doubts (shubuhat), and branch testimony contains doubt because it is not direct observation. Therefore, the requirement for certainty in these serious matters is not met. This is supported by athar from Masruq and Shuraih. Regarding the number of witnesses, the Hanafi school requires two branch witnesses for each original witness, but the same two branch witnesses can serve for both original witnesses. Imam al-Shafi'i, based on an athar from Sha'bi, requires separate (four) branch witnesses. The passage also includes a hadith analogizing transmission of testimony to transmission of hadith, and a practical need for such testimony when the original witness is unable to attend court.

Key Terms
شهادة على شهادة (shahada ala al-shahada): Testimony based on another witness's testimony, not direct observation.
حدود (hudud): Fixed punishments for offenses against God, e.g., theft, zina.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation for murder or injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many branch witnesses are required when two original witnesses cannot attend court and both authorize the same branch witnesses?
A) Four branch witnesses, two for each original.
B) Two branch witnesses, the same two can serve for both originals.
C) One branch witness is sufficient if he is trustworthy.
D) Branch testimony is not allowed at all in such a case.

Key Takeaway
Testimony on testimony is a valid legal tool in rights but excluded from hudud and qisas due to the doubt principle.
