Procedure for Making a Branch Witness
Describes the correct verbal formula for appointing a branch witness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct procedure for appointing a branch witness and identify the minimum wording required in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Formal appointment with 'Ashhad 'ala shahadati' is required; merely hearing testimony is insufficient.

In Islamic legal procedure, testimony may be transmitted from an original witness to a branch witness when the original is unable to attend court. This lesson explains the precise verbal formula required by the Hanafi school to make such a branch witness valid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actors
Recognize the two parties: the original witness (asl) who directly observed the event or confession, and the branch witness (far') who will transmit the testimony.
2
State the core requirement
The original witness must formally appoint the branch witness by saying words such as 'Ashhad 'ala shahadati anni ashhadu anna fulan...' (Be a witness on my testimony that I testify that so-and-so...).
This explicit appointment is essential; simply hearing the testimony does not qualify one as a branch witness.
3
Note the optional element
The original witness may also add 'ashhadani 'ala nafsihi' (he made me a witness on himself), but this phrase is not necessary for validity. It is recommended.
Omitting it does not affect the validity of the appointment.
4
Recognize the underlying principle
The requirement for formal appointment ensures certainty and prevents confusion. An athar from Shuraih supports this: the branch witness should say that a just person made him a witness.
5
Apply the rule
Distinguish between valid and invalid scenarios. For example, if Ali hears Zayd testify but Zayd never formally appoints him, Ali cannot testify as a branch witness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۵۲ (۴۳) وصفة الاشهاد ان يقول شاهد الاصل لشاهد الفرع اشهد على شهادتي انی اشهد ان فلان بن فلان اقرَّ عندى بكذاو اشهدنى على نفسه وان لم يقل اشهدني على نفسه جاز [۲۸۵۲] (۴۳) گواہ بنانے کا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ اصل گواہ فرع گواہ سے کہے، میری گواہی پر گواہ بن جاؤ میں گواہی دیتا ہوں کہ فلاں ابن ، فلاں نے میرے سامنے اتنے کا اقرار کیا ہے اور مجھے اپنی ذات پر گواہ بنایا ہے۔ اور اگر اشهدنی علی نفسہ نہیں کہا تب بھی جائز ہے۔ یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ اصل گواہ جب تک باضابطہ طور پر فرع کو اپنی گواہی کا گواہ نہیں بنائے گا تو وہ گواہ نہیں بن سکے گا۔ صرف گواہی دیتے ہوئے سن لینے سے گواہ نہیں بن سکے گا۔ مسئلے کی تشریح یہ ہے کہ، اصل گواہ فرع گواہ سے با ضابطہ کہے کہ تم میری گواہی پر گواہ بنو اس بات کا کہ فلاں نے فلاں کا اتنے روپے کا میرے سامنے اقرار کیا ہے۔ اور مجھے اقرار پر گواہ بھی بنایا ہے، تاہم اگر یوں نہ کہے کہ مجھے اپنے اقرار پر گواہ بھی بنایا ہے تب بھی فرع کو گواہ بنانا درست ہو جائے گا۔ اثر میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن شريح قال تجوز شهادة الرجل على الرجل في الحقوق، ويقول شريح للشاهد قل: اشهدني ذو عدل (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شهادة الرجل على الرجل ، ج ثامن ص ۱۳۳۸، نمبر ۱۵۴۴۷) اس اثر میں ہے۔ قل اشھد فی ذو عدل، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ فرع گواہ گواہی دیتے وقت کہے گا کہ مجھے عادل آدمی نے گواہ بنایا ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ اصل گواہ اپنی گواہی پر باضابطہ گواہ بنائے تب فرع گواہ بن سکے گا۔
[2852] (43) The description of making a witness is that the original witness should say to the branch witness: 'Be a witness on my testimony, indeed I testify that so-and-so son of so-and-so acknowledged before me such-and-such, and he made me a witness on himself.' And if he does not say 'he made me a witness on himself', it is permissible. [2852] (43) The method of making a witness is that the original witness says to the branch witness: 'Become a witness on my testimony, I testify that so-and-so son of so-and-so acknowledged such-and-such before me and made me a witness on his own person.' And if he does not say 'he made me a witness on himself', it is still permissible. This matter is based on the principle that as long as the original witness does not formally make the branch a witness on his testimony, he cannot become a witness. Simply hearing the testimony being given does not make one a witness. The explanation of the matter is that the original witness should formally say to the branch witness: 'You be a witness on my testimony that so-and-so acknowledged such-and-such rupees before me, and he made me a witness on the acknowledgment.' However, if he does not say 'he made me a witness on his acknowledgment', it is still valid to make the branch witness. There is an indication of this in an athar: from Shuraih, he said: 'Testimony of a man on a man is permissible in rights, and Shuraih would say to the witness: Say: A just person made me a witness.' In this athar it is: 'Say: A just person made me a witness', from which it is known that the branch witness at the time of testifying will say that a just person made me a witness. From this it is known that when the original witness formally makes him a witness on his testimony, then the branch can become a witness.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing the procedure (sifah) for making a branch witness (shahadat al-far'). The original witness (shahid al-asl) must formally designate the branch witness (shahid al-far') by saying specific words: 'Ashhad 'ala shahadati anni ashhadu anna fulan...' The key requirement is that the original witness must explicitly ask the branch to be a witness on his testimony; merely hearing the original testify is insufficient. The passage also notes that it is not necessary to include the phrase 'ashhadani 'ala nafsihi' (he made me a witness on himself) for validity, but it is recommended. An athar from Shuraih supports the requirement of formal appointment, as he instructed the witness to say 'a just person made me a witness.' This emphasizes that the branch witness must identify himself as a secondary witness, not as an original witness.

Key Terms
اشهد على شهادتي (ashhad 'ala shahadati): Formula for appointing a branch witness: 'Be a witness on my testimony'.
أصل (asl): Original witness who directly observed the event or confession.
فرع (far'): Branch witness who testifies based on the original witness's testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum requirement for an original witness to make a branch witness?
A) The original witness must say: 'I testify that so-and-so confessed.'
B) The original witness must formally say: 'Be a witness on my testimony' or similar words.
C) The branch witness must hear the original testify in court.
D) The original witness must write a signed statement.

Key Takeaway
A branch witness must be formally appointed by the original witness using the words 'Ashhad 'ala shahadati'; the phrase 'ashhadani 'ala nafsihi' is recommended but not required.

Wording of Branch Witness When Testifying
Specifies the exact wording the branch witness must use in court

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact wording a branch witness must use in court and identify the key components that distinguish him from an original witness.

Core Idea
The branch witness must explicitly identify as a secondary witness and reference the original's testimony.

When a person witnesses another's testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada), the court requires a precise formula to avoid confusion with original testimony. This lesson breaks down the required wording that the Hanafi school mandates for the branch witness at the time of performance (ada'). You will learn what to say and what not to say, and why the formula matters for legal validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Required Statement
Locate the Arabic phrase the branch witness must utter: 'Ashhadu anna fulanan ashhadani 'ala shahadatihi annahu yashhadu anna fulanan aqarra 'indahu bikadha.'
The translation: 'I testify that so-and-so made me a witness on his testimony that he testifies that so-and-so acknowledged before him such-and-such.'
2
Deconstruct the Formula
Break the formula into three parts: (1) the branch witness's own testimony ('Ashhadu'), (2) the original witness's act of making him a witness ('fulanan ashhadani'), and (3) the content of the original testimony ('annahu yashhadu...').
Each part serves a distinct legal function: identifying the speaker as a secondary witness, linking to the original, and conveying the original's testimony.
3
Understand the Prohibition
Note what the branch witness must NOT say: 'I am the original witness.' The passage explicitly forbids this and requires him to state that he is a branch witness and that the original witness made him a witness.
Claiming to be the original witness is a mufsid (invalidator) because it misrepresents the source of knowledge.
4
Connect to the Athar of Shuraih
The passage cites an athar from Judge Shuraih, who instructed the branch witness to say: 'A just person made me a witness' (ashhadani dhu 'adl). This emphasizes that the original witness must be just (adl) and that the branch witness must attribute the testimony to him.
The requirement of 'adalah in the original witness is a condition for accepting branch testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۵۳ (۴۴) ويقول شاهد الفرع عند الاداء اشهد ان فلانااشهدنى على سهادته انه يشهد ان فلانا اقر عنده بكذا [ ۲۸۵۴ (۴۵) وقال لي اشهد على شهادتي [۲۸۵۳] (۴۴) فرع گواہ ادائیگی کے وقت کہے گا فلاں نے مجھ کو اپنی گواہی پر گواہ بنایا ہے۔ وہ گواہی دیتے ہیں کہ فلاں نے اس کے پاس اتنے کا اقرار کیا ہے۔ فرع گواہ گواہی دیتے وقت یوں نہیں کہے گا کہ میں اصل گواہ ہوں بلکہ با ضابطہ کہے گا میں فرع گواہ ہوں اور اصل گواہ نے مجھ کو اپنی گواہی پر گواہ بنایا ہے اس بات کا کہ اس کے سامنے فلاں نے اتنی رقم کا اقرار کیا ہے۔ (۱۲۸۵۴ (۴۵) اور مجھ کو کہا کہ میری اس گواہی پر گواہ بن جاؤ۔ اس لئے میں اس بات کی گواہی دیتا ہوں۔ ان فرع گواہ قاضی کے سامنے کہے گا کہ مجھے اصل گواہ نے کہا تھا کہ میری اس گواہی پر گواہ بنو۔ چونکہ میں اس کی گواہی پر گواہ بن چکا ہوں اس لئے میں اس کی گواہی دیتا ہوں۔ او پراثر میں گزرا کہ قاضی شریح فرع گواہ سے کہلواتے تھے کہ مجھے عادل آدمی نے گواہ بنایا ہے۔ عن شریح قال ... قل اشهدني ذو عدل (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب شهادة الرجل على الرجل ، ج ثامن، ص ۱۳۳۸، نمبر ۱۵۴۴۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ فرع گواہ اقرار کرے کہ مجھ کو حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت شریح نے فرمایا شہادۃ علی الشہادۃ حقوق میں جائز ہے۔ حضرت شریح گواہ سے فرماتے تھے، کہو مجھ کو عادل نے گواہ بنایا ہے۔
[2853] (44) The branch witness at the time of giving testimony should say: 'I testify that so-and-so made me a witness on his testimony, that he testifies that so-and-so acknowledged before him such-and-such.' [2854] (45) 'And he said to me: Be a witness on my testimony.' [2853] (44) The branch witness at the time of performance will say: 'So-and-so made me a witness on his testimony. They testify that so-and-so acknowledged such-and-such before him.' The branch witness when giving testimony will not say 'I am the original witness,' but will formally say 'I am a branch witness and the original witness made me a witness on his testimony, that before him so-and-so acknowledged such-and-such amount.' (12/2854) (45) 'And he said to me: Be a witness on this testimony of mine. Therefore I testify to this matter.' That is, the branch witness will say before the judge: 'The original witness told me: Be a witness on this testimony of mine. Since I have become a witness on his testimony, I therefore give his testimony.' And earlier in the athar it passed that Judge Shuraih used to instruct the branch witness: 'Say: A just person made me a witness.' From Shuraih he said: '...Say: A just person made me a witness.' In this athar it is that the branch witness should acknowledge that he was made a witness by a just person. Hashiya: (a) Hadrat Shuraih said: Testimony on testimony is permissible in rights. Hadrat Shuraih used to tell the witness: 'Say: A just person made me a witness.'
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement specifying the exact wording (qawl) the branch witness (shahid al-far') must use when testifying in court. The formula is: 'Ashhadu anna fulanan ashhadani 'ala shahadatihi annahu yashhadu anna fulanan aqarra 'indahu bikadha.' Essentially, the branch witness must state: (1) that the original witness made him a witness on his testimony, and (2) the content of that original testimony (e.g., that someone confessed). He must not claim to be an original witness. The passage also includes an alternative formula with 'Qala li ashhad 'ala shahadati.' An athar from Shuraih indicates that the branch witness should say 'A just person made me a witness,' emphasizing that he is a secondary witness. The hashia confirms that shahada ala al-shahada is permissible in rights (huquq).

Key Terms
اشهدني على شهادته (ashhadani 'ala shahadatihi): He made me a witness on his testimony; phrase used by branch witness.
ذو عدل (dhu 'adl): A just person; refers to the original witness being just.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a branch witness say when giving testimony in court according to the Hanafi school?
A) 'I testify that so-and-so confessed.'
B) 'So-and-so made me a witness on his testimony that he testifies that so-and-so confessed.'
C) 'I am the original witness and I testify that so-and-so confessed.'
D) 'A just person told me that so-and-so confessed.'

Key Takeaway
The branch witness must use a specific formula that identifies him as a secondary witness and recites the original testimony; failing to do so invalidates the testimony.

When Is Secondary Witness Testimony Accepted?
Ruling with proof: conditions for accepting shuhud al-far'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions under which Hanafi law accepts secondary witness testimony and apply them to factual scenarios.

Core Idea
Secondary testimony is only a substitute — accepted only when the primary cannot testify due to death, long travel, or incapacitating illness.

This lesson examines the strict Hanafi position on secondary witnesses (shuhud al-far'). While some schools allow broader acceptance, the Hanafi school limits it to three specific excuses. Understanding these conditions is essential for practicing fiqh in court proceedings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The text begins with 'wa la tuqbal' — secondary testimony is not accepted. This is the default. The burden is on the proponent to show an exception.
2
List the three exceptions
The passage gives three excuses: death of primary witnesses, travel of three days or more, and illness that prevents attending court. Memorize these precisely.
The travel distance is measured as three days' journey — less than that does not qualify.
3
Analyze the underlying principle
The commentary explains 'al-asl' — the primary witness is the foundation. Secondary witnesses are only a necessity (darurah) substitute.
This explains why the exceptions are narrow.
4
Examine the proof
The athar from Shurayh states he did not accept secondary testimony while the primary was alive, even with an oath. This supports the strict limitation.
The proof is zanni in transmission but qati in meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا تُقبل شهادة شهود الفرع الا ان يموت شهود الاصل او يغيبوا مسيرة ثلثة ايام فصاعدا او يمرضوا مرضا لا يستطيعون معه حضور مجلس الحاكم [ا یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ گواہی کے لئے اصل گواہ ضروری ہے۔ فرع گواہ مجبوری کے درجے میں مہیا کئے جائیں گے۔ اس لئے اصل گواہ مرجائیں یا تین دن یا اس سے زیادہ کی مسافت پر چلے جائیں یا ایسا بیمار ہو جائیں کہ مجلس قضا میں حاضر ہونا مشکل ہو تب فرع گواہ بنانا جائز ہوگا۔ اور وہ گواہی دے سکے گا۔ فرع گواہ اصل کی مجبوری کے بعد ہے۔ (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن شريح انه كان لا يجيز شهادة الشاهد مادام حيا ولو كان باليمين (مصنف ابن ابي هيبة ، ۳۸۰ في شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد ، ج رابع ص ۵۵۴ نمبر ۲۳۰۶۹) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اصل گواہ کو ایسی مجبوری ہو جائے جن سے مجلس قضاء میں حاضر ہونا ناممکن ہو تب فرع گواہ کی گواہی قبول کی جائے گی۔]
The testimony of secondary witnesses is not accepted unless the primary witnesses die, or they go away a distance of three days or more, or they become ill such that they cannot attend the court of the judge.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof passage from the Hanafi school. The author states that testimony from secondary witnesses (shuhud al-far') is only admissible when the primary witnesses (shuhud al-asl) are unable to testify in person due to three specific excuses: death, travel of at least three days' journey, or illness preventing attendance at court. The underlying principle (usul) is that the primary witness is essential; secondary witnesses are a substitute only in cases of necessity. An athar from Shurayh is cited: he did not accept secondary testimony as long as the primary witness was alive, even if the secondary witness swore an oath, indicating the strict limitation.

Key Terms
شهود الاصل (shuhud al-asl): Primary witnesses who directly witnessed the event.
شهود الفرع (shuhud al-far'): Secondary witnesses who testify on behalf of the primary witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the primary witnesses are busy with work
B) When the primary witnesses are ill and cannot attend court
C) When the primary witnesses are absent for less than three days
D) When the secondary witnesses are more knowledgeable

Key Takeaway
Secondary witness testimony is only a substitute for primary witnesses, accepted in Hanafi law only when the primary is unavailable due to death, long travel, or incapacitating illness.

Secondary Witnesses and Declaration of Justness
Ruling on secondary witnesses and ta'dil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether secondary witnesses must explicitly declare the primary witnesses just, and explain the evidence from the athar of Shurayh.

Core Idea
Secondary witnesses may either declare or silence; the judge must verify if they remain silent.

This lesson addresses a procedural point in shahadat al-shahadat (witnessing upon a witness). The Hanafi school permits the secondary witnesses to either explicitly state that the primary witnesses are 'adil or remain silent on that point. The judge's duty is to independently investigate the character of the primary witnesses if the secondary ones do not comment. This ruling is supported by an athar from the tabi'i Shurayh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the secondary witnesses commenting on the justness of the primary witnesses. The ruling is that it is permissible (ja'iz) whether they do so or not.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is an athar from Shurayh via Hasan ibn Salih and Ja'd ibn Zakwan, recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba.
The athar is a marfu' report from Shurayh, a famous judge.
3
Analyze the athar
Shurayh said: 'I accept the testimony of a witness upon a witness when the primary witnesses have formally appointed them.' This implies that formal appointment suffices, not explicit ta'dil.
The hadith uses 'shahida 'alayhim' meaning they appointed them as witnesses upon themselves.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) require the secondary witnesses to explicitly state the primary witnesses are just (tazkiyah). The Hanafi school does not.
The difference stems from interpretation of the condition of 'adalah in witnesses.
5
Determine the practical implication
If secondary witnesses remain silent, the judge must independently investigate the 'adalah of the primary witnesses. Their testimony is not automatically rejected.
The judge's investigation preserves the integrity of testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان عدل شهود الاصل شهود الفرع جاز وان سكتوا عن اصل گواہ نے گواہ بنایا ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن حسن بن صالح قال قلت للجعد بن زكوان،شهدت شريحا يقول: اجيز شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد اذا شهد عليهما (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۲۸۰ في شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد ، ج رابع ص ۵۵۴ ، نمبر ۲۳۰۶۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ گواہ بنائے تو گواہ بن سکتا ہے ا ہے۔ [۲۸۵۶] (۴۷) فان عدل شهود الاصل شهود الفرع جاز وان سكتوا عن اصل گواہ نے گواہ بنایا ہے (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن حسن بن صالح قال قلت للجعد بن زكوان،شهدت شريحا يقول: اجيز شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد اذا شهد عليهما (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۲۸۰ في شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد ، ج رابع ص ۵۵۴ ، نمبر ۲۳۰۶۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ گواہ بنائے تو گواہ بن سکتا ہے ا ہے۔ [۲۸۵۶] (۴۷) اور نہیں قبول کی جائے گی فرع گواہوں کی گواہی مگر یہ کہ اصل گواہ مرجائیں، یا تین دن یا اس سے زیادہ کی مسافت پر چلے یا جائیں یا ایسا بیمار ہو جائیں کہ اس کی وجہ سے حاکم کی مجلس میں حاضر نہ ہو سکیں۔
If the secondary witnesses declare the primary witnesses just, it is permissible; and if they remain silent, it is also permissible.
Source pages p. 170

Commentary
This passage addresses the procedure when secondary witnesses testify. If they explicitly state that the primary witnesses are 'adil (just), the court accepts their testimony. If they remain silent on the issue, the judge must independently investigate the character of the primary witnesses. The athar from Shurayh supports that secondary testimony is only valid if the primary witnesses formally appointed them. The ruling ensures that the integrity of the chain of witnesses is maintained.

Key Terms
تعديل (ta'dil): Declaration that a witness is just and reliable.
شهود الأصل (shuhud al-asl): Primary witnesses who have direct knowledge of the case.
شهود الفرع (shuhud al-far'): Secondary witnesses who testify about the testimony of the primary witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Secondary witnesses may remain silent on the justness of primary witnesses; the judge must verify if needed.

Effect of Primary Denial on Secondary Testimony
Ruling when primary witnesses deny the testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for accepting secondary testimony and apply the ruling when primary witnesses deny the testimony.

Core Idea
Secondary testimony relies on primary witness confirmation; denial voids it.

In shahada (testimony), secondary (fara) witnesses may testify on behalf of primary (asl) witnesses only with the latter's appointment. This lesson examines the consequence when primary witnesses deny either the original testimony or the appointment. The Hanafi ruling is clear: secondary testimony is rejected, as the necessary condition is missing. The proof is an athar from Shurayh requiring formal appointment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is secondary testimony after primary witnesses deny. The ruling is that it is not accepted (la tuqbal).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites an athar from Shurayh: secondary testimony is only accepted when primary witnesses testify (appoint).
Reference: Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The athar implies that appointment (tawkiyya) is a necessary condition. Denial of appointment means the condition is absent, so secondary testimony is invalid.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may accept secondary testimony if primary witnesses are unavailable, even without explicit appointment. Hanafi requires explicit appointment.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi based on Zahir al-Riwayah and the requirement of certainty in testimony.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان انكر شهود الاصل الشهادة لم تُقبل شهادة شهود الفرع [ا اگر اصل گواہوں نے گواہی کا انکار کر دیا تو فرع گواہوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ اصل گواہوں نے کہا کہ میں نے فرع کو اپنا گواہ نہیں بنایا ہے تو چونکہ گواہ بنانا نہیں پایا گیا جو ضروری ہے اس لئے فرع گواہ کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ اثر میں گزرا۔ عن حسن بن صالح قال قلت للجعد بن ذكوان شهدت شريحا يقول اجيز شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد اذا شهد عليهما (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، ۳۸۰ في شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد ، ج راطع ، ص ۵۵۴ نمبر ۲۳۰۶۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اصل گواہ اپنی گواہی پر فرع کو گواہ بنائے تب بنے گا ورنہ نہیں۔ اور یہاں اصل نے گواہ بنانے سے انکار کر دیا اس لئے اس کی گواہی کیسے قبول کی جائے گی۔ عبارت کا دوسرا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اصل گواہ نے اس بات کا انکار کر دیا کہ وہ اس بات کا گواہ ہے۔ اس صورت میں اصل گواہی کا انکار ہو گیا اس لئے فرع گواہ بنانے کا سوال پیدا نہیں ہوتا اس لئے فرع گواہ خود بخود ساقط ہو جائے گا۔]
If the primary witnesses deny the testimony, the testimony of the secondary witnesses is not accepted.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage explains that if the primary witnesses deny either that they testified or that they appointed the secondary witnesses, the secondary testimony is rejected. The reasoning is that the appointment of secondary witnesses is a necessary condition; if the primary witnesses deny it, the basis for the secondary testimony disappears. An athar from Shurayh is cited requiring formal appointment for validity. The commentary also notes that if the primary witnesses deny the original event, the matter is even more clear.

Key Terms
انكار (inkar): Denial by the primary witness of his testimony or appointment of secondary witnesses.
شهود الاصل (shuhud al-asl): Primary witnesses who directly witness the event.
شهود الفرع (shuhud al-far): Secondary witnesses who testify based on the testimony of primary witnesses.
توكية (tawkiyya): Appointment of secondary witnesses by primary witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Secondary testimony is rejected when primary witnesses deny either the testimony or the appointment of secondary witnesses.

Punishment for False Witness: Tashhir over Ta'zir (Abu Hanifa)
Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on false witness punishment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling on the punishment of a false witness, explain the Quranic and sīra-based proofs, and distinguish it from the view allowing ta'zir.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa prescribes public exposure (tashhir) for false witnesses, not corporal punishment (ta'zir).

False testimony is a grave sin, but how should a false witness be punished? Imam Abu Hanifa uniquely argues that public exposure (tashhir) in the market is sufficient, based on the Quran's command to shun false testimony and the practice of Caliph Umar. This lesson unpacks his reasoning and the proofs he cites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is giving false testimony (shahādat al-zūr). The ruling is that the false witness must be paraded publicly (tashhīr) and not given discretionary corporal punishment (ta'zīr).
Tashhīr is a form of disgraceful punishment meant to deter and expose.
2
Locate the primary dalīl
Abu Hanifa cites the Quranic verse: 'And shun false testimony' (Sūrah al-Ḥajj, 22:30). The command 'ijtanibū' is a strong prohibition implying avoidance of false testimony in all forms.
The verse is qaṭ‘ī al-thubūt but ẓannī al-dalāla for this specific punishment.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalālah
The imperative to avoid false testimony implies that the false witness must be made known to the community so that people can indeed avoid him. Tashhīr achieves this; ta'zīr (corporal) does not publicize his identity.
Thus tashhīr directly fulfills the purpose of the command.
4
Consider the supporting athar
Umar ibn al-Khaṭṭāb (ra) ordered that a false witness have his face blackened and be paraded among tribes. This practice (athar) supports tashhīr as the sunna of the Companions.
The athar is cited from Muṣannaf ‘Abd al-Razzāq and Ibn Abī Shayba.
5
Note the ikhtilāf
Some scholars allow ta'zīr (corporal punishment) in addition to or instead of tashhīr. Abu Hanifa restricts it to tashhīr only, arguing that the verse and the Companion practice do not indicate ta'zīr.
The difference is a legitimate ikhtilāf based on textual interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال ابو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى في شاهد الزور أشهره في السوق ولا أعزّره. [امام ابو حنیفہ نے جھوٹے گواہ کے سلسلے میں فرمایا میں بازار میں اس کی تشہیر کروں گا اور اس کو سزا نہیں دوں گا۔ آیت میں ہے کہ جھوٹے گواہ سے دور رہو اس لئے اس کی شکل یہی ہو سکتی ہے کہ اس کے بارے میں قوم اور بازار میں تشہیر کی جائے تاکہ لوگ اس سے پرہیز کریں۔ آیت میں ہے۔ فاجتنبوا الرجس من الاوثان واجتنبوا قول الزور (آیت ۳۰ ،سورۃ الحج ۲۲) اس آیت میں جھوٹی گواہی سے دور رہنے کی تاکید ہے۔ (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ ان عمر بن الخطاب امر بشاهد الزور ان يسخم وجهه ويلقى في عنقه عمامته ويطاف به في القبائل ويقال ان هذا شاهد الزور فلا تقبلوا له شهادة (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب عقوبة شاهد الزور ، ج ثامن، ص ۳۲۷، نمبر ۱۵۳۹۴، مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۴۶۵ شاهد الزور ما يصنع به؟ ، ج رابع ، ص ۵۵۰ نمبر ۲۳۰۳۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ جھوٹے گواہ کی تشہیر کی گئی ہے۔ اس لئے امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک صرف تشہیر کی جائے گی۔]
And Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said regarding a false witness: I will publicize him in the market and I will not give him ta'zir.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage presents Imam Abu Hanifa's specific ruling on the punishment of a false witness (shahid al-zur). He prescribes public exposure (tashhir) in the market, not discretionary corporal punishment (ta'zir). The proof is from the Quranic verse 'shun false testimony' (Surah al-Hajj, 30), which implies deterrence through exposure. An athar from Umar ibn al-Khattab supports this: he ordered the false witness's face blackened and paraded among tribes. Thus, Abu Hanifa's view is that the punishment is purely disgraceful and not physical.

Key Terms
شاهد الزور (shahid al-zur): A person who gives false testimony intentionally.
تشہیر (tashhir): Public exposure as a punishment, parading in the market.
تعزیر (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment, usually corporal, left to the judge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the punishment for a false witness?
A) Imprisonment
B) Flogging
C) Public exposure in the market
D) Fine

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa uniquely prescribes tashhir (public exposure) as the exclusive punishment for a false witness, based on the Quranic command to shun false testimony.

Original Witnesses' Denial Invalidates Subordinate Testimony
Ruling on subordinate testimony when original witnesses deny

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on subordinate testimony when original witnesses deny, and identify the condition (tawkiy) that must be present for subordinate testimony to be accepted.

Core Idea
If original witnesses deny, subordinate testimony falls — the condition of appointment is missing.

This lesson addresses a key rule in the chapter of testimony (shahada): the validity of subordinate testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) depends on the original witnesses' acknowledgment. When they deny either the appointment of the subordinates or the underlying fact, the subordinate testimony becomes inadmissible. We will examine the reasoning and the supporting evidence from the practice of the early scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The passage states: إذا أنكر شهود الأصل الشهادة لا تقبل شهادة شهود الفرع. The ruling is clear: subordinate testimony is rejected when original witnesses deny.
2
Understand the Two Interpretations
The commentary explains two scenarios: (a) denial of appointing the subordinates (tawkiy), and (b) denial of the underlying fact itself. Both lead to invalidity.
The text uses 'شهود الاصل' and 'شهود الفرع'.
3
Examine the Dalil
The author cites the practice of Shuraih (an early judge) who required the original witness to say 'a just person made me a witness.' This demonstrates that explicit appointment is necessary.
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Apply to a Case
If original witnesses say 'I did not appoint him,' the condition is missing, so testimony rejected. If they say 'I never witnessed that event,' the basis is gone, so also rejected.
5
Note the Hanafi Distinctiveness
The Hanafi school insists on this condition, unlike some other schools that may accept subordinate testimony independently.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان انكر شهود الاصل الشهادة لم تُقبل شهادة شهود الفرع
ہیں۔ تا کہ قاضی صاحب کو اصل گواہوں کے بارے میں اطمینان ہو جائے اثریہ ہے۔ ویقول شريح للشاهد قل اشهدني ذو عدل (الف) (مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب شهادة الرجل على الرجل، ج ثامن ، ص ۱۳۳۸، نمبر ۱۵۴۴۷)
(۲۸۵۷) (۴۸) اگر اصل گواہوں نے گواہی کا انکار کر دیا تو فرع گواہوں کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔ اصل گواہوں نے کہا کہ میں نے فرع کو اپنا گواہ نہیں بنایا ہے تو چونکہ گواہ بنانا نہیں پایا گیا جو ضروری ہے اس لئے فرع گواہ کی گواہی قبول نہیں کی جائے گی۔
اثر میں گزرا۔ عن حسن بن صالح قال قلت للجعد بن ذكوان شهدت شريحا يقول اجيز شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد اذا شهد عليهما (ب) (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، ۳۸۰ في شهادة الشاهد على الشاهد ، ج راطع ، ص ۵۵۴ نمبر ۲۳۰۶۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ اصل گواہ اپنی گواہی پر فرع کو گواہ بنائے تب بنے گا ورنہ نہیں۔ اور یہاں اصل نے گواہ بنانے سے انکار کر دیا اس لئے اس کی گواہی کیسے قبول کی جائے گی۔ عبارت کا دوسرا مطلب یہ ہے کہ اصل گواہ نے اس بات کا انکار کر دیا کہ وہ اس بات کا گواہ ہے۔ اس صورت میں اصل گواہی کا انکار ہو گیا اس لئے فرع گواہ بنانے کا سوال پیدا نہیں ہوتا اس لئے فرع گواہ خود بخود ساقط ہو جائے گا۔
And if the original witnesses deny the testimony, the testimony of the subordinate witnesses is not accepted. ... So that the judge may be satisfied about the original witnesses. There is an athar: Shuraih said to the witness, 'Say: a just person made me a witness.' ... (48) If the original witnesses deny the testimony, then the testimony of the subordinate witnesses will not be accepted. The original witnesses said, 'I did not make the subordinate my witness.' Since the appointment of a witness, which is necessary, is not found, therefore the subordinate witness's testimony will not be accepted. ... In this athar, the original witness makes the subordinate a witness upon his testimony, only then it is valid, otherwise not. And here the original has denied making a witness, so how can his testimony be accepted? Another meaning is that the original witness has denied being a witness to that matter. In this case, the original testimony is denied, so the issue of making a subordinate witness does not arise, and the subordinate witness automatically falls.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Kitab al-Shahadat regarding subordinate testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada). The ruling states: if the original witnesses (shuhud al-asl) deny the testimony, then the testimony of the subordinate witnesses (shuhud al-far') is not accepted. The commentary explains two possible meanings: first, the original witnesses deny having appointed the subordinates as witnesses, so the necessary condition of tawkiy (appointment) is missing; second, the original witnesses deny the very fact they were testifying about, which invalidates the basis for subordinate testimony. The author supports this with an athar from Shuraih requiring explicit appointment. Thus, the subordinate testimony is rendered invalid in either case.

Key Terms
شهود الاصل (shuhud al-asl): The witnesses who directly witnessed the event and whose testimony is the basis for subordinate testimony.
شهود الفرع (shuhud al-far'): The witnesses who testify on behalf of the original witnesses, i.e., that the original witnesses had testified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the original witnesses deny having appointed the subordinate witnesses, what happens to the subordinate testimony?
A) It is still accepted because the subordinate witnesses are reliable.
B) It is rejected because the condition of tawkiy (appointment) is missing.
C) The judge investigates further before deciding.
D) It is accepted only if the subordinate witnesses are two men.

Key Takeaway
Subordinate testimony is invalid when original witnesses deny, because the condition of appointment (tawkiy) is missing or the basis of testimony is undermined.

Punishment for False Witness: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the punishment for false witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's positions on the punishment for false witnesses, identify their respective proofs, and evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa punishes false witnesses by public shaming; the Sahibayn add beating and imprisonment.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the punishment for a false witness (shahid al-zur). While the crime is unanimously condemned, the appropriate punishment is disputed between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The difference stems from conflicting evidence from the Quran and the practice of Caliph Umar. By the end, you will understand not only the two positions but also how the Hanafi school reconciles such differences.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify exactly what Imam Abu Hanifa prescribes for the false witness: public shaming (tashhir) in the market, no ta'zir (corporal punishment). Note the key Arabic terms: أشهر (I make him known) and لا أعزره (I do not give ta'zir).
This is the first part of the passage: 'أشهره في السوق ولا أعزّره'.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's position
Identify what Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani prescribe: beating and imprisonment. Note the term 'نوجعه ضربا' (inflict pain by beating) and 'نحبسه' (imprison him).
This is the second part: 'نوجعُه ضربا ونحبسه'.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Consider his proofs: (a) Quranic verse 22:30 – 'avoid false testimony' – from which he deduces that public shaming suffices as a deterrent. (b) The practice of Umar who blackened the face and paraded the false witness. Understand the wajh al-dalalah: the verse commands avoidance, so the punishment should serve to warn others.
The passage cites the Quran and an athar from Umar.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
Consider their proof: another narration from Umar that he beat the false witness forty lashes. This indicates that ta'zir (corporal punishment) is also prescribed.
The passage cites an athar from Makhul: 'ضرب شاهد الزور أربعون سوطا'.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response and determine the tarjih
Understand how Abu Hanifa responds: the beating narration may be interpreted as part of tashhir or is not general. Then note that later Hanafi practice often prefers the Sahibayn view, giving the judge discretion to beat and imprison.
The text does not explicitly state the mufta bihi, but later authorities lean towards the Sahibayn.

And Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, said regarding the false witness: 'I will make him known in the market and I will not give him ta'zir.' ... [Urdu explanation] ... And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: 'We will inflict pain on him by beating and imprison him.' ... There is an athar: from Makhul that Umar ibn al-Khattab beat the false witness forty lashes.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the punishment for a false witness (shahid al-zur). Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the false witness should be publicly shamed (tashhir) in the market and not given ta'zir (discretionary corporal punishment). His evidence is the Quranic command to avoid false testimony (Surah al-Hajj 22:30) and the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab who blackened the face and paraded the false witness. The two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn), hold that the false witness should be given ta'zir by beating and imprisonment. Their evidence is another narration from Umar that he beat the false witness forty lashes. The commentary explains that Abu Hanifa sees tashhir as sufficient deterrence, while the Sahibayn consider physical punishment necessary. The mufta bihi position is not explicitly stated here, but later Hanafi practice often follows the Sahibayn on ta'zir.

Key Terms
شاهد الزور (shahid al-zur): A witness who bears false testimony knowingly.
تعزیر (ta'zir): Discretionary punishment for offences not prescribed in the Quran or Sunnah.
تشہیر (tashhir): Public shaming by parading the offender and announcing his crime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Beating with forty lashes
B) Imprisonment for a fixed term
C) Public shaming in the market
D) A fine payable to the state

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on the punishment for false witness: Abu Hanifa prescribes public shaming, while the Sahibayn prescribe beating and imprisonment; later practice often adopts the Sahibayn view.

Punishment of False Witness: Sahibayn's View
Intra-Hanafi ruling with companion precedent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Sahibayn's ruling on punishing a false witness, identify the proof from Umar ibn al-Khattab, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on imprisonment.

Core Idea
The false witness must be beaten and imprisoned — the Sahibayn require both.

In this passage, we encounter the position of the two leading students of Abu Hanifa, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), on how to deal with a witness who deliberately lies. They do not stop at a simple reprimand; they prescribe a ta'zir beating and imprisonment. To support this, they bring an action of Caliph Umar, who set the precedent of forty lashes. This ruling is not merely a static rule but part of a live debate within the Hanafi school itself, as Abu Hanifa is reported to have differed on the element of imprisonment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the Arabic phrase: 'نوجعُه ضربا ونحبسه' — 'We will punish him by beating and imprison him.' This is the core ruling of the Sahibayn.
The pronoun 'نا' refers to the Sahibayn collectively.
2
Recognize the type of punishment
The beating is ta'zir, a discretionary punishment, not a fixed hadd. Ta'zir leaves room for judicial discretion, but the Sahibayn here make it seem obligatory (wajib) by their wording.
Ta'zir can include lashes, imprisonment, or both.
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The text cites an athar from Makhul that 'Umar ibn al-Khattab struck a false witness forty lashes.' This companion precedent provides the basis for the ruling.
The athar is found in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
While Abu Hanifa's view is not quoted here, it is known that he agreed on ta'zir but may have opposed imprisonment. The Sahibayn's insistence on both beating and imprisonment is their distinctive position.
This shows that even within a single madhhab, ikhtilaf exists on subsidiary matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The footnote emphasizes Umar's practice of forty lashes.

Key Terms
شاهد الزور (shahid al-zur): A witness who intentionally gives false testimony.
تعزیر (ta'zir): Discretionary corporal punishment for offenses not covered by fixed hadd penalties.

Retraction of Testimony: Before and After Judgment
Two rulings on retraction of testimony and consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on retraction of testimony before and after judgment and explain the consequence of daman for harmful retraction.

Core Idea
Retraction after judgment does not undo the verdict; witnesses must compensate for harm.

In Islamic legal procedure, witnesses may sometimes retract their testimony. The effect of such retraction depends crucially on timing: if it occurs before the judge passes judgment, the testimony is void and no liability attaches. But if it occurs after judgment, the verdict remains binding, yet the witnesses must pay compensation (daman) for any harm caused. This distinction reflects the Hanafi principle that a final judgment is not easily overturned, but wrongdoers must answer for their actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Scenarios
Note the two time points: retraction before judgment and retraction after judgment. Each has a different ruling.
The first scenario is mentioned in paragraph [2860], the second in [2861].
2
State the Consequence for Each
Before judgment: testimony becomes void (sâqit) and no daman. After judgment: judgment remains (lā yufsakh) and daman is wajib.
Daman is financial compensation for harm caused by false testimony.
3
Identify the Underlying Principle
The principle is that whoever causes harm is liable for it. Since retraction before judgment prevents harm, no liability. After judgment, harm has occurred, so liability attaches.
The author mentions this principle in the note: 'whoever causes harm is liable for that harm.'
4
Analyze the Dalil for Retraction Before Judgment
The hadith of Mā‘iz ibn Mālik shows that retracting a confession of zinā prevents the hadd punishment. This is analogous to retracting testimony before judgment.
The hadith is from Abu Dawud (no. 4419, 4434).
5
Understand the Rationale for the Ruling After Judgment
The judgment is based on the apparent truth at the time. Retraction after does not retroactively invalidate the court's decision. Instead, the witnesses must compensate the injured party.
This protects the finality of judgments while ensuring justice for the harmed party.

وماعز بن مالك لو رجعا بعد اعترافهما او قال لو لم يرجعا بعد اعترافهما لم يطلبهما وانما رجمها عند الرابعة - دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ حدثنی يزيد بن نعيم بن هزال عن ابيه قال كان ماعز بن مالك يتيما ... ثم اتى تو حد نہ لگتی۔ اس سے گواہوں کا رجوع کرنا ثابت ہوا۔ نوٹ اس باب کے اکثر مسائل اس اصول پر ہیں کہ جس نے جس کا جتنا نقصان کیا وہ اتنے کا ذمہ دار ہو گیا۔ آیت اور اثر سے اس کی دلیلیں آگے آرہی ہیں۔ [۲۸۶۰] (۱) اگر گواہ اپنی گواہی سے فیصلے سے پہلے رجوع کر جائیں تو اس کی شہادت ساقط ہو جائے گی اور ان پر ضمان لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ او پر حدیث گزری۔ ماعز بن مالک لو رجعا بعد اعترافهما ... لم يطلبهما (ابوداؤد شریف، نمبر ۴۴۳۴ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حد کا اقرار کرنے والا فیصلے کے بعد بھی رجوع کر جائے تو ان کی گواہی پر کوئی فیصلہ نہیں ہو سکے گا۔ کیونکہ دونوں شہادتیں آپس میں متعارض ہو گئیں۔ اور چونکہ گواہی سے ابھی کوئی نقصان نہیں ہوا ہے اس لئے اس پر کچھ ضمان بھی لازم نہیں آئے گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ سألت الزھری عن رجل شهد عند الامام فاثبت الامام شهادته ثم دعى لها فبدلها اتجوز شهادته الاولى او الآخرة؟ قال لا شهادة له في الأولى ولا في الآخرة. قال الشيخ وهذا في الرجوع قبل امضاء الحكم بالاولى (ب) (سن للبیہقی ، باب الرجوع عن الشهادة ، ج عاشر ص ۲۲۵، نمبر ۲۱۱۹۵) اس اثر میں ہے کہ فیصلے سے پہلے رجوع کر جائے تو پہلی یا دوسری کسی گواہی کا اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ [۲۸۶۱) (۲) پس اگر ان کی گواہی سے فیصلہ کر دیا پھر وہ رجوع کئے تو فیصلہ فسخ نہیں ہو گا ۔ اور ان کی شہادت سے جو نقصان ہوا اس کا ضمان لازم حاشیہ : (الف) عبداللہ بن بریدہ اپنے باپ سے نقل کرتے ہیں کہ فرمایا ہم حضور کے اصحاب حضرت غامد یہ اور حضرت ماعڑ کے بارے میں باتیں کرتے تھے کہ اگر وہ زنا کے اعتراف سے رجوع کر جاتے یا یوں فرمایا اعتراف کے بعد دوبارہ واپس نہ آتے تو دونوں کو نہ بلاتے کیونکہ چوتھی مرتبہ رحم فرمایا۔ دوسری روایت میں ہے پھر لوگ حضور کے پاس آئے اور حضرت ماعر کا تذکرہ کیا تو آپ نے فرمایا ان کو چھوڑ کیوں نہ دیا؟ شاید وہ تو بہ کرتا تو اللہ تعالی تو بہ قبول فرما لیتے ۔ (ب) میں نے حضرت زہری سے پوچھا کوئی آدمی امام کے پاس گواہی دے اور امام اس کی گواہی لکھ لے۔ پھر دوبارہ بلایا جائے تو گواہی بدل دے تو اس کی پہلی گواہی صحیح مانی جائے گی یا بعد والی ؟ فرمایا نہ اس کی پہلی گواہی مانی جائے گی نہ بعد کی۔ حضرت شیخ نے فرمایا یہ بات پہلی گواہی پر فیصلے سے پہلے کی بات ہے کہ گواہی کا اعتبار نہیں۔
The Book of Retraction of Testimony) The Book of Retraction of Testimony) 12860) When the witnesses retract their testimony before judgment is passed, their testimony is void and no liability is upon them. [2861] (2) If judgment is passed on their testimony then they retract, the judgment is not annulled, and upon them is... The Book of Retraction of Testimony. Important note: Withdrawing after giving testimony is called retraction of testimony. Its proof is in this hadith: 'Abdullah ibn Buraidah narrated from his father: We, the companions of the Messenger of Allah, were saying that al-Ghamidiyyah and Ma'iz ibn Malik, if they had retracted after their confession, or he said if they did not retract after their confession, he would not have sought them, and he only stoned her at the fourth time. Another narration: Yazid ibn Nu'aym ibn Hazzal narrated from his father: Ma'iz ibn Malik was an orphan... then he came to the Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) and mentioned that to him, so he said: Why did you not leave him, perhaps he would repent and Allah would accept his repentance. (a) (Abu Dawood, chapter on stoning Ma'iz, no. 4419, 4434) In this hadith, if Ma'iz had retracted after confessing to zina, the hadd would not be applied. This proves retraction by witnesses. Note: Most issues in this chapter are based on the principle that whoever causes harm is liable for that harm. The proofs from Quran and athar will come later. [2860] (1) If the witnesses retract from their testimony before the judgment, their testimony is void and no liability is upon them. The hadith mentioned above: Ma'iz ibn Malik, if they had retracted after their confession... he would not have sought them (Abu Dawood, no. 4434). This hadith indicates that if someone confesses to a hadd and retracts even after judgment, no judgment can be based on their confession because the two statements conflict. And since no harm has yet occurred from the testimony, no liability is required. (2) In an athar: I asked al-Zuhri about a man who testified before the imam, and the imam recorded his testimony, then he was called again and changed his testimony: Is his first testimony valid or the last? He said: Neither his first nor his last testimony is accepted. Al-Shaykh said: This is about retraction before the execution of the first judgment. (b) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on retraction of testimony, vol. 10, p. 225, no. 21195) This athar indicates that if one retracts before judgment, neither the first nor the second testimony is considered. [2861] (2) So if judgment was passed on their testimony and then they retracted, the judgment is not annulled, and for the harm caused by their testimony, liability is required. Footnote: (a) 'Abdullah ibn Buraidah narrated from his father... (b) I asked al-Zuhri...
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on retraction of testimony (Kitab al-Ruju' an al-Shahada). It begins with two key rulings: First, if witnesses retract their testimony before the judge passes judgment, their testimony becomes void and they incur no financial liability because no harm has yet resulted. Second, if they retract after the judgment has been passed, the judgment remains valid (it is not annulled), but the witnesses are liable for any harm caused by their false testimony. The author supports these rulings with several proofs: a hadith about Ma'iz ibn Malik (if he had retracted his confession, the hadd punishment would not be applied—analogously, retraction of testimony before judgment nullifies the evidence), and an athar from al-Zuhri confirming that retraction before judgment invalidates both the original and subsequent testimony. A footnote provides the full text of the hadith. The author notes that many issues in this chapter are based on the general principle that one who causes harm must compensate for it.

Key Terms
الرجوع عن الشهادة (al-ruju' 'an al-shahada): The act of a witness retracting or withdrawing their testimony after having given it.
ضمان (daman): Financial liability/compensation for harm caused.
ساقط (sāqit): Void, fallen; used to describe testimony that is no longer valid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if witnesses retract their testimony after the judge has passed judgment?
A) The judgment is annulled and the witnesses are not liable.
B) The judgment is annulled and the witnesses must compensate.
C) The judgment remains valid and the witnesses must compensate for harm.
D) The judgment remains valid and the witnesses are not liable.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, retraction of testimony before judgment makes the testimony void and no compensation is due; retraction after judgment leaves the verdict intact but imposes a duty to compensate for harm.

Shahadat — Testimony

6 min
Liability of Two Witnesses Who Retract Property Testimony
Ruling with proof from Quran and effect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witnesses who retract property testimony after judgment, and explain the evidence from Quran and early precedents.

Core Idea
Witnesses who retract after judgment must jointly compensate the full loss they caused.

Witness testimony is a cornerstone of Islamic legal proof. But what happens when witnesses later confess they lied? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling: the judgment stands, but the witnesses become liable for the property they wrongfully took from the defendant. The ruling is supported by the Quranic principle of proportionality and early caliphal precedent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is the retraction (ruju') of two witnesses after the judge has passed judgment in a property case. The ruling is that both witnesses guarantee (damana) the full property for the defendant.
The ruling applies only after judgment; retraction before judgment would nullify the testimony without liability.
2
Note the condition: retraction after judgment
The ruling is conditional on retraction occurring after the judge has executed the judgment. The witnesses must come before the judge and retract; this is shown in the effect of Ali (ra).
3
Identify the amount and nature of liability
The witnesses are jointly and severally liable for the entire property. Each is responsible for the full amount, not just half. The defendant can recover from either witness.
This is joint liability, not proportional.
4
Locate the dalil
The author cites the Quranic verse (5:45) establishing proportionality in retaliation, and effects (athar) from Ali and Ibn Shubruma showing that retraction is accepted and compensation is imposed.
The Quranic verse is used as a general principle (qiyas) rather than direct ruling.
5
Understand the wisdom (istihsan)
The ruling is based on istihsan: compensating the harm caused. Without this, false witnesses would escape accountability after causing loss.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۶۳] (۴) واذا شهد شاهدان بمال فحكم الحاكم به ثم رجعا ضمنا المال للمشهود علیه
میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن الشعبی ان رجلين شهدا عند على على رجل بالسرقة فقطع على يده ثم جاء ا بآخر فقالا هذا هو السارق لا الاول (الف) (سنن البيهقي، باب رجوع عن الشهادة ، ج عاشر ص ۴۲۴، نمبر۲۱۱۹۲) اس اثر میں پہلے گواہ حضرت علی کے پاس آئے اور دوسرے گواہ بھی رجوع کرنے کے لئے حضرت علی کے پاس آئے۔ اور حضرت علی قاضی تھے جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ رجوع کے لئے بھی قاضی کے پاس آئے تب رجوع مقبول ہے۔
وجه
اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن شبرمة في رجلين شهدا على رجل بحق فاخذا منه ثم قالا انما شهدنا عليه بزور يغرمانه في اموالهما (ب) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الشاهد يرجع عن شهادته او يشهد ثم سجد ، ج ثامن، ص ۳۵۴ نمبر ۱۵۵۱۶ ورواه البيهقي ، باب الرجوع عن الشهادة ، ج عاشر ، ص۴۲۴، نمبر ۲۱۱۹۴) اس اثر میں ہے کہ گواہوں نے مشہود علیہ کا جو نقصان کیا ہے وہ ادا کرنا ہوگا (۲) اس آیت میں بھی اس قاعدے کا ثبوت ہے کہ جس کا جتنا نقصان کیا ہے اس پر اتنا ہی ضمان لازم ہوگا ۔ و كتبنا عليهم فيها ان النفس بالنفس والعين بالعين والانف بالانف والاذن بالاذن والسن بالسن والجروح قصاص (ج) ( آیت ۴۵ ،سورۃ المائدۃ ۵ )
-
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت شعمی نے فرمایا ایک آدمی نے حضرت علی کے سامنے کسی آدمی پر چوری کی گواہی دی۔ پس حضرت علی نے اس کا ہاتھ کاٹ دیا پھر دوبارہ آیا اور کہا کہ یہ چور ہے پہلا نہیں ہے ( ب ) حضرت ابن شبرمہ فرماتے ہیں کہ دو آدمی کسی کے خلاف گواہی دے کسی کے حق کی اور اس سے لیا گیا پھر کہا میں نے اس پر جھوٹی گواہی دی تو دونوں کو ان کے مال میں تاوان لازم کیا جائے گا (ج) ہم نے یہودیوں پر فرض کیا جان جان کے بدلے میں اور آنکھ آنکھ کے بدلے میں اور ناک ناک کے بدلے میں اور کان کان کے بدلے میں اور دانت دانت کے بدلے میں کاٹا جائے گا اور زخموں کا بھی بدلہ ہے
[2863] (4) And if two witnesses testify for property, and the judge passes judgment based on it, then they both retract, they both guarantee the property for the one against whom it was testified. In this there is an indication. From al-Sha'bi that two men testified before 'Ali against a man for theft, so 'Ali cut off his hand, then they came with another and said: 'This is the thief, not the first.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on retraction from testimony, vol. 10, p. 424, no. 21192). In this effect, the first witnesses came to 'Ali and the second witnesses also came to 'Ali to retract. And 'Ali was a judge, so it is known that for retraction also, they come to the judge and then retraction is accepted. Evidence: There is an effect from Ibn Shubruma regarding two men who testified against a man for a right, and they took from him, then they said: 'We only testified falsely against him,' they will be made to pay it from their wealth. (Musannaf 'Abd al-Razzaq, chapter on the witness who retracts his testimony or testifies then prostrates, vol. 8, p. 354, no. 15516, and al-Bayhaqi narrated it, chapter on retraction from testimony, vol. 10, p. 424, no. 21194). In this effect, the witnesses must compensate for the loss they caused to the one against whom they testified. (2) In this verse also there is proof for this principle: whoever causes a loss, he is liable for that much. 'And We prescribed for them therein: the life for the life, the eye for the eye, the nose for the nose, the ear for the ear, the tooth for the tooth, and for wounds is legal retribution.' (Surah al-Ma'idah 5:45). Footnote: (a) Hadrat al-Sha'bi said: A man testified before 'Ali against a man for theft, so 'Ali cut off his hand, then he came again and said: 'This is the thief, not the first.' (b) Hadrat Ibn Shubruma said: Two men testify against someone for a right, and it is taken from him, then he says: 'I testified falsely against him,' then both are made liable for compensation from their wealth. (c) We prescribed for the Jews: life for life, eye for eye, nose for nose, ear for ear, tooth for tooth, and wounds have retribution.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding witnesses who retract their testimony after a judge has passed judgment in a property case. The ruling is that if both witnesses retract, they are jointly liable for the entire property amount, as their testimony caused the loss to the defendant. The author supports this with two effects (athar) and a Quranic verse. The first effect from al-Sha'bi illustrates that retraction must be made before the judge to be accepted. The second effect from Ibn Shubruma directly states that witnesses who testify falsely must pay the amount from their own wealth. The Quranic verse (5:45) on retribution is cited to establish the general principle that liability corresponds to the loss caused. This is a case of istihsan based on the principle of compensating harm.

Key Terms
شهادة (shahada): Testimony given in court by witnesses.
رجوع عن الشهادة (ruju' 'an al-shahada): Retraction of testimony after it has been given and possibly acted upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two witnesses testify for property and the judge passes judgment, then both retract, what is the liability?
A) No liability
B) Each guarantees half
C) Both jointly guarantee the full property
D) Only one guarantees the full property

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that witnesses who retract after judgment must jointly compensate the full loss they caused, based on the Quranic principle of proportionality and early precedents.

Liability of a Single Retracting Witness
Ruling with proof from effect of Ibrahim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a single retracting witness guarantees half of the property or blood-money and explain the proof from the effect of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i.

Core Idea
One retracting witness guarantees half – liability follows the number of witnesses causing the loss.

When witnesses retract after a judgment, their liability is proportional to their contribution to the loss. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling for a single retracting witness, supported by an effect from the tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i. The lesson clarifies why the liability is half, not full, and how this rule applies to both property and blood-money cases by analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the retraction of one witness after a judgment based on two witnesses. The ruling is that the retracting witness guarantees half of the lost property or blood-money.
The ruling is from the Hanafi school; the other witness's testimony still stands.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is an effect (athar) from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, transmitted by Imam Muhammad in al-Asl. It explicitly states the same rule for a hand-cutting case.
The effect is a Sunnah of a tabi'i, considered a valid proof in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The effect directly gives the ruling: if both witnesses retract, they pay full blood-money; if one retracts, he pays half. By qiyas, property cases follow the same proportional division.
The explicit text (mantiq) indicates the half-share; the analogy is straightforward because the cause (loss from testimony) is identical.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The ruling is mukhtalaf fih – some schools may disagree. For example, some may hold that retraction after judgment is not accepted, or that the retracting witness is liable for the full amount.
The Hanafi position is based on the clear text of the effect and the principle of proportional liability.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The author states 'wa bihi na'khudh' – we take this as our position. Thus, the mufta bihi is that one retracting witness guarantees half.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is relied upon in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۶۴](۵) وان رجع احدهما ضمن النصف.
اگر دونوں گواہوں میں سے ایک نے رجوع کیا تو آدھے کا ضامن ہوگا۔ (1) دو گواہوں کی گواہی سے نقصان ہوا ہے اس لئے اس پر آدھے کا ضمان ہو گا (۲) اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابراهيم قال اذا شهد شاهدان على قطع يد فقضى القاضى بذلك ثم رجعا عن الشهادة فعليهما الدية وان رجع احدهما فعليه نصف الدية وبه ناخذ (د) (ذکر محمد فی الاصل کمافی المبسوط، اعلاء السنن ، باب الرجوع عن الشهادة ، ج عاشر ص ۲۹۷، نمبر ۵۰۴۳) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایک گواہ نے رجوع کیا تو آدھے نقصان کا ذمہ دار ہوگا۔
حاشیہ : (1) حضرت ابراہیم نے فرمایا اگر دو آدمی کسی کے ہاتھ کاٹنے کی گواہی دے اور قاضی اس کا فیصلہ کر دے پھر گواہی سے رجوع کر جائے تو ان دونوں گواہوں پر دیت لازم ہوگی اور اگر ایک رجوع کرے تو آدھی دیت لازم ہوگی (باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
[2864] (5) And if one of them retracts, he guarantees half. If one of the two witnesses retracts, he will be guarantor of half. (1) Because the loss was caused by two witnesses, so he is liable for half. (2) There is an effect from Ibrahim: He said: 'If two witnesses testify for cutting off a hand, and the judge passes judgment based on that, then they retract from the testimony, then both are liable for the blood-money, and if one of them retracts, he is liable for half the blood-money, and we take this (as our position).' (Muhammad mentioned it in al-Asl, as in al-Mabsut, I'la' al-Sunan, chapter on retraction from testimony, vol. 10, p. 297, no. 5043). From this effect it is known that when one witness retracts, he is responsible for half the loss. Footnote: (1) Hadrat Ibrahim said: If two men testify for cutting off a hand, and the judge passes judgment, then they retract, then both are liable for the blood-money, and if one retracts, half the blood-money is due.
Source pages p. 175

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling for a case where only one of the two witnesses retracts after judgment. The ruling is that the retracting witness guarantees half of the property (or blood-money in analogical cases). The author explains that since the loss was caused by the testimony of two witnesses, the retraction of one makes him liable for half. The proof is an effect from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, who explicitly states the same rule for a hand-cutting case: both witnesses together pay full blood-money, one pays half. This is adopted as the school's position (wa bihi na'khudh). The footnote mentions the same effect but is cut off.

Key Terms
نصف (nisf): Half of the property or blood-money, as the share of one witness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If one of two witnesses retracts after judgment in a property case, what does he guarantee according to the Hanafi school?
A) The full property
B) Nothing
C) Half the property
D) Quarter of the property

Key Takeaway
One retracting witness guarantees half the property or blood-money because liability is proportional to the number of witnesses who caused the loss.

Shahadat — Testimony
intermediate
8 min
Liability When One of Three Witnesses Retracts Property Testimony
Ruling with proof from effect on weight of number in testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the liability of retracting witnesses when three testify for property, and apply the Hanafi principle that judgment is based on only two witnesses.

Core Idea
One extra witness beyond the required two does not add weight; only the two effective witnesses matter for liability upon retraction.

In Hanafi law, property testimony is conclusive with two male witnesses (or one man and two women). When a third witness joins, that extra witness does not strengthen the proof. This lesson examines how liability for retraction is apportioned when three witnesses testify, then one or two retract. The ruling hinges on the principle that preference is not given by multiplicity of witnesses (tarjih bi-kathrat al-adad).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Three witnesses testify for property. One retracts, then another retracts. Determine the liability of each retracting witness.
2
Apply the principle of effective testimony
Judgment in property cases is based on two witnesses. The third witness is superfluous and does not affect the ruling.
The principle is derived from the effect (athar) of Shuraih and Ali, who state that multiplicity of number does not give preference.
3
Determine liability for first retractor
Since the judgment was based on the other two witnesses, the first retractor bears no liability. The remaining two are sufficient.
4
Determine liability for second retractor
When a second witness retracts, only one witness remains, which is insufficient for proof. The retraction of two witnesses undermines the judgment, so both retractors jointly guarantee half the property.
Each pays half of the half, i.e., one-quarter each, if the property was 20 dirhams, each pays 5.
5
Generalise the rule
Any number of witnesses beyond the required two do not increase the evidentiary weight. Liability for retraction is limited to those whose testimony forms the basis of the judgment.
This is specific to property cases; different rules apply to hudud and other matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۲۸۶۵](۶) وان شهد بالمال ثلثة فرجع احدهم فلا ضمان عليه فان رجع آخر ضمن الراجعان نصف المال
معلوم ہوا کہ ایک گواہ نے رجوع کیا تو آدھے نقصان کا ذمہ دار ہوگا۔ [۲۸۶۵] (۶) اگر مال کی گواہی تین گواہوں نے دی۔ پس ان میں سے ایک نے رجوع کیا تو اس پر ضمان نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر دوسرے نے بھی رجوع کر لیا تو دونوں رجوع کرنے والے آدھے مال کے ضامن ہوں گے۔
دو گواہوں سے مال کا فیصلہ ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن یہاں تین آدمیوں نے گواہی دی ہے اس لئے ایک زیادہ ہے۔ دو سے زیادہ گواہ گواہی دے سکتا ہے لیکن اس کا زیادہ اعتبار نہیں ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ کتب عبد الرحمن بن اذينة الى شريح في ناس من الازدادعوا قبل ناس من بنى اسد قال واذا غدا هؤلاء ببينة راح اولئك باكثر منهم قال فكتب اليه ليست من التهاتر والتكاثر في شيء، الدابة لمن هي في ايديهم اذا اقاموا البينة - اور دوسری روایت میں ہے۔ عن حنش عن على انه لا يرجح بكثرة العدد (الف) ( سنن البيهقي، باب من قال لا يرجح في الشهادات بكثرة العدد، ج عاشر ص ۴۳۴، نمبر ۲۱۲۲۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ دو سے زیادہ گواہوں پر فیصلے کا مدار نہیں ہے۔ اس قاعدے کے بعد مسئلے کی صورت یہ ہے کہ تین آدمیوں نے مال کی گواہی دی پھر ایک آدمی اپنی گواہی سے رجوع کر گیا تو اس پر ضمان لازم نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس پر فیصلے کا مدار نہیں تھا۔ بعد میں دوسرا گواہ بھی رجوع کر گیا تو گویا کہ آدھی گواہی رجوع کر گئی اس لئے ان دونوں پر آدھا ضمان لازم ہوگا۔ مثلا ہیں درہم کا فیصلہ ہوا تھا تو رجوع کرنے والے دونوں گواہوں پر دس درہم ضمان لازم ہوگا اور ہر ایک کے حصے میں پانچ پانچ در ہم آئیں گے۔
اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ دو سے زیادہ گواہوں پر فیصلے کا مدار نہیں ہے۔
[2865] (6) And if three testify for property, and one of them retracts, there is no liability on him; then if another retracts, the two retracting ones guarantee half the property. It is known that one witness retracting is responsible for half the loss. [2865] (6) If three witnesses testify for property, and one of them retracts, there is no liability on him. Then if the other also retracts, both retracting witnesses are guarantors for half the property. Property judgment is based on two witnesses. But here three men testified, so one is extra. More than two witnesses can testify, but their testimony is not given more weight. There is an effect: 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Udhayna wrote to Shuraih regarding some people from Azd who claimed against some people from Banu Asad. He said: 'If these come with a bayyinah (evidence) in the morning, and those come with more witnesses in the evening, then what?' So he (Shuraih) wrote back: 'This is not a matter of mutual nullification or multiplication. The animal belongs to those in whose possession it is, if they establish bayyinah.' And in another narration, from Hanash from 'Ali that he does not give preference by multiplicity of number. (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on whoever said preference is not given in testimonies by multiplicity of number, vol. 10, p. 434, no. 21227). From this effect it is known that judgment is not based on more than two witnesses. Based on this rule, the issue is: three men testified for property; then one man retracted, so no liability is necessary on him because judgment was not based on him. Later, the second witness also retracted, so effectively half the testimony retracted, so both are liable for half the property. For example, if the judgment was for twenty dirhams, then both retracting witnesses are liable for ten dirhams, each paying five. The principle is that judgment is not based on more than two witnesses.
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage deals with the case of three witnesses testifying for property. Since the effective testimony for judgment is based on two witnesses, the third is redundant. Therefore, if only one of the three retracts, there is no liability on that retracting witness because the judgment was based on the other two. However, if another retracts (i.e., total of two retract), then since the remaining testimony is only one witness, which is insufficient, the loss is attributed to the two retracting witnesses, and they jointly guarantee half the property. The author provides a proof from an effect in which Shuraih and 'Ali confirm that multiplicity of witnesses does not give added weight; the basis for judgment remains two witnesses. The example given: if the property was 20 dirhams, the two retracting witnesses pay 10 dirhams total, each paying 5.

Key Terms
ترجيح بكثرة العدد (tarjih bi-kathrat al-'adad): Giving preference to testimony based on a larger number of witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If three witnesses testify for property, and one retracts, what is the liability?
A) He guarantees one-third of the property
B) He guarantees half of the property
C) No liability
D) He guarantees the full property

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, only the two essential witnesses matter for testimony in property cases; an extra witness bears no liability for retraction.
